Faith and Disbelief
intermediate
8 min
Exception in the Root of Faith: Abu Hanifa's View
Maydani presents Abu Hanifa's ruling on exception in faith.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Abu Hanifa considers exception in the root of faith as invalid and the crucial distinction between doubt in the foundation of faith and hope for its future stability.

Core Idea
Exception in the root of faith is like a contract-breaker — it voids faith itself.

This passage from Maydani's commentary on the Tahawiyyah presents the Hanafi position on the phrase 'in sha' Allah' when declaring faith. Abu Hanifa argues that such an exception introduces doubt into the very foundation of belief, which is unacceptable. However, he distinguishes between doubting the root of faith and expressing hope for its continuance or acceptance.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Begin by reading the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the literal translation. Let the author's argument unfold naturally.
Notice the footnote marker (۳) — it's from the original text.
2
Understand key terms
Focus on 'asl al-iman' (root of faith), 'istithna'' (exception), and 'shakk' (doubt). These are central to the ruling.
3
Analyze the contract analogy
Abu Hanifa compares the declaration of faith to a contract. Just as an exception invalidates contracts like divorce or sale, it invalidates the 'contract' of faith. Grasp this analogy.
Why does he use contract examples? Faith is a covenant with Allah.
4
Note the distinction in exceptions
The passage gives examples of permissible exceptions that relate to permanence, stability, and acceptance. Contrast these with the impermissible exception in the root itself.
5
Apply the ruling
Consider the case of a disbeliever saying 'I am a believer if Allah wills' — why does he not become a believer? Apply the principle to similar statements.
This reinforces the core idea.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي بحر الكلام والاستثناء في أصل الأيمان غير صحيح عند أبي حنيفة وأصحابه ؛ لأن الاستثناء يرفع جميع العقود نحو الطلاق والعتاق والبيع فكذلك يرفع عقد الإيمان، والاستثناء قوله أنا مؤمن إن شاء الله؛ لأن هذا الاستثناء شك، والشك في أصل الإيمان كفر وضلالة؛ ولذا لو قال الكافر أنا مؤمن إن شاء الله لا يصير مؤمنًا، وكذا لو وقف وقال : آمنت بالله ورسوله إلى ألف سنة لا يصير مؤمنًا، ولو قال: أكون مؤمناً غدًا إن شاء الله أو أموت مؤمنًا إن شاء الله أو يكون إيماني مقبولاً إن شاء الله يكون مستحسنا؛ لأن هذا الاستثناء في الدوام والثبات والقبول لا في أصل الإيمان (۳).
And in Bahr al-Kalam: The exception (istithna') in the root of faith (asl al-iman) is not valid according to Abu Hanifa and his companions; because exception invalidates all contracts such as divorce, manumission, and sale, so likewise it invalidates the contract of faith. And the exception is one's saying: 'I am a believer if Allah wills (ana mu'min in sha' Allah),' because this exception is doubt (shakk), and doubt in the root of faith is disbelief (kufr) and misguidance (dalala). Therefore, if a disbeliever says, 'I am a believer if Allah wills,' he does not become a believer. Similarly, if he pauses and says, 'I believe in Allah and His Messenger up to a thousand years,' he does not become a believer. And if he says, 'I will be a believer tomorrow if Allah wills,' or 'I will die a believer if Allah wills,' or 'My faith be accepted if Allah wills,' that is commendable (mustahsan); because this exception is in permanence (dawam), stability (thabat), and acceptance (qabul), not in the root of faith.
Source pages p. 100

Commentary
This passage quotes from the work 'Bahr al-Kalam' to present the position of Abu Hanifa and his school on the issue of making an exception (istithna') when declaring faith. According to them, saying 'I am a believer if Allah wills' in the context of the root of faith (asl al-iman) is invalid because it introduces doubt (shakk) into the very act of believing, and doubt in one's foundational belief is tantamount to disbelief. The analogy is drawn from contracts: just as an exception invalidates a contract of divorce, manumission, or sale, so it invalidates the 'contract' of faith. They then distinguish between different types of istithna': one that doubts the root of faith itself (which is impermissible) and one that pertains to the continuation, stability, or acceptance of faith (which is permissible and even commendable). For example, saying 'I will be a believer tomorrow' or 'I will die a believer' are acceptable because they do not doubt the present reality of faith but express hope for the future.

Key Terms
أصل الأيمان
الاستثناء
الشك
الكفر
الضلالة
الدوام
الثبات
القبول

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: All statements containing 'in sha' Allah' regarding faith are permissible and show humility.
Correction: Abu Hanifa distinguishes between doubting the root of faith (impermissible) and hoping for its future stability or acceptance (permissible).

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, what is the ruling on a disbeliever saying 'I am a believer if Allah wills'?
A) He becomes a believer
B) He does not become a believer
C) It is commendable
D) It is permissible but disliked

Key Takeaway
Abu Hanifa holds that any exception that casts doubt on the foundational act of faith (asl al-iman) is invalid and amounts to disbelief, while exceptions regarding its continuance or acceptance are acceptable.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever, even for a moment, felt hesitation in declaring 'I am a believer' without adding 'if Allah wills'? What does that hesitation reveal about the certainty in your heart, and what will you do today to remove it?
?
Your faith is not a negotiation—it is a contract. Is there any area of your life where you treat your commitment to Allah as conditional? What specific step will you take to renew that contract with absolute certainty?
?
Abu Hanifa warns that doubt in the root of faith is kufr. Now search your soul: do you truly believe without any reservation, or is there a hidden 'if' lurking in your heart? Confess it to Allah and ask for strength to replace doubt with unwavering conviction.

Faith and Disbelief

The Ruling on Saying 'I Am a Believer if Allah Wills'
Sa'd explains the intentions behind the exception statement and their rulings.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the different intentions behind saying 'I am a believer if Allah wills' and the ruling for each case according to Sa'd al-Din al-Taftazani.

Core Idea
The ruling depends on intention: doubt is kufr, but other motives are permissible yet better avoided.

This lesson explores a nuanced issue: whether a believer can say 'I am a believer if Allah wills.' Imam al-Nasafi stated it is not appropriate, but Sa'd al-Din al-Taftazani explains that this ruling varies based on intention. We'll examine the different motives and the reasoning behind the permissibility for some intentions.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic passage from Sa'd's commentary, focusing on the different intentions listed.
Notice the distinctions: doubt, politeness, uncertainty about the end, blessing, avoiding self-praise.
2
Identify the ruling for each intention
Identify which intentions make the statement kufr, permissible but disliked, or acceptable. Sa'd explains why al-Nasafi said 'does not befit' rather than 'forbidden'.
3
Compare with other statements
Sa'd contrasts this with saying 'I am young if Allah wills' and compares it to 'I am an ascetic if Allah wills'. Understand why the comparison matters.
This helps clarify the reasoning behind the ruling.
4
Reflect on the muhaqqiqun's view
Some scholars hold that tasdiq varies in strength and the perfect tasdiq is subject to Allah's will. Consider how this supports the permissibility of the statement.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقال السعد في شرح العقائد عند قول النسفي: «وإذا وجد من العبد التصديق والإقرار صح له أن يقول: أنا مؤمن حقا - لتحقق الإيمان- ولا ينبغي أن يقول: أنا مؤمن إن شاء الله»: لأنه إن كان للشك فهو كفر لا محالة، وإن كان للتأدب وإحالة الأمور إلى مشيئة الله تعالى أو للشك في العاقبة والمآل لا في الآن والحال أو للتبرك بذكر الله تعالى أو للتبرؤ عن تزكية نفسه والإعجاب بحاله فالأولى تركه لما أنه يوهم الشك؛ ولهذا قال: "ولا ينبغي " دون أن يقول: "ولا يجوز "؛ لأنه إذا لم يكن للشك فلا معنى لنفي الجواز، كيف وقد ذهب إليه كثير من السلف حتى الصحابة والتابعين أجمعين، وليس هذا مثل قولك : أنا شاب إن شاء الله؛ لأن الشباب ليس من الأفعال المكتسبة ولا مما يتصور البقاء عليه في العاقبة والمآل ولا مما تحصل به تزكية النفس والإعجاب؛ بل مثل قولك: أنا زاهد متق إن شاء الله . وذهب بعض المحققين إلى أن الحاصل للعبد هو حقيقة التصديق الذي به يخرج عن الكفر، لكن التصديق بنفسه قابل للشدة والضعف، وحصول التصديق الكامل المنجي المشار إليه بقوله تعالى: (أَوَلَتِبِكَ هُمُ الْمُؤْمِنُونَ حَقًّا هُمْ دَرَجَتُ ... الآية [سورة الأنفال آية : ٤] إنما هو في مشيئة الله تعالى(۱). قلت: فعلى هذا تكون مسألة الاستثناء في الإيمان مبنية على مسألة زيادة الإيمان ونقصانه كما أن مسألة السعادة والشقاوة مبنية على مسألة الاستثناء في الإيمان كما ذكرنا؛ فمن قال: إن الإيمان يزيد وينقص قال بجواز الاستثناء فيه وبعدم التبديل والتغيير في السعادة والشقاوة، ومن قال إن الإيمان لا يزيد ولا ينقص قال بعدم جواز الاستثناء وقال بالتبديل والتغيير في السعادة والشقاوة وسيأتي في كلام المصنف مسألة الزيادة والنقصان في الإيمان. والحاصل أن الخلاف لفظي كما ذكرنا وأن الإيمان والكفر حالتان يوصف بهما العباد؛ فمن وصف بالإيمان فهو مؤمن ومن وصف بالكفر فهو كافر، كما أن الكبر والصَّغَر حالتان؛ فمن وصف بالكبر فهو كبير ومن وصف بالصغر فهو صغير، كما أن من وصف بالكبر فهو كبير فسار من الأكبر إلى الأصغر.
And al-Sa'd said in his commentary on al-'Aqa'id, commenting on al-Nasafi's statement: 'When the servant has both tasdiq (affirmation) and iqrar (confession), it is correct for him to say: I am a believer in truth — because faith is realized — and it is not appropriate for him to say: I am a believer if Allah wills.' [Sa'd explains:] Because if it is for doubt, it is undoubtedly disbelief (kufr). But if it is for politeness (ta'addub) and referring matters to the will of Allah (mashi'at Allah), or due to doubt in the final outcome (al-'aqiba) and end (al-ma'al), not in the present moment, or for seeking blessing (tabarruk) by mentioning Allah, or for disclaiming self-praise and self-admiration, then it is better to avoid it because it implies doubt. That is why he said 'it is not appropriate' rather than 'it is not permissible'? Because if it is not for doubt, there is no reason to negate permissibility. Indeed, many of the Salaf, including the Companions and the Successors collectively, held this view. And this is not like your saying: 'I am young if Allah wills' because youth is not among acquired actions (af'al muktasaba), nor is it something that can be conceived to continue in the final outcome, nor does it involve self-praise or admiration. Rather, it is like your saying: 'I am a ascetic (zahid), pious (muttaqi) if Allah wills.' And some investigators (muhaqqiqun) opined that what the servant attains is the reality of tasdiq by which he leaves disbelief, but tasdiq itself is susceptible to intensity (shidda) and weakness (du'f). And attaining the perfect tasdiq that saves, referred to in His statement: 'Those are the believers in truth. For them are degrees...' (Quran 8:4), is only within the will of Allah (mashi'at Allah). I say: Therefore, the issue of exception in faith is based on the issue of the increase (ziyada) and decrease (nuqsan) of faith, just as the issue of happiness and misery is based on the issue of exception in faith as we mentioned. So whoever says that faith increases and decreases permits exception in it and holds that there is no change (tabaddul) in happiness and misery. And whoever says that faith does not increase or decrease does not permit exception and holds that change occurs in happiness and misery. And the issue of increase and decrease of faith will come in the speech of the author. The conclusion is that the disagreement is verbal (lafzi) as we mentioned, and that faith and disbelief are two states (halatan) by which servants are described. Whoever is described by faith is a believer, and whoever is described by disbelief is a disbeliever, just as greatness (kibr) and smallness (sighar) are two states: whoever is described by greatness is great, and whoever is described by smallness is small, just as whoever is described by greatness is great, so he goes from the greater to the smaller.
Source pages p. 100

Commentary
This passage begins with a citation from Sa'd al-Din al-Taftazani's commentary on al-Nasafi's al-'Aqa'id. The issue is the ruling on a believer saying 'I am a believer if Allah wills (ana mu'min in sha' Allah)'. Sa'd explains that if the statement stems from doubt (shakk) in one's faith, it is kufr. However, if it is motivated by politeness (ta'addub), referring matters to Allah's will, uncertainty about the final outcome (not the present state), seeking blessing, or avoiding self-praise, then it is better to avoid it because it may create the impression of doubt. This is why al-Nasafi said 'does not befit' (la yanbaghi) rather than 'is not permissible' (la yajuz), since permissibility is not negated if the intention is not doubt. Many salaf, including companions, used such expressions. The passage then distinguishes this from statements like 'I am young if Allah wills' because youth is not an acquired act subject to moral evaluation or final outcome. Instead, it is analogous to 'I am an ascetic if Allah wills' because such claims involve self-praise. Next, some investigators (muhaqqiqun) hold that the servant possesses the reality of tasdiq (affirmation) that removes him from kufr, but that tasdiq varies in strength and weakness. The perfect tasdiq that leads to salvation and high degrees is subject to Allah's will. Then the commentator (Maydani) adds: 'I say' (qultu), concluding that the issue of exception in faith is based on the issue of increase and decrease of faith, just as the issue of happiness and misery was based on the issue of exception. Thus, those who hold that faith increases and decreases permit exception and deny change in ultimate states, while those who deny increase and decrease prohibit exception and affirm change. This is ultimately a verbal disagreement. Faith and disbelief are merely descriptive states (halatan) like qualities of bigness and smallness. The final sentence about moving from greater to smaller seems to be an example of how description works: one described as great is great, so he moves from the greater to the smaller (perhaps a metaphorical statement about the nature of change? But the exact meaning is unclear in context).

Key Terms
أنا مؤمن إن شاء الله
التأدب
إحالة الأمور إلى مشيئة الله
الشك في العاقبة
التبريك
التبرؤ من تزكية النفس
التصديق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think saying 'in sha' Allah' about faith is always prohibited regardless of intention.
Correction: Sa'd clarifies that it is only kufr if motivated by doubt. For other intentions, it is permissible but better to avoid.

Checkpoint
According to Sa'd's explanation, if someone says 'I am a believer if Allah wills' out of politeness and not doubt, what is the ruling?
A) It is forbidden (haram)
B) It is permissible but better to avoid
C) It is recommended
D) It is obligatory

Key Takeaway
The statement 'I am a believer if Allah wills' is permissible for valid intentions other than doubt, but it is better to avoid it to prevent misunderstanding.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you say 'if Allah wills' about your faith, what is the true intention in your heart? Is it humility or hidden doubt? Be honest with yourself.
?
Are you comfortable with the idea that your faith is weak and subject to Allah's will? Or do you feel pride in your certainty? How does that affect your reliance on Him?
?
How often do you consider that your final outcome is unknown, and does that drive you to seek Allah's mercy or lull you into complacency? What one change will you make today to address this?

Faith and Disbelief

Exception in Faith and the Debate on Its Increase and Decrease
Maydani shows the relationship between the exception in faith and the increase/decrease debate.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the issue of exception in faith is linked to the debate on whether faith increases and decreases, and why the disagreement is ultimately verbal.

Core Idea
The permissibility of exception in faith depends on whether one believes faith can increase and decrease.

In this lesson, we continue from Sa'd's explanation and see how Maydani connects the exception statement to the broader theological debate about the nature of faith. He argues that the issue of saying 'if Allah wills' is built upon whether faith is considered to increase and decrease. This connection also relates to the question of ultimate happiness and misery.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the passage starting from 'قلت: فعلى هذا تكون...' and note how Maydani links the two issues.
Look for the phrases 'مبنية على' and 'مبنية على'.
2
Identify the two positions
Identify the two conflicting views: those who say faith increases and decreases, and those who say it does not. Note the consequences for exception and for ultimate states.
3
Understand the verbal disagreement
Maydani concludes that the disagreement is verbal (lafzi). Reflect on what he means by this and how the analogy with 'greatness' and 'smallness' illustrates it.
The final sentence about moving from greater to smaller may be obscure; focus on the main point.
4
Connect to previous lesson
How does this lesson build on the previous one about intention? Notice that the permissibility of exception is now tied to a doctrinal position on faith's nature.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقال السعد في شرح العقائد عند قول النسفي: «وإذا وجد من العبد التصديق والإقرار صح له أن يقول: أنا مؤمن حقا - لتحقق الإيمان- ولا ينبغي أن يقول: أنا مؤمن إن شاء الله»: لأنه إن كان للشك فهو كفر لا محالة، وإن كان للتأدب وإحالة الأمور إلى مشيئة الله تعالى أو للشك في العاقبة والمآل لا في الآن والحال أو للتبرك بذكر الله تعالى أو للتبرؤ عن تزكية نفسه والإعجاب بحاله فالأولى تركه لما أنه يوهم الشك؛ ولهذا قال: "ولا ينبغي " دون أن يقول: "ولا يجوز "؛ لأنه إذا لم يكن للشك فلا معنى لنفي الجواز، كيف وقد ذهب إليه كثير من السلف حتى الصحابة والتابعين أجمعين، وليس هذا مثل قولك : أنا شاب إن شاء الله؛ لأن الشباب ليس من الأفعال المكتسبة ولا مما يتصور البقاء عليه في العاقبة والمآل ولا مما تحصل به تزكية النفس والإعجاب؛ بل مثل قولك: أنا زاهد متق إن شاء الله . وذهب بعض المحققين إلى أن الحاصل للعبد هو حقيقة التصديق الذي به يخرج عن الكفر، لكن التصديق بنفسه قابل للشدة والضعف، وحصول التصديق الكامل المنجي المشار إليه بقوله تعالى: (أَوَلَتِبِكَ هُمُ الْمُؤْمِنُونَ حَقًّا هُمْ دَرَجَتُ ... الآية [سورة الأنفال آية : ٤] إنما هو في مشيئة الله تعالى(۱). قلت: فعلى هذا تكون مسألة الاستثناء في الإيمان مبنية على مسألة زيادة الإيمان ونقصانه كما أن مسألة السعادة والشقاوة مبنية على مسألة الاستثناء في الإيمان كما ذكرنا؛ فمن قال: إن الإيمان يزيد وينقص قال بجواز الاستثناء فيه وبعدم التبديل والتغيير في السعادة والشقاوة، ومن قال إن الإيمان لا يزيد ولا ينقص قال بعدم جواز الاستثناء وقال بالتبديل والتغيير في السعادة والشقاوة وسيأتي في كلام المصنف مسألة الزيادة والنقصان في الإيمان. والحاصل أن الخلاف لفظي كما ذكرنا وأن الإيمان والكفر حالتان يوصف بهما العباد؛ فمن وصف بالإيمان فهو مؤمن ومن وصف بالكفر فهو كافر، كما أن الكبر والصَّغَر حالتان؛ فمن وصف بالكبر فهو كبير ومن وصف بالصغر فهو صغير، كما أن من وصف بالكبر فهو كبير فسار من الأكبر إلى الأصغر.
And al-Sa'd said in his commentary on al-'Aqa'id, commenting on al-Nasafi's statement: 'When the servant has both tasdiq (affirmation) and iqrar (confession), it is correct for him to say: I am a believer in truth — because faith is realized — and it is not appropriate for him to say: I am a believer if Allah wills.' [Sa'd explains:] Because if it is for doubt, it is undoubtedly disbelief (kufr). But if it is for politeness (ta'addub) and referring matters to the will of Allah (mashi'at Allah), or due to doubt in the final outcome (al-'aqiba) and end (al-ma'al), not in the present moment, or for seeking blessing (tabarruk) by mentioning Allah, or for disclaiming self-praise and self-admiration, then it is better to avoid it because it implies doubt. That is why he said 'it is not appropriate' rather than 'it is not permissible'? Because if it is not for doubt, there is no reason to negate permissibility. Indeed, many of the Salaf, including the Companions and the Successors collectively, held this view. And this is not like your saying: 'I am young if Allah wills' because youth is not among acquired actions (af'al muktasaba), nor is it something that can be conceived to continue in the final outcome, nor does it involve self-praise or admiration. Rather, it is like your saying: 'I am a ascetic (zahid), pious (muttaqi) if Allah wills.' And some investigators (muhaqqiqun) opined that what the servant attains is the reality of tasdiq by which he leaves disbelief, but tasdiq itself is susceptible to intensity (shidda) and weakness (du'f). And attaining the perfect tasdiq that saves, referred to in His statement: 'Those are the believers in truth. For them are degrees...' (Quran 8:4), is only within the will of Allah (mashi'at Allah). I say: Therefore, the issue of exception in faith is based on the issue of the increase (ziyada) and decrease (nuqsan) of faith, just as the issue of happiness and misery is based on the issue of exception in faith as we mentioned. So whoever says that faith increases and decreases permits exception in it and holds that there is no change (tabaddul) in happiness and misery. And whoever says that faith does not increase or decrease does not permit exception and holds that change occurs in happiness and misery. And the issue of increase and decrease of faith will come in the speech of the author. The conclusion is that the disagreement is verbal (lafzi) as we mentioned, and that faith and disbelief are two states (halatan) by which servants are described. Whoever is described by faith is a believer, and whoever is described by disbelief is a disbeliever, just as greatness (kibr) and smallness (sighar) are two states: whoever is described by greatness is great, and whoever is described by smallness is small, just as whoever is described by greatness is great, so he goes from the greater to the smaller.
Source pages p. 100

Commentary
This passage begins with a citation from Sa'd al-Din al-Taftazani's commentary on al-Nasafi's al-'Aqa'id. The issue is the ruling on a believer saying 'I am a believer if Allah wills (ana mu'min in sha' Allah)'. Sa'd explains that if the statement stems from doubt (shakk) in one's faith, it is kufr. However, if it is motivated by politeness (ta'addub), referring matters to Allah's will, uncertainty about the final outcome (not the present state), seeking blessing, or avoiding self-praise, then it is better to avoid it because it may create the impression of doubt. This is why al-Nasafi said 'does not befit' (la yanbaghi) rather than 'is not permissible' (la yajuz), since permissibility is not negated if the intention is not doubt. Many salaf, including companions, used such expressions. The passage then distinguishes this from statements like 'I am young if Allah wills' because youth is not an acquired act subject to moral evaluation or final outcome. Instead, it is analogous to 'I am an ascetic if Allah wills' because such claims involve self-praise. Next, some investigators (muhaqqiqun) hold that the servant possesses the reality of tasdiq (affirmation) that removes him from kufr, but that tasdiq varies in strength and weakness. The perfect tasdiq that leads to salvation and high degrees is subject to Allah's will. Then the commentator (Maydani) adds: 'I say' (qultu), concluding that the issue of exception in faith is based on the issue of increase and decrease of faith, just as the issue of happiness and misery was based on the issue of exception. Thus, those who hold that faith increases and decreases permit exception and deny change in ultimate states, while those who deny increase and decrease prohibit exception and affirm change. This is ultimately a verbal disagreement. Faith and disbelief are merely descriptive states (halatan) like qualities of bigness and smallness. The final sentence about moving from greater to smaller seems to be an example of how description works: one described as great is great, so he moves from the greater to the smaller (perhaps a metaphorical statement about the nature of change? But the exact meaning is unclear in context).

Key Terms
زيادة الإيمان
نقصان الإيمان
الاستثناء
الخلاف لفظي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that the debate on increase and decrease of faith is unrelated to the permissibility of saying 'in sha' Allah' about faith.
Correction: Maydani explicitly states that the exception issue is built upon the increase/decrease issue.

Checkpoint
According to Maydani, what is the consequence for those who say faith does not increase or decrease regarding the exception in faith?
A) They permit exception
B) They do not permit exception
C) They consider it obligatory
D) They are silent on the matter

Key Takeaway
The permissibility of exception in faith is logically tied to whether one believes faith increases and decreases, and the disagreement is ultimately verbal.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If faith can increase, what does that mean for the moments you feel distant from Allah? Are you content with your current state, or do you actively seek growth? What specific step will you take today to increase your faith?
?
The passage calls the disagreement 'verbal'—but how often do you treat theological debates as mere words while your heart remains unchanged? Is your belief in the increase and decrease of faith merely an intellectual stance, or does it drive you to repent, seek knowledge, and perform good deeds?
?
Consider the analogy: faith and disbelief are states like greatness and smallness. Are you truly described by your faith, or do you rely on a label while your actions tell a different story? Will you let this lesson push you to embody faith, not just affirm it?

The Ruling on Istithna' in Faith
Al-Maydani states the ruling and explains intentions behind istithna'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the ruling on saying 'I am a believer, if Allah wills' and the different intentions that affect its permissibility.

Core Idea
Saying 'if Allah wills' about faith is only blameworthy when it stems from doubt.

Al-Maydani explains the ruling on the statement 'I am a believer, if Allah wills,' distinguishing between permissible and impermissible intentions. He clarifies that while it is better to avoid it, it is not forbidden when said for politeness or to avoid self-praise.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on the ruling
Read the Arabic passage that states the ruling and the reasons for saying 'if Allah wills'. Notice the author's distinction between 'la yanbaghi' and 'la yajuz'.
The passage begins with 'التصديق والإقرار صح له أن يقول...'
2
Identify the different intentions
List the five intentions mentioned: doubt (shakk), politeness, doubt about the end, seeking blessing, and avoiding self-praise. Understand the ruling for each.
Only doubt leads to disbelief; the others make it disliked, not forbidden.
3
Compare with the youth example
Understand why saying 'if Allah wills' about youth is different from saying it about faith. Al-Maydani explains that youth is not an acquired action or a matter of outcome.
This clarifies that the ruling is specific to faith-related statements.

شرح العقيدة الطحاوية المسماة: بيان السنة والجماعة
التصديق والإقرار صح له أن يقول: أنا مؤمن حقا - لتحقق الإيمان- ولا ينبغي أن يقول: أنا مؤمن إن شاء الله»: لأنه إن كان للشك فهو كفر لا محالة، وإن كان للتأدب وإحالة الأمور إلى مشيئة الله تعالى أو للشك في العاقبة والمآل لا في الآن والحال أو للتبرك بذكر الله تعالى أو للتبرؤ عن تزكية نفسه والإعجاب بحاله فالأولى تركه لما أنه يوهم الشك؛ ولهذا قال: "ولا ينبغي " دون أن يقول: "ولا يجوز "؛ لأنه إذا لم يكن للشك فلا معنى لنفي الجواز، كيف وقد ذهب إليه كثير من السلف حتى الصحابة والتابعين أجمعين، وليس هذا مثل قولك : أنا شاب إن شاء الله؛ لأن الشباب ليس من الأفعال المكتسبة ولا مما يتصور البقاء عليه في العاقبة والمآل ولا مما تحصل به تزكية النفس والإعجاب؛ بل مثل قولك: أنا زاهد متق إن شاء الله . وذهب بعض المحققين إلى أن الحاصل للعبد هو حقيقة التصديق الذي به يخرج عن الكفر، لكن التصديق بنفسه قابل للشدة والضعف، وحصول التصديق الكامل المنجي المشار إليه بقوله تعالى: (أَوَلَتِبِكَ هُمُ الْمُؤْمِنُونَ حَقًّا هُمْ دَرَجَتُ ... الآية [سورة الأنفال آية : ٤] إنما هو في مشيئة الله تعالى. قلت: فعلى هذا تكون مسألة الاستثناء في الإيمان مبنية على مسألة زيادة الإيمان ونقصانه كما أن مسألة السعادة والشقاوة مبنية على مسألة الاستثناء في الإيمان كما ذكرنا؛ فمن قال: إن الإيمان يزيد وينقص قال بجواز الاستثناء فيه وبعدم التبديل والتغيير في السعادة والشقاوة، ومن قال إن الإيمان لا يزيد ولا ينقص قال بعدم جواز الاستثناء وقال بالتبديل والتغيير في السعادة والشقاوة وسيأتي في كلام المصنف مسألة الزيادة والنقصان في الإيمان. والحاصل أن الخلاف لفظي كما ذكرنا وأن الإيمان والكفر حالتان يوصف بهما العباد؛ فمن وصف بالإيمان فهو مؤمن ومن وصف بالكفر فهو كافر، كما أن الكبر والصَّغَر حالتان؛ فمن وصف بالكبر فهو كبير ومن وصف بالصغر فهو صغير، ولو كان المعتبر في صحة الوصف الخاتمة ما كان الموصوف بالصغر يسمى صغيرًا؛ لأنه إذا كبر ومات مات كبيرًا لا صغيرًا ولا نزاع في صحة تسمية من اتصف بالصغر صغيرًا في تلك الحالة فكذا هذا، ومتى صح الاتصاف كان مقطوعا به من غير شك؛ فمن اتصف بالإيمان فهو مؤمن حقا في تلك الحالة ومن اتصف بالكفر فهو كافر حقا في تلك الحالة.
وأما بقاء وصف الإيمان على المؤمن إلى الموت وبقاء وصف الكفر على الكافر إلى الموت فليس من الأمور التي تدخل تحت مقدور المكلف إلا باعتبار الوقت الذي هو فيه لعدم علمه بذلك؛ فإن الله تعالى هو الذي استأثر بعلمه. وبيان ذلك: أن الساعة التي أنت فيها إن كانت إيمانًا فقل : أنا مؤمن إيمانا حقا، واشكر نعمة الله تعالى عليك باعترافك بتحققها فيك، ولا تقل أنا مؤمن إن شاء الله فتكون شاكا في تلك النعمة مترددًا فيها ربما إنها تكون نقمة غير شاكر عليها ربك؛ فيلزم من ذلك أنك لا تشكر ربك على نعمة من نعمه التي أنعمها عليك أبدًا، لأن أعظم النعم التي هي نعمة الإيمان ترددت في أنها نعمة عليك أم نقمة؛ فكيف غيرها من النعم، وهو ينافي حصول الشكر من أحد، وشكر المنعم فرض. وإن كانت ساعتك التي أنت فيها كفرًا فقل : أنا كافر حقا واعزم على إزالة ذلك منك في الحال بضده وهو الإيمان، واشكر ربك على التوفيق لذلك، وبالله المستعان، كذا في المطالب للعارف سيدي عبدالغني
Explanation of al-Aqida al-Tahawiyya named: Bayan al-Sunna wal-Jama'a. [Regarding] affirmation and attestation, it is correct for him to say: 'I am a believer truly' - due to the realization of faith - and he should not say: 'I am a believer, if Allah wills' - because if it is for doubt, it is unbelief without exception, and if it is for politeness and deferring matters to the will of Allah Most High, or for doubt about the end and outcome not about the present and current state, or for seeking blessing by mentioning Allah Most High, or for disavowing self-praise and admiration of one's state, then it is better to leave it because it suggests doubt. For this reason he said: 'he should not' without saying 'it is not permissible'; because if it is not for doubt, there is no meaning to denying permissibility, especially since many of the Salaf, even the Companions and the Followers altogether, held this view. And this is not like your saying: 'I am a young man, if Allah wills', because youth is not among acquired actions nor among things that can be conceived to continue in the end and outcome, nor does it involve self-praise and admiration. Rather, it is like your saying: 'I am a pious ascetic, if Allah wills.' And some investigators held that what the servant possesses is the reality of tasdiq (affirmation) by which he leaves unbelief, but tasdiq in itself is susceptible to strength and weakness, and the attainment of complete saving tasdiq indicated by His saying: 'It is those who are the believers in truth. For them are degrees...' [Surat al-Anfal: 4] is only in the will of Allah Most High. I say: On this basis, the issue of istithna' (exception) in faith is built on the issue of increase and decrease of faith, just as the issue of happiness and misery is built on the issue of istithna' in faith as we mentioned. Thus, whoever says that faith increases and decreases permits istithna' in it and denies alteration and change in happiness and misery; and whoever says that faith does not increase or decrease denies the permissibility of istithna' and affirms alteration and change in happiness and misery. And the issue of increase and decrease of faith will come in the words of the author. The conclusion is that the dispute is verbal as we mentioned, and that faith and unbelief are two states by which servants are described; so whoever is described by faith is a believer, and whoever is described by unbelief is an unbeliever, just as greatness and smallness are two states; so whoever is described by greatness is great, and whoever is described by smallness is small. And if the criterion for the validity of the description were the end, then he who is described by smallness would not be called small, because when he grows up and dies, he dies great, not small; and there is no dispute about the correctness of calling one who is characterized by smallness 'small' in that state; so likewise this. And whenever the description is valid, it is certain without doubt; so whoever is characterized by faith is a believer truly in that state, and whoever is characterized by unbelief is an unbeliever truly in that state. As for the persistence of the description of faith on the believer until death and the persistence of the description of unbelief on the unbeliever until death, this is not among the things that fall under the power of the morally responsible except in consideration of the moment he is in, due to his lack of knowledge of it; for Allah Most High alone has exclusive knowledge of it. And the clarification of that: if the hour you are in is faith, then say: 'I am a believer truly with faith', and thank Allah Most High for His grace upon you by acknowledging its realization in you, and do not say 'I am a believer, if Allah wills', for then you become doubtful of that grace, hesitant about it, perhaps it is a punishment, ungrateful to your Lord for it; and it follows from that that you never thank your Lord for any of His graces that He has bestowed upon you, because the greatest of graces, which is the grace of faith, you are hesitant about whether it is a grace upon you or a punishment; then what about other graces? And this contradicts the attainment of gratitude from anyone, and gratitude to the Bestower of grace is an obligation. And if the hour you are in is unbelief, then say: 'I am an unbeliever truly' and resolve to remove that from yourself immediately by its opposite, which is faith, and thank your Lord for granting success to that. And Allah is the one sought for help. Thus in al-Matalib by the gnostic Sayyidi Abdul Ghani.
Source pages p. 101

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the Tahawiyya text regarding the statement 'I am a believer, if Allah wills' (istithna' fi al-iman). It is a combination of a ruling, an analysis of intentions, and a theological argument about the nature of faith. The author begins by stating the ruling: it is correct for one who possesses faith to say 'I am a believer truly', and he should not say 'I am a believer, if Allah wills.' He then explains the reasons one might say the latter. If it is due to doubt (shakk), it is outright disbelief. But if it is for politeness, deferring to Allah's will, doubt about the final outcome (not the present state), seeking blessing, or avoiding self-praise, then it is better to avoid it because it suggests doubt. The commentator notes that the imam said 'he should not' (la yanbaghi) rather than 'it is not permissible' (la yajuz) because when the intention is not doubt, prohibition is inappropriate; indeed, many salaf including Companions and Followers said it for such reasons. He distinguishes it from saying 'I am a young man, if Allah wills,' since youth is not an acquired action or a matter of enduring outcome, but it is like saying 'I am a pious ascetic, if Allah wills,' which involves acquired virtue and future uncertainty. Next, he cites some investigators who hold that what the servant obtains is the reality of tasdiq (affirmation) that removes him from unbelief, but tasdiq itself is susceptible to strength and weakness. The complete, saving tasdiq mentioned in the Qur'an (al-Anfal: 4) is subject to Allah's will. The commentator then offers his own analysis: the issue of istithna' in faith is built on the issue of increase and decrease of faith. Those who affirm increase and decrease permit istithna' and deny that happiness and misery (final destiny) change. Those who deny increase and decrease prohibit istithna' and affirm that happiness and misery can change. He concludes that the dispute is verbal, using an analogy: faith and unbelief are states just like greatness and smallness. A person is called great or small based on their current state, not their end. Similarly, one who has faith now is truly a believer in that state, and one who has unbelief is truly an unbeliever in that state. The persistence of these states until death is not known to the servant, but that does not affect the current description. Finally, he gives practical advice: if you are in a state of faith, say 'I am a believer truly' and be grateful; do not say 'if Allah wills,' which implies doubt about the present grace. If you are in a state of unbelief, say 'I am an unbeliever truly' and resolve to change immediately. The passage thus covers the ruling, its rationale, the underlying theological dispute, and the practical implication.

Key Terms
إيمان
استثناء
شك
تصديق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think saying 'I am a believer, if Allah wills' is always forbidden.
Correction: It is only forbidden (kufr) when said out of doubt; otherwise it is merely disliked, and many Salaf said it.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, if someone says 'I am a believer, if Allah wills' out of doubt (shakk), what is the ruling?
A) It is permissible but disliked
B) It is disbelief (kufr) without exception
C) It is permitted because it shows humility
D) It is recommended

Key Takeaway
Saying 'I am a believer, if Allah wills' is only impermissible (disbelief) when it stems from doubt; otherwise it is better avoided but not forbidden.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you say 'I am a believer, if Allah wills,' do you ever pause to examine whether a trace of doubt lingers in your heart? What would it take for you to speak with the certainty that your faith is truly realized?
?
Is there an area of your faith or piety where you secretly admire your own devotion? How can the habit of attaching 'if Allah wills' break that pride and remind you that every good deed is from Allah?
?
If you heard a fellow Muslim say 'I am a believer, if Allah wills,' would you assume the worst of their intention? Are you ready to give them the benefit of the doubt as the Salaf did, even if you personally choose not to say it?

The Verbal Dispute and Practical Application
Al-Maydani discusses the connection to increase/decrease, the verbal dispute, and practical advice.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the dispute over istithna' in faith is verbal and how to apply the ruling to your own state of faith or unbelief.

Core Idea
Faith and unbelief are current states, judged truly in the moment, not by the unknown end.

Al-Maydani explores the deeper theological issue behind istithna': whether faith increases and decreases, and how this relates to eternal destiny. He concludes it is a verbal dispute and provides practical guidance for testing one's own state.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage from 'some investigators' onward
Read the Arabic passage that discusses the reality of tasdiq, increase and decrease of faith, and the conclusion that the dispute is verbal.
Notice the connection between istithna' and the issue of increase/decrease of faith.
2
Analyze the analogy with greatness/smallness
Understand how faith and unbelief are like being great or small: they are current states. The validity of the description does not depend on the end.
This shows why the dispute is verbal: both sides agree that a person is described by their current state.
3
Apply the practical advice
Learn the practical guidance: if you are in a state of faith, say 'I am a believer truly' and be grateful; if in unbelief, acknowledge it and resolve to change.
This advice aligns with the ruling and avoids doubt.

وأما بقاء وصف الإيمان على المؤمن إلى الموت وبقاء وصف الكفر على الكافر إلى الموت فليس من الأمور التي تدخل تحت مقدور المكلف إلا باعتبار الوقت الذي هو فيه لعدم علمه بذلك؛ فإن الله تعالى هو الذي استأثر بعلمه. وبيان ذلك: أن الساعة التي أنت فيها إن كانت إيمانًا فقل : أنا مؤمن إيمانا حقا، واشكر نعمة الله تعالى عليك باعترافك بتحققها فيك، ولا تقل أنا مؤمن إن شاء الله فتكون شاكا في تلك النعمة مترددًا فيها ربما إنها تكون نقمة غير شاكر عليها ربك؛ فيلزم من ذلك أنك لا تشكر ربك على نعمة من نعمه التي أنعمها عليك أبدًا، لأن أعظم النعم التي هي نعمة الإيمان ترددت في أنها نعمة عليك أم نقمة؛ فكيف غيرها من النعم، وهو ينافي حصول الشكر من أحد، وشكر المنعم فرض. وإن كانت ساعتك التي أنت فيها كفرًا فقل : أنا كافر حقا واعزم على إزالة ذلك منك في الحال بضده وهو الإيمان، واشكر ربك على التوفيق لذلك، وبالله المستعان، كذا في المطالب للعارف سيدي عبدالغني
Explanation of al-Aqida al-Tahawiyya named: Bayan al-Sunna wal-Jama'a. [Regarding] affirmation and attestation, it is correct for him to say: 'I am a believer truly' - due to the realization of faith - and he should not say: 'I am a believer, if Allah wills' - because if it is for doubt, it is unbelief without exception, and if it is for politeness and deferring matters to the will of Allah Most High, or for doubt about the end and outcome not about the present and current state, or for seeking blessing by mentioning Allah Most High, or for disavowing self-praise and admiration of one's state, then it is better to leave it because it suggests doubt. For this reason he said: 'he should not' without saying 'it is not permissible'; because if it is not for doubt, there is no meaning to denying permissibility, especially since many of the Salaf, even the Companions and the Followers altogether, held this view. And this is not like your saying: 'I am a young man, if Allah wills', because youth is not among acquired actions nor among things that can be conceived to continue in the end and outcome, nor does it involve self-praise and admiration. Rather, it is like your saying: 'I am a pious ascetic, if Allah wills.' And some investigators held that what the servant possesses is the reality of tasdiq (affirmation) by which he leaves unbelief, but tasdiq in itself is susceptible to strength and weakness, and the attainment of complete saving tasdiq indicated by His saying: 'It is those who are the believers in truth. For them are degrees...' [Surat al-Anfal: 4] is only in the will of Allah Most High. I say: On this basis, the issue of istithna' (exception) in faith is built on the issue of increase and decrease of faith, just as the issue of happiness and misery is built on the issue of istithna' in faith as we mentioned. Thus, whoever says that faith increases and decreases permits istithna' in it and denies alteration and change in happiness and misery; and whoever says that faith does not increase or decrease denies the permissibility of istithna' and affirms alteration and change in happiness and misery. And the issue of increase and decrease of faith will come in the words of the author. The conclusion is that the dispute is verbal as we mentioned, and that faith and unbelief are two states by which servants are described; so whoever is described by faith is a believer, and whoever is described by unbelief is an unbeliever, just as greatness and smallness are two states; so whoever is described by greatness is great, and whoever is described by smallness is small. And if the criterion for the validity of the description were the end, then he who is described by smallness would not be called small, because when he grows up and dies, he dies great, not small; and there is no dispute about the correctness of calling one who is characterized by smallness 'small' in that state; so likewise this. And whenever the description is valid, it is certain without doubt; so whoever is characterized by faith is a believer truly in that state, and whoever is characterized by unbelief is an unbeliever truly in that state. As for the persistence of the description of faith on the believer until death and the persistence of the description of unbelief on the unbeliever until death, this is not among the things that fall under the power of the morally responsible except in consideration of the moment he is in, due to his lack of knowledge of it; for Allah Most High alone has exclusive knowledge of it. And the clarification of that: if the hour you are in is faith, then say: 'I am a believer truly with faith', and thank Allah Most High for His grace upon you by acknowledging its realization in you, and do not say 'I am a believer, if Allah wills', for then you become doubtful of that grace, hesitant about it, perhaps it is a punishment, ungrateful to your Lord for it; and it follows from that that you never thank your Lord for any of His graces that He has bestowed upon you, because the greatest of graces, which is the grace of faith, you are hesitant about whether it is a grace upon you or a punishment; then what about other graces? And this contradicts the attainment of gratitude from anyone, and gratitude to the Bestower of grace is an obligation. And if the hour you are in is unbelief, then say: 'I am an unbeliever truly' and resolve to remove that from yourself immediately by its opposite, which is faith, and thank your Lord for granting success to that. And Allah is the one sought for help. Thus in al-Matalib by the gnostic Sayyidi Abdul Ghani.
Source pages p. 101

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the Tahawiyya text regarding the statement 'I am a believer, if Allah wills' (istithna' fi al-iman). It is a combination of a ruling, an analysis of intentions, and a theological argument about the nature of faith. The author begins by stating the ruling: it is correct for one who possesses faith to say 'I am a believer truly', and he should not say 'I am a believer, if Allah wills.' He then explains the reasons one might say the latter. If it is due to doubt (shakk), it is outright disbelief. But if it is for politeness, deferring to Allah's will, doubt about the final outcome (not the present state), seeking blessing, or avoiding self-praise, then it is better to avoid it because it suggests doubt. The commentator notes that the imam said 'he should not' (la yanbaghi) rather than 'it is not permissible' (la yajuz) because when the intention is not doubt, prohibition is inappropriate; indeed, many salaf including Companions and Followers said it for such reasons. He distinguishes it from saying 'I am a young man, if Allah wills,' since youth is not an acquired action or a matter of enduring outcome, but it is like saying 'I am a pious ascetic, if Allah wills,' which involves acquired virtue and future uncertainty. Next, he cites some investigators who hold that what the servant obtains is the reality of tasdiq (affirmation) that removes him from unbelief, but tasdiq itself is susceptible to strength and weakness. The complete, saving tasdiq mentioned in the Qur'an (al-Anfal: 4) is subject to Allah's will. The commentator then offers his own analysis: the issue of istithna' in faith is built on the issue of increase and decrease of faith. Those who affirm increase and decrease permit istithna' and deny that happiness and misery (final destiny) change. Those who deny increase and decrease prohibit istithna' and affirm that happiness and misery can change. He concludes that the dispute is verbal, using an analogy: faith and unbelief are states just like greatness and smallness. A person is called great or small based on their current state, not their end. Similarly, one who has faith now is truly a believer in that state, and one who has unbelief is truly an unbeliever in that state. The persistence of these states until death is not known to the servant, but that does not affect the current description. Finally, he gives practical advice: if you are in a state of faith, say 'I am a believer truly' and be grateful; do not say 'if Allah wills,' which implies doubt about the present grace. If you are in a state of unbelief, say 'I am an unbeliever truly' and resolve to change immediately. The passage thus covers the ruling, its rationale, the underlying theological dispute, and the practical implication.

Key Terms
زيادة الإيمان ونقصانه
خلاف لفظي
تصديق
سعادة
شقاوة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that because the end is unknown, one cannot say 'I am a believer truly' now.
Correction: The passage shows that current state is the valid basis for description; the unknown end does not negate the present reality.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the basis for calling someone a believer or unbeliever?
A) Their final end at death
B) Their current state of faith or unbelief
C) Their intention when speaking
D) The opinion of the majority

Key Takeaway
The dispute over istithna' is verbal because faith and unbelief are judged by the present state, not the unknown end, and one should acknowledge their current state with certainty and gratitude.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you currently acknowledge the grace of faith in your life with certainty, or do you doubt it? What action can you take today to strengthen that certainty and thank Allah for it?
?
If you are aware of any unbelief in your heart—whether doubts, neglect, or sin—are you resolved to immediately remove it by affirming faith and turning back to Allah, or do you delay? What is one step you will take right now?
?
The text says that doubting the grace of faith leads to ingratitude for all blessings. Where in your life have you been ungrateful because you were uncertain about Allah's favor? How will you change that today, starting with the greatest blessing of faith?

Faith and Disbelief

Describing a Person as Truly Believer or Disbeliever in the Present State
Analogy proving present-state description of faith/disbelief

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why a person can be called a true believer or disbeliever in their present state, based on an analogy, and why saying 'if Allah wills' about one's faith can be a form of ingratitude.

Core Idea
Present faith is certain; doubting it with 'in sha Allah' is ingratitude.

This passage from Imam al-Tahawi's creed, as explained by Imam Maydani, addresses a subtle point: can we say someone is truly a believer or disbeliever right now, or must we wait for their final end? Using a clear analogy, the author shows that we describe people based on their current state, not their future. Moreover, he warns against a common misuse of the phrase 'if Allah wills' that can undermine gratitude for the greatest blessing.

Guided Path
1
Read the analogy of the small child
Read the analogy that if the final outcome were the criterion, a small child could not be called small. Notice how this establishes that present state is what matters.
The analogy is simple but powerful for showing the absurdity of using the end to judge the present.
2
Understand the rule of present description
The passage states that whoever is described with faith is truly a believer in that state, and similarly for disbelief. This is certain and not doubtful.
The author emphasizes 'certain without doubt' to counter any hesitation.
3
Consider the two cases: faith and disbelief
The author explains what one should say if in a state of faith (acknowledge and thank Allah) and if in disbelief (acknowledge and resolve to change).
Pay attention to the contrast: for faith, gratitude; for disbelief, immediate action.
4
Reflect on the danger of saying 'if Allah wills'
The passage argues that saying 'if Allah wills' about present faith implies doubt about the blessing, which contradicts the obligation of gratitude.
This is a practical application: we must be certain of our present faith to be grateful.

صغير، ولو كان المعتبر في صحة الوصف الخاتمة ما كان الموصوف بالصغر يسمى صغيرًا؛ لأنه إذا كبر ومات مات كبيرًا لا صغيرًا ولا نزاع في صحة تسمية من اتصف بالصغر صغيرًا في تلك الحالة فكذا هذا، ومتى صح الاتصاف كان مقطوعا به من غير شك؛ فمن اتصف بالإيمان فهو مؤمن حقا في تلك الحالة ومن اتصف بالكفر فهو كافر حقا في تلك الحالة. وأما بقاء وصف الإيمان على المؤمن إلى الموت وبقاء وصف الكفر على الكافر إلى الموت فليس من الأمور التي تدخل تحت مقدور المكلف إلا باعتبار الوقت الذي هو فيه لعدم علمه بذلك؛ فإن الله تعالى هو الذي استأثر بعلمه. وبيان ذلك: أن الساعة التي أنت فيها إن كانت إيمانًا فقل: أنا مؤمن إيمانا حقا، واشكر نعمة الله تعالى عليك باعترافك بتحققها فيك، ولا تقل أنا مؤمن إن شاء الله فتكون شاكا في تلك النعمة مترددًا فيها ربما إنها تكون نقمة غير شاكر عليها ربك؛ فيلزم من ذلك أنك لا تشكر ربك على نعمة من نعمه التي أنعمها عليك أبدًا، لأن أعظم النعم التي هي نعمة الإيمان ترددت في أنها نعمة عليك أم نقمة؛ فكيف غيرها من النعم، وهو ينافي حصول الشكر من أحد، وشكر المنعم فرض. وإن كانت ساعتك التي أنت فيها كفرًا فقل: أنا كافر حقا واعزم على إزالة ذلك منك في الحال بضده وهو الإيمان، واشكر ربك على التوفيق لذلك، وبالله المستعان. كذا في المطالب للعارف سيدي عبدالغني
Small, and if the consideration for the validity of description were the final outcome, then the one described as small would not be called small; because when he grows up and dies, he dies as an adult, not as a child, and there is no dispute about the validity of calling one who is described with smallness 'small' in that state. So likewise this. And whenever the description is valid, it is certain without doubt. So whoever is described with faith is truly a believer in that state, and whoever is described with disbelief is truly a disbeliever in that state. As for the continuation of the description of faith upon the believer until death, and the continuation of the description of disbelief upon the disbeliever until death, it is not among the matters that fall under the ability of the accountable person except in relation to the time he is in, because of his lack of knowledge of that. Indeed, Allah Almighty alone has exclusive knowledge of it. And the explanation of that is: the hour in which you are, if it is faith, then say: 'I am a believer truly,' and thank Allah Almighty for His blessing upon you by acknowledging its realization in you. And do not say: 'I am a believer if Allah wills,' for then you would be doubtful of that blessing, wavering concerning it, perhaps it is a punishment, not thanking your Lord for it. So it follows from that that you would never thank your Lord for any of His blessings that He has bestowed upon you, because the greatest of blessings, which is the blessing of faith, you have doubted whether it is a blessing upon you or a punishment. So how about other blessings? And that contradicts the occurrence of gratitude from anyone, and gratitude to the Benefactor is obligatory. And if the hour in which you are is disbelief, then say: 'I am a disbeliever truly,' and resolve to remove that from yourself immediately by its opposite, which is faith, and thank your Lord for success in that. And Allah is the one whose help is sought. Thus in 'al-Matalib' by the knower Sayyidi 'Abd al-Ghani.
Source pages p. 102

Commentary
This passage is an argument establishing the validity of describing a person as truly a believer or disbeliever in his present state, based on an analogy. The author begins by drawing an analogy: if we consider the final outcome (khatima) as the criterion for the correctness of a description, then a person who is currently small would not be called 'small' because he will grow up and die as an adult. Yet there is no dispute that we call a small person 'small' in that present state. Similarly, faith and disbelief are attributed truthfully based on the present state, without regard to the end. The author then emphasizes that when the description is valid, it is certain and not doubtful. Whoever is presently characterized by faith is truly a believer, and whoever is presently characterized by disbelief is truly a disbeliever, in that state. Then he addresses the continuation of these descriptions until death: that is not within the ability of the accountable person to control because he does not know the future; only Allah knows it. The author then explains that one should not say 'I am a believer if Allah wills' regarding one's current faith, because that implies doubt about the blessing of faith, which is the greatest blessing. If one doubts it, he would be ungrateful, and gratitude to Allah is obligatory. Similarly, if one is in a state of disbelief, he should acknowledge it truthfully and immediately resolve to change. The passage concludes by citing this from 'al-Matalib' of Sayyidi 'Abd al-Ghani.

Correction: This passage shows it can be ingratitude when used for present faith, because it implies doubt about the blessing.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why should one not say 'I am a believer if Allah wills' about one's current state of faith?
A) Because it implies doubt about the greatest blessing of faith and ingratitude to Allah.
B) Because one must always be humble and never claim certainty in faith.
C) Because the future is unknown and one might lose faith.
D) Because it is a form of bida in speech.

Key Takeaway
A person is truthfully called believer or disbeliever based on their present state; gratitude for faith demands certainty, not conditional phrasing.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you describe your own faith, do you sometimes add 'in sha Allah' out of humility? Have you considered that this might actually be ingratitude for the faith you have right now? Will you commit to saying 'Alhamdulillah, I am a believer' instead, as an act of gratitude?
?
If you were to examine your heart this very hour, are you certain that you have iman? Or is there a hidden wavering that you have been afraid to confront? What would it cost you to honestly say 'I am a believer truly' or 'I am a disbeliever truly' and act accordingly?
?
The lesson says that doubting the greatest blessing (faith) prevents all gratitude. Can you think of a time when your uncertainty about your own faith made you less thankful to Allah? How will you change that today?

The Two Types of Knowledge and the Necessity of Taslim
Maydani classifies knowledge into existing and absent, with consequences for belief.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two categories of knowledge in Islam (existing and absent) and why proper faith requires both accepting revealed knowledge and abandoning the pursuit of hidden knowledge.

Core Idea
Faith is built on accepting what Allah has revealed and leaving the unseen to Him.

This passage from the Sharh al-Tahawiyyah explains a fundamental principle of Islamic creed: knowledge is divided into two types. The first is the knowledge that Allah has made available through revelation and the Shari'ah; the second is the hidden knowledge that only Allah possesses. The author, Imam Maydani, draws out the theological implications of this division, showing that both denying revealed knowledge and claiming hidden knowledge are acts of disbelief. As we read, pay attention to how the concept of 'taslim' (submission) is tied to the rank of those firmly grounded in knowledge.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the key terms: العلم الموجود and العلم المفقود. Also note the Qur'anic reference to the 'rasikhun fi al-ilm'.
The passage begins by stating this is the sum of what is needed by the illuminated saints.
2
Identify the two types of knowledge
Find where the author states 'knowledge is two kinds'. Understand what each type refers to: existing knowledge is what is available in creation (Shari'ah), absent is hidden with Allah.
3
Understand the consequences
Note the two rules: denying existing knowledge is kufr, and claiming absent knowledge is kufr. Ask yourself why the second is also kufr?
The second is kufr because it claims what only Allah knows.
4
Grasp the necessity of taslim
Read the conclusion: faith is only valid by accepting existing knowledge and abandoning the search for absent knowledge. This is the meaning of taslim.
Taslim is the characteristic of the firmly grounded in knowledge.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فهذا جملة ما يحتاج إليه مَنْ هُوَ مُنَوَّرٌ قَلْبُهُ مِنْ أَوْلِيَاءِ الله تَعَالَى، وَهِيَ دَرَجَةُ الرَّاسِخِينَ في العِلْمِ؛ لأَنَّ العِلْمَ عِلْمَانِ عِلْمٌ فِي الخَلْقِ مَوْجُودٌ وَعِلْمٌ فِي الخَلْقِ مَفْقُودٌ؛ فَإِنْكَارُ العِلْمِ المَوْجُودِ كُفْرٌ، وَادَّعَاءُ العِلْمِ المَفْقُودِ كُفْرٌ، وَلَا يَصِحُ الإِيمَانُ إِلَّا بِقَبُولِ العِلْم الموجود وترك طلب العلم المفقود. فهذا جملة ما يحتاج إليه مريد اليقين من هو منور قلبه من أولياء الله تعالى المتقين (وهي) أي صفة التسليم (درجة) أي مرقاة الراسخين في العلم) (يقولون وامنا به كل من عند ربنا) [سورة آل عمران آية: ٧]؛ (لأن العلم علمان علم في الخلق (موجود) وفيه مرغوب وإليه مندوب وعلم في الخلق مفقود استأثر بعلمه علام الغيوب؛ فإنكار العلم الموجود برد أو طعن أو تهاون بالحدود (كفر) بلا خلاف وجحود، وادعاء العلم المفقود الذي بلا خلاف وجحود، استأثر بعلمه علام الغيوب (كفر) أيضًا وعنود؛ (و) لذا قال: (لا يصح الإيمان إلا بقبول العلم الموجود) والعمل على مقتضاه (وترك طلب العلم المفقود) بالتسليم وتفويض علمه لمولاه .
This is the sum of what is needed by one whose heart is illuminated from the saints of Allah Most High, and it is the rank of those firmly grounded in knowledge. Because knowledge is two kinds: knowledge existing in creation and knowledge absent from creation. Denying the existing knowledge is disbelief, and claiming the absent knowledge is disbelief. Faith is not valid except by accepting the existing knowledge and abandoning the search for the absent knowledge. This is the sum of what is needed by the seeker of certainty whose heart is illuminated from the saints of Allah Most High, the pious. (And it) i.e., the characteristic of al-taslim (is a rank) i.e., a ladder of those firmly grounded in knowledge (who say: 'We believe in it; all is from our Lord') [Qur'an 3:7]; (because knowledge is two kinds: knowledge in creation (existing) and it is desirable and recommended; and knowledge in creation (absent) with which the Knower of the unseen has exclusive knowledge. Denying the existing knowledge, by rejection or criticism or negligence of the limits, is disbelief without dispute and denial; and claiming the absent knowledge, which without dispute and denial, the Knower of the unseen has exclusive knowledge, is also disbelief and stubbornness. (And) therefore he said: 'Faith is not valid except by accepting the existing knowledge' and acting accordingly 'and abandoning the search for the absent knowledge' by submission and delegating its knowledge to his Lord.
Source pages p. 107

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on a statement from the Tahawiyyah creed regarding knowledge and submission. It begins by stating that this is what is needed by the illuminated saints, and it is the rank of the 'rasikhun fi al-ilm' (those firmly grounded in knowledge). The reason is that knowledge is of two types: existing knowledge (al-ilm al-mawjud) which is available in creation (through revelation and Shari'ah), and absent knowledge (al-ilm al-mafqud) which is hidden and known only to Allah. Denying the existing knowledge—whether by rejecting it, criticizing it, or being negligent of its boundaries—is clear disbelief. Claiming to possess the absent knowledge is also disbelief, because it is exclusive to Allah. Therefore, faith is only valid by accepting the existing knowledge and acting upon it, and by abandoning the pursuit of the absent knowledge, through submission (taslim) and delegating its knowledge to Allah. The commentary then quotes the Quranic verse from Surah Al-Imran (3:7) about those firmly grounded in knowledge who say 'We believe in it; all is from our Lord.' The passage emphasizes that the path of the righteous is to accept what Allah has revealed and not to delve into what He has not revealed.

Key Terms
العلم الموجود
العلم المفقود
التسليم
الراسخون في العلم
الإيمان

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Seeking hidden knowledge (ilm al-ghayb) is a virtuous act of piety.
Correction: Claiming knowledge of the unseen is kufr, as it is exclusive to Allah. The passage clearly states that claiming the absent knowledge is disbelief.

Checkpoint
According to this passage, what is the consequence of denying the existing knowledge?
A) It is a minor sin
B) It is disbelief (kufr)
C) It is permissible if done with good intention
D) It is only discouraged

Key Takeaway
Faith requires accepting the knowledge Allah has revealed and leaving the hidden knowledge to Him.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Which 'existing knowledge' from Allah have you been neglecting, criticizing, or treating lightly? Will you commit to accepting it fully starting today?
?
Have you ever sought knowledge that is hidden and belongs only to Allah, such as trying to predict the future or insisting on knowing the wisdom behind every decree? How does this passage challenge that pursuit?
?
The passage says faith is not valid without taslim. Is there an area of your life where you have refused to submit to what Allah has revealed? What will you do about that resistance today?

Faith and Disbelief
beginner

Creedal Affirmations on Angels, Prophets, and Books
Affirms belief in angels, prophets, books, and their protection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the core creedal statements regarding angels, prophets, and revealed books, and the doctrine that prophets are protected from anything that diminishes their rank.

Core Idea
The prophets and angels were upon clear truth and divinely protected.

This lesson focuses on the foundational affirmations of faith in the unseen: angels, prophets, and books. The text emphatically declares that all prophets and messengers were upon clear truth and were safeguarded from any deficiency in their lofty stations. Understanding this protection is key to respecting their role.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice that the passage contains both a concise and a detailed version of the creed.
2
Identify the three categories
The passage mentions angels, prophets, and books. Find each one and note how they are described.
Look for the word 'المكرمين' for angels and 'جميع' for prophets and books.
3
Reflect on the doctrine of protection
The text says prophets are 'معصومين' from everything that leads to deficiency. Consider what this means for their role in conveying revelation.
This doctrine distinguishes Sunni Islam from some other perspectives.

وَنُؤْمِنُ بِالمَلائِكَةِ وَالنَّبِيِّينَ وَالكُتُبِ المُنَزَّلَةِ عَلَى الْمُرْسَلِينَ، وَنَشْهَدُ أَنَّهُمْ كَانُوا عَلَى الحَقِّ المُبِينِ، وَنُسَمِّي أَهْلَ قِبْلَتِنَا مُسْلِمِينَ مُؤْمِنِينَ مَا دَامُوا بِمَا جَاءَ بِهِ النَّبِيُّ عَلَيهِ الصَّلَاةُ وَالسَّلَامُ مُعْتَرِفِينَ وَلَهُ بِكُلِّ مَا قَالَ وَأَخْبَرَ مُصَدِّقِينَ غَيْرَ مُكَذِّبِينَ. ونؤمن بالملائكة المكرمين وبجميع النبيين والمرسلين وبجميع الكتب المنزلة على الأنبياء المرسلين صلوات الله وسلامه عليهم أجمعين ونشهد أنهم كلهم كانوا على الحق المبين، وعن جميع ما يؤدي إلى نقص مراتبهم العلية معصومين. ونسمي أهل قبلتنا وهم الذين شهدوا شهادتنا واستقبلوا قبلتنا وصلوا صلاتنا وأكلوا ذبيحتنا مسلمين ومؤمنين وإن وصفوا بارتكاب الكبائر فاسقين ما داموا أي مدة دوامهم بما أي بالذي جاء به النبي عليه الصلاة والسلام معترفين وله بكل ما قال وأخبر به مصدقين جازمين به غير مكذبين؛ ففي صحيح البخاري عن أنس بن مالك قال: قال رسول الله : مَنْ صَلَّى صَلَاتَنَا وَاسْتَقْبَلَ قِبْلَتَنَا وَأَكَلَ ذَبِيحَتَنَا فَذَلِكَ المُسْلِمُ الَّذِي لَهُ ذِمَّةُ الله وَذِمَّةٌ رَسُولِهِ فَلَا تُخْفِرُوا الله في ذِمَّتِهِ، وفيه عن أنس قال: قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم: أُمِرْتُ أَنْ أُقَاتِلَ النَّاسَ حَتَّى يَقُولُوا: لَا إِلَهَ إِلَّا اللهُ فَإِذَا قَالُوهَا وَصَلُّوا صَلَاتَنَا وَاسْتَقْبَلُوا قِبْلَتَنَا وَذَبَحُوا ذَبِيحَتَنَا فَقَدْ حَرَّمَتْ عَلَيْنَا دِمَاؤُهُم وَأَمْوَالَهُم إِلَّا بِحَقِّهَا وَحِسَابُهُم عَلَى الله.
We believe in the angels, and the prophets, and the books revealed to the messengers, and we testify that they were upon clear truth, and we name the people of our qibla as Muslims and believers as long as they are acknowledging what the Prophet (peace and salutation be upon him) brought and are believing in all he said and informed, not denying. And we believe in the honored angels, and all the prophets and messengers, and all the books revealed to the prophets, the messengers, may the blessings of Allah and His peace be upon them all, and we testify that all of them were upon clear truth, and they are protected from everything that leads to deficiency in their lofty ranks. And we name the people of our qibla—those who bear witness to our testimony, face our qibla, pray our prayer, and eat our slaughtered meat—as Muslims and believers, even if they are described as committing major sins and are sinful, as long as—i.e., the duration of their continuance—they are acknowledging what—i.e., that which—the Prophet (peace and salutation be upon him) brought, and are believing in all he said and informed, affirming it, not denying. For in Sahih al-Bukhari from Anas ibn Malik: The Messenger of Allah said: 'Whoever prays our prayer, faces our qibla, and eats our slaughtered meat, then that is the Muslim who has the protection of Allah and the protection of His Messenger, so do not violate Allah's protection concerning him.' And in it from Anas: The Messenger of Allah said: 'I have been commanded to fight people until they say: There is no god but Allah. When they say it, pray our prayer, face our qibla, and slaughter our slaughter, then their blood and wealth are forbidden to us except by its right, and their account is with Allah.'
Source pages p. 119

Commentary
This passage is a combination of creedal affirmations and a ruling on the identity of fellow Muslims. It begins with the affirmation of belief in angels, prophets, and revealed books, testifying that all the prophets were upon clear truth and were protected from anything that diminishes their rank. Then it addresses the naming of the people of our qibla—those who share our testimony, direction of prayer, prayer, and slaughtered meat—as Muslims and believers, even if they commit major sins, as long as they acknowledge and affirm all that the Prophet brought. The passage then cites two hadith from Sahih al-Bukhari that define the Muslim by outward actions and establish inviolability of life and property. The overall argument establishes a clear criterion for identifying Muslims without delving into their inner state.

Key Terms
الملائكة
النبيين
الكتب المنزلة
المرسلين
الحق المبين
معصومين

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think prophets are not protected from minor errors or that their rank can be diminished by human weaknesses.
Correction: The text explicitly states they are protected from everything that leads to deficiency in their lofty ranks, affirming the doctrine of ʿiṣmah.

Checkpoint
What does the text say about the prophets and messengers regarding their rank?
A) They are ordinary humans with no special protection.
B) They are protected from everything that leads to deficiency in their lofty ranks.
C) They only conveyed part of the message and could err.
D) They were not all upon clear truth.

Key Takeaway
The prophets and messengers were upon clear truth and protected from anything that would lessen their lofty status.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly believe that the prophets and angels were upon clear truth, even when societal pressures or your own desires contradict their message? What would change in your daily decisions if you internalized this certainty?
?
When you hear the Prophet's teachings, do you accept all of them without denying any part, or do you selectively choose what fits your lifestyle? This lesson calls you to be a 'true believer' who acknowledges everything he brought. Are you?
?
The prophets are protected from anything that diminishes their rank. How does this affect your trust in the Quran and Sunnah as preserved guidance? If you have any doubts, what action will you take to remove them starting today?

The Ruling on Calling Ahl al-Qibla Muslims and Believers
States the ruling on calling ahl al-qibla Muslims and believers despite major sins, with hadith evidence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Sunni position that Muslims who commit major sins remain believers as long as they acknowledge the truth brought by the Prophet, and how outward signs of Islam define membership in the community.

Core Idea
Major sins do not remove one from faith; outward Islamic practice defines the community.

This lesson addresses a crucial question: Can a person who commits major sins still be called a believer? The text affirms that as long as a person acknowledges and affirms everything the Prophet brought, they are named Muslims and believers, even if they are sinful. The passage then supports this with two hadith from Sahih al-Bukhari that define a Muslim by visible acts: praying towards the qibla, eating slaughtered meat, and reciting the shahada.

Guided Path
1
Read the extended ruling
Read the Arabic passage for the ruling carefully. Notice its structure: a statement of principle followed by hadith evidence.
2
Identify the conditions for being called Muslim
The text lists outward actions: bearing witness to the shahada, facing the qibla, praying, and eating slaughtered meat.
These are the minimum outward signs of Islamic identity.
3
Understand the role of major sins
The text explicitly says 'even if they are described as committing major sins and are sinful' — they are still called Muslims and believers.
This refutes the Kharijite view that major sins nullify faith.
4
Examine the hadith evidence
Read the two hadith. The first defines a Muslim by outward acts; the second links those acts to protection of life and property.
Both hadith are from Sahih al-Bukhari.

وَنُؤْمِنُ بِالمَلائِكَةِ وَالنَّبِيِّينَ وَالكُتُبِ المُنَزَّلَةِ عَلَى الْمُرْسَلِينَ، وَنَشْهَدُ أَنَّهُمْ كَانُوا عَلَى الحَقِّ المُبِينِ، وَنُسَمِّي أَهْلَ قِبْلَتِنَا مُسْلِمِينَ مُؤْمِنِينَ مَا دَامُوا بِمَا جَاءَ بِهِ النَّبِيُّ عَلَيهِ الصَّلَاةُ وَالسَّلَامُ مُعْتَرِفِينَ وَلَهُ بِكُلِّ مَا قَالَ وَأَخْبَرَ مُصَدِّقِينَ غَيْرَ مُكَذِّبِينَ. ونؤمن بالملائكة المكرمين وبجميع النبيين والمرسلين وبجميع الكتب المنزلة على الأنبياء المرسلين صلوات الله وسلامه عليهم أجمعين ونشهد أنهم كلهم كانوا على الحق المبين، وعن جميع ما يؤدي إلى نقص مراتبهم العلية معصومين. ونسمي أهل قبلتنا وهم الذين شهدوا شهادتنا واستقبلوا قبلتنا وصلوا صلاتنا وأكلوا ذبيحتنا مسلمين ومؤمنين وإن وصفوا بارتكاب الكبائر فاسقين ما داموا أي مدة دوامهم بما أي بالذي جاء به النبي عليه الصلاة والسلام معترفين وله بكل ما قال وأخبر به مصدقين جازمين به غير مكذبين؛ ففي صحيح البخاري عن أنس بن مالك قال: قال رسول الله : مَنْ صَلَّى صَلَاتَنَا وَاسْتَقْبَلَ قِبْلَتَنَا وَأَكَلَ ذَبِيحَتَنَا فَذَلِكَ المُسْلِمُ الَّذِي لَهُ ذِمَّةُ الله وَذِمَّةٌ رَسُولِهِ فَلَا تُخْفِرُوا الله في ذِمَّتِهِ، وفيه عن أنس قال: قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم: أُمِرْتُ أَنْ أُقَاتِلَ النَّاسَ حَتَّى يَقُولُوا: لَا إِلَهَ إِلَّا اللهُ فَإِذَا قَالُوهَا وَصَلُّوا صَلَاتَنَا وَاسْتَقْبَلُوا قِبْلَتَنَا وَذَبَحُوا ذَبِيحَتَنَا فَقَدْ حَرَّمَتْ عَلَيْنَا دِمَاؤُهُم وَأَمْوَالَهُم إِلَّا بِحَقِّهَا وَحِسَابُهُم عَلَى الله.
We believe in the angels, and the prophets, and the books revealed to the messengers, and we testify that they were upon clear truth, and we name the people of our qibla as Muslims and believers as long as they are acknowledging what the Prophet (peace and salutation be upon him) brought and are believing in all he said and informed, not denying. And we believe in the honored angels, and all the prophets and messengers, and all the books revealed to the prophets, the messengers, may the blessings of Allah and His peace be upon them all, and we testify that all of them were upon clear truth, and they are protected from everything that leads to deficiency in their lofty ranks. And we name the people of our qibla—those who bear witness to our testimony, face our qibla, pray our prayer, and eat our slaughtered meat—as Muslims and believers, even if they are described as committing major sins and are sinful, as long as—i.e., the duration of their continuance—they are acknowledging what—i.e., that which—the Prophet (peace and salutation be upon him) brought, and are believing in all he said and informed, affirming it, not denying. For in Sahih al-Bukhari from Anas ibn Malik: The Messenger of Allah said: 'Whoever prays our prayer, faces our qibla, and eats our slaughtered meat, then that is the Muslim who has the protection of Allah and the protection of His Messenger, so do not violate Allah's protection concerning him.' And in it from Anas: The Messenger of Allah said: 'I have been commanded to fight people until they say: There is no god but Allah. When they say it, pray our prayer, face our qibla, and slaughter our slaughter, then their blood and wealth are forbidden to us except by its right, and their account is with Allah.'
