The Two Pillars of Iman: Tasdiq and Iqrar
The commentator distinguishes the two pillars of iman and the waiving of iqrar.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the distinct roles of tasdiq (internal assent) and iqrar (verbal declaration) as pillars of iman, and the conditions under which iqrar may be waived.

Core Idea
Tasdiq is essential; iqrar may be dropped in coercion or incapacity.

Before exploring the many schools' definitions of iman, Imam al-Tahawi's commentator establishes a foundational principle: iman consists of two pillars, but they are not equal in their necessity. Tasdiq is non-negotiable, while iqrar can be waived under duress or inability. This lesson explains that key distinction.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic and translation
Read the short passage once to grasp the basic statement.
2
Identify the two pillars
Note that both tasdiq and iqrar are called pillars, but with different rules.
3
Understand the exception
Consider why iqrar can be dropped in cases of ikrah (coercion) and 'ajz (incapacity). This is important for understanding later discussions on the status of the coerced believer.
This exception shows the priority of internal belief over external expression.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَاعْلَمْ أَنَّ كُلًّا مِنْهُمَا رُكْنٌ إِلَّا أَنَّ التَّصْدِيقَ رُكْنٌ لَا يَحْتَمِلُ السُّقُوطَ أَصْلًا وَالِإقْرَارُ قَدْ يَحْتَمِلُهُ كَمَا فِي حَالَةِ الْإِكْرَاهِ وَالْعَجْزِ، وَفِي الْمُسَايَرَةِ فِي أَوَّلِ الْخَاتِمَةِ فِي بَحْثِ الْإيمَانِ وَمَفْهُومِهِ فَقِيلَ : هُوَ التَّصْدِيقُ بِالْقَلْبِ فَقَطْ، وَهُوَ الْمُخْتَارُ عِنْدَ جُمْهُورِ الْأَشَاعِرَةِ، أَوْ مَعَ الطَّاعَةِ، وَهُوَ قَوْلُ الْخَوَارِجِ؛ وَلِذَا كَفَّرُوا بِالذَّنْبِ لِانْتِقَاءِ جُزْءِ الْمَاهِيَّةِ، أَوْ بِاللِّسَانِ فَقَطْ وَهُوَ قَوْلُ الْكَرَّامِيَّةِ؛ فَإِنْ طَابَقَ تَصْدِيقَ الْقَلْبِ فَهُوَ مُؤْمِنٌ نَاجٍ وَإِلَّا فَهُوَ مُؤْمِنٌ مُخَلَّدٌ فِي النَّارِ، أَوْ بِالْقَلْبِ وَاللِّسَانِ وَهُوَ مَنْقُولٌ عَنْ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ وَمَشْهُورٌ عَنْ أَصْحَابِهِ، وَبَعْضُ الْمُحَقِّقِينَ مِنَ الْأَشَاعِرَةِ قَالُوا: لَمَّا كَانَ الْإيمَانُ التَّصْدِيقَ، وَالتَّصْدِيقُ كَمَا يَكُونُ بِالْقَلْبِ يَكُونُ بِاللِّسَانِ فَيَكُونُ كُلٌّ مِنْهُمَا رُكْنًا فِي الْبَابِ فَلَا يَثْبُتُ الْإيمَانُ إِلَّا بِهِمَا إِلَّا عِنْدَ الْعَجْزِ، وَكَذَا الِاحْتِيَاطُ وَاقِعٌ عَلَيْهِ وَالنُّصُوصُ دَالَّةٌ عَلَيْهِ، وَذَكَرُوا مَا تَعَلَّقَتْ بِهِ؛ يَعْنِي الْكَرَّامِيَّةَ؛ يَعْنِي مِنْ نَحْوِ قَوْلِهِ عَلَيْهِ الصَّلَاةُ وَالسَّلَامُ: «أُمِرْتُ أَنْ أُقَاتِلَ النَّاسَ حَتَّى يَقُولُوا لَا إِلَهَ إِلَّا اللَّهُ» (1)، وَمِنْ قَوْلِهِ تَعَالَى: (مَن كَفَرَ بِاللهِ مِنْ بَعْدِ إِيمَنِهِ إِلَّا مَنْ أُكْرةَ .... الآية [سورة النحل آية: ١٠٦] جَعَلَ الْمُتَكَلِّمَ كَافِرًا مَعَ أَنَّ قَلْبَهُ مُطْمَئِنٌّ بِالْإيمَانِ وَلَكِنْ عُفِيَ عَنْهُ، وَإِذَا كَانَ كَافِرًا بِاعْتِبَارِ اللِّسَانِ يَكُونُ مُؤْمِنًا بِاعْتِبَارِهِ لِاتِّحَادِ مَوْرِدِ الْإيمَانِ وَالْكُفْرِ، وَصَرَّحَ فِي الْآيَةِ بِإِثْبَاتِ الْإيمَانِ لِلْقَلْبِ وَالْكُفْرِ أَيْضًا لَهُ بِقَوْلِهِ: (وَقَلْبُهُ مُطْمَيِنَ بِالْإِيمَنِ وَلَكِن مِّن شَرَحَ بِالْكُفْرِ صَدْرًا) [سورة النحل آية: ١٠٦] وَهُوَ مَحَلُّ اتِّفَاقٍ بَيْنَ الْفَرِيقَيْنِ؛ فَوَجَبَ كَوْنُ الْإيمَانِ بِهِمَا وَهُوَ الِاحْتِيَاطُ
Know that each of the two is a pillar, except that tasdiq is a pillar that cannot be dropped at all, while iqrar may be dropped, as in a state of coercion or incapacity. In al-Musayara at the beginning of the epilogue in the discussion of iman and its meaning, it was said: it is tasdiq by the heart alone, and this is the chosen opinion according to the majority of the Ash'aris; or with obedience, and that is the saying of the Khawarij, which is why they declare the sinner a disbeliever because part of the essence is missing; or by the tongue alone, and that is the saying of the Karamiyya; if it matches the tasdiq of the heart, then he is a successful believer, otherwise he is a believer eternally in the Fire; or by the heart and the tongue, and that is reported from Abu Hanifa and well-known from his companions. And some of the verifying scholars from the Ash'aris said: Since iman is tasdiq, and tasdiq can be by the heart as it can be by the tongue, each of them is a pillar in the matter, so iman is not established except by both, except in the case of incapacity; and caution requires this, and the texts indicate it. They mentioned what the Karamiyya relied upon, like his saying, peace be upon him: 'I have been commanded to fight people until they say la ilaha illa Allah,' and His saying, exalted be He: 'Whoever disbelieves in Allah after his iman, except one who is compelled ...' [Surah al-Nahl 16:106]. He made the speaker a disbeliever even though his heart was reassured with iman, but he was excused. And if he is a disbeliever in terms of the tongue, he is a believer in terms of it, because the locus of iman and kufr is one. And the verse explicitly affirms iman for the heart and also kufr for it in His saying: 'his heart is reassured with iman, but whoever opens his breast to kufr' [Surah al-Nahl 16:106]. This is a point of agreement between the two groups; so it is necessary that iman is by both, and that is the cautionary position.
Source pages p. 126

Commentary
This passage discusses the two pillars of iman and the scholarly differences on its definition. It begins by stating that both iqrar and tasdiq are pillars, but tasdiq cannot be waived, while iqrar can be waived in cases of coercion or incapacity. Then it references al-Musayara, summarizing the various positions: the Ash'ari view (tasdiq by heart only), the Kharijite view (tasdiq plus obedience), the Karamiyya view (iqrar only), and the Hanafi view (heart and tongue). Some Ash'ari scholars argue that since tasdiq can be by tongue as well, both are needed except when one is unable (e.g., mute). They support this with caution and textual evidence, specifically the hadith about fighting until people say the shahada, and the Quranic verse about coercion (16:106). In that verse, a person who utters kufr under coercion is considered a disbeliever in terms of the tongue, even if the heart is firm, but is excused. The verse explicitly mentions both heart (iman) and breast (kufr), and both groups agree on the implication that iman must involve both heart and tongue as a cautionary measure.

Key Terms
ركن
إكراه
عجز

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, under what circumstances may iqrar be waived?
A) When one is ignorant
B) In cases of coercion or incapacity
C) When one commits a major sin
D) Never

Key Takeaway
Iman comprises two pillars, but tasdiq is irreducible while iqrar may be excused under coercion or incapacity.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever feared that outward denial, even under extreme pressure, would invalidate your iman? What does this lesson reveal about the safety of your inner conviction? How can you build a tasdiq so strong that no worldly power can shake it?
?
Are you more concerned with people's perception of your faith than with your inner certainty before Allah? How does the irreducibility of tasdiq challenge you to prioritize what truly matters?
?
If you were placed in a situation of coercion tomorrow, would your tasdiq remain firm? What practical step can you take today to fortify your heart so that no trial can uproot your belief?

Schools' Definitions of Iman: Heart, Tongue, and Actions
The commentator enumerates four theological definitions of iman.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to differentiate the four main schools' definitions of iman: Ash'ari (heart alone), Khawarij (heart+actions), Karamiyya (tongue alone), and Hanafi (heart+tongue).

Core Idea
Scholars disagree on iman's essence: is it only internal, only external, or both?

Having established the two pillars, the commentator now presents the major theological positions on iman's definition. Quoting from al-Musayara, he lists four views: the Ash'ari (heart only), Khawarij (heart plus deeds), Karamiyya (tongue only), and Hanafi (heart and tongue). This lesson surveys these definitions and their implications.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation, noting the four definitions as they appear.
2
List each view
Identify each school and their essential element: heart alone, heart with obedience, tongue alone, or both heart and tongue.
3
Consider the Ash'ari addition
Notice that some verifying Ash'aris argue that tasdiq can be by tongue too, so both are needed unless inability.
4
Reflect on the implications
Think about how each definition affects rulings on who is a believer (e.g., Khawarij excommunicating sinners).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That all schools agree iman is only tasdiq (heart).
Correction: In fact, many schools require both heart and tongue, and the Khawarij require actions. The hadith and Quranic verse prove the importance of verbal utterance.

Checkpoint

B) Hypocrite

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

?

Textual Evidence for Iman by Heart and Tongue
The commentator provides textual proofs for iman requiring both heart and tongue.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Quranic verse on coercion (16:106) and the hadith about fighting until shahada support the necessity of both tasdiq and iqrar for iman.

Core Idea
The Quran and Sunnah show that verbal declaration with the heart is the cautious standard.

The commentator now brings the textual proof that both heart and tongue are required for iman. He cites the well-known hadith 'I have been commanded to fight people until they say la ilaha illa Allah' and the Quranic verse about the coerced believer (16:106). These texts demonstrate that even when the heart is firm, uttering kufr makes one a disbeliever in terms of speech—but the excused person is not held accountable. The lesson concludes that caution dictates requiring both.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation, noting the two proofs and the commentator's analysis.
2
Analyze the hadith
The hadith shows that verbal shahada is the criterion for fighting, indicating its importance.
3
Analyze the Quranic verse
The verse explicitly mentions both heart (iman) and breast (kufr), showing that iman involves both.
4
Understand the conclusion
The commentator concludes that both are necessary as a cautious position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَاعْلَمْ أَنَّ كُلًّا مِنْهُمَا رُكْنٌ إِلَّا أَنَّ التَّصْدِيقَ رُكْنٌ لَا يَحْتَمِلُ السُّقُوطَ أَصْلًا وَالِإقْرَارُ قَدْ يَحْتَمِلُهُ كَمَا فِي حَالَةِ الْإِكْرَاهِ وَالْعَجْزِ، وَفِي الْمُسَايَرَةِ فِي أَوَّلِ الْخَاتِمَةِ فِي بَحْثِ الْإيمَانِ وَمَفْهُومِهِ فَقِيلَ : هُوَ التَّصْدِيقُ بِالْقَلْبِ فَقَطْ، وَهُوَ الْمُخْتَارُ عِنْدَ جُمْهُورِ الْأَشَاعِرَةِ، أَوْ مَعَ الطَّاعَةِ، وَهُوَ قَوْلُ الْخَوَارِجِ؛ وَلِذَا كَفَّرُوا بِالذَّنْبِ لِانْتِقَاءِ جُزْءِ الْمَاهِيَّةِ، أَوْ بِاللِّسَانِ فَقَطْ وَهُوَ قَوْلُ الْكَرَّامِيَّةِ؛ فَإِنْ طَابَقَ تَصْدِيقَ الْقَلْبِ فَهُوَ مُؤْمِنٌ نَاجٍ وَإِلَّا فَهُوَ مُؤْمِنٌ مُخَلَّدٌ فِي النَّارِ، أَوْ بِالْقَلْبِ وَاللِّسَانِ وَهُوَ مَنْقُولٌ عَنْ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ وَمَشْهُورٌ عَنْ أَصْحَابِهِ، وَبَعْضُ الْمُحَقِّقِينَ مِنَ الْأَشَاعِرَةِ قَالُوا: لَمَّا كَانَ الْإيمَانُ التَّصْدِيقَ، وَالتَّصْدِيقُ كَمَا يَكُونُ بِالْقَلْبِ يَكُونُ بِاللِّسَانِ فَيَكُونُ كُلٌّ مِنْهُمَا رُكْنًا فِي الْبَابِ فَلَا يَثْبُتُ الْإيمَانُ إِلَّا بِهِمَا إِلَّا عِنْدَ الْعَجْزِ، وَكَذَا الِاحْتِيَاطُ وَاقِعٌ عَلَيْهِ وَالنُّصُوصُ دَالَّةٌ عَلَيْهِ، وَذَكَرُوا مَا تَعَلَّقَتْ بِهِ؛ يَعْنِي الْكَرَّامِيَّةَ؛ يَعْنِي مِنْ نَحْوِ قَوْلِهِ عَلَيْهِ الصَّلَاةُ وَالسَّلَامُ: «أُمِرْتُ أَنْ أُقَاتِلَ النَّاسَ حَتَّى يَقُولُوا لَا إِلَهَ إِلَّا اللَّهُ» (1)، وَمِنْ قَوْلِهِ تَعَالَى: (مَن كَفَرَ بِاللهِ مِنْ بَعْدِ إِيمَنِهِ إِلَّا مَنْ أُكْرةَ .... الآية [سورة النحل آية: ١٠٦] جَعَلَ الْمُتَكَلِّمَ كَافِرًا مَعَ أَنَّ قَلْبَهُ مُطْمَئِنٌّ بِالْإيمَانِ وَلَكِنْ عُفِيَ عَنْهُ، وَإِذَا كَانَ كَافِرًا بِاعْتِبَارِ اللِّسَانِ يَكُونُ مُؤْمِنًا بِاعْتِبَارِهِ لِاتِّحَادِ مَوْرِدِ الْإيمَانِ وَالْكُفْرِ، وَصَرَّحَ فِي الْآيَةِ بِإِثْبَاتِ الْإيمَانِ لِلْقَلْبِ وَالْكُفْرِ أَيْضًا لَهُ بِقَوْلِهِ: (وَقَلْبُهُ مُطْمَيِنَ بِالْإِيمَنِ وَلَكِن مِّن شَرَحَ بِالْكُفْرِ صَدْرًا) [سورة النحل آية: ١٠٦] وَهُوَ مَحَلُّ اتِّفَاقٍ بَيْنَ الْفَرِيقَيْنِ؛ فَوَجَبَ كَوْنُ الْإيمَانِ بِهِمَا وَهُوَ الِاحْتِيَاطُ
Know that each of the two is a pillar, except that tasdiq is a pillar that cannot be dropped at all, while iqrar may be dropped, as in a state of coercion or incapacity. In al-Musayara at the beginning of the epilogue in the discussion of iman and its meaning, it was said: it is tasdiq by the heart alone, and this is the chosen opinion according to the majority of the Ash'aris; or with obedience, and that is the saying of the Khawarij, which is why they declare the sinner a disbeliever because part of the essence is missing; or by the tongue alone, and that is the saying of the Karamiyya; if it matches the tasdiq of the heart, then he is a successful believer, otherwise he is a believer eternally in the Fire; or by the heart and the tongue, and that is reported from Abu Hanifa and well-known from his companions. And some of the verifying scholars from the Ash'aris said: Since iman is tasdiq, and tasdiq can be by the heart as it can be by the tongue, each of them is a pillar in the matter, so iman is not established except by both, except in the case of incapacity; and caution requires this, and the texts indicate it. They mentioned what the Karamiyya relied upon, like his saying, peace be upon him: 'I have been commanded to fight people until they say la ilaha illa Allah,' and His saying, exalted be He: 'Whoever disbelieves in Allah after his iman, except one who is compelled ...' [Surah al-Nahl 16:106]. He made the speaker a disbeliever even though his heart was reassured with iman, but he was excused. And if he is a disbeliever in terms of the tongue, he is a believer in terms of it, because the locus of iman and kufr is one. And the verse explicitly affirms iman for the heart and also kufr for it in His saying: 'his heart is reassured with iman, but whoever opens his breast to kufr' [Surah al-Nahl 16:106]. This is a point of agreement between the two groups; so it is necessary that iman is by both, and that is the cautionary position.
Source pages p. 126

Commentary
This passage discusses the two pillars of iman and the scholarly differences on its definition. It begins by stating that both iqrar and tasdiq are pillars, but tasdiq cannot be waived, while iqrar can be waived in cases of coercion or incapacity. Then it references al-Musayara, summarizing the various positions: the Ash'ari view (tasdiq by heart only), the Kharijite view (tasdiq plus obedience), the Karamiyya view (iqrar only), and the Hanafi view (heart and tongue). Some Ash'ari scholars argue that since tasdiq can be by tongue as well, both are needed except when one is unable (e.g., mute). They support this with caution and textual evidence, specifically the hadith about fighting until people say the shahada, and the Quranic verse about coercion (16:106). In that verse, a person who utters kufr under coercion is considered a disbeliever in terms of the tongue, even if the heart is firm, but is excused. The verse explicitly mentions both heart (iman) and breast (kufr), and both groups agree on the implication that iman must involve both heart and tongue as a cautionary measure.

Key Terms
إكراه
قلب
لسان
احتياط

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what does Quran 16:106 indicate about a person forced to utter kufr?

B) They are excused but considered a disbeliever in terms of the tongue
C) Their iman becomes void
D) They are a hypocrite

Key Takeaway
The Quranic account of the coerced believer shows that iman involves both heart and tongue, making the cautious position of requiring both the most sound.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

The Hanafi View: Iman as Tasdiq and the Role of Iqrar
Hanafi view on iman as tasdiq and iqrar as condition for rulings.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Hanafi position that iman is tasdiq in the heart, and that iqrar is a condition for worldly rulings, not a component of iman itself.

Core Idea
Iman is inner belief; iqrar is for worldly status, not for salvation.

The Hanafi school, echoed by the Ash'aris, defines iman as heartfelt affirmation (tasdiq). However, for purposes of applying Islamic rulings in this life, verbal confession (iqrar) is required. This passage clarifies that view and explains the nuanced stance on obstinate refusal.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Notice the key terms: tasdiq, iqrar, and kufr 'inad.
The passage contains a nuanced argument about the role of iqrar.
2
Identify the Hanafi definition of iman
The passage states that according to the author of al-Umda (the Hanafi view), iman is tasdiq. Find where this is stated and note that iqrar is not part of iman itself.
3
Understand the condition of iqrar
The passage explains that iqrar is a condition for applying worldly rulings. Identify what these rulings include (prayer behind him, burial, etc.) and note that this view matches the Ash'ari chosen opinion.
4
Examine the agreement on kufr 'inad
Even those who do not require iqrar for iman agree that if a person is asked to affirm and refuses out of obstinacy, that refusal is kufr. Note that abandoning obstinacy is a condition.
This shows that iqrar is not irrelevant; it has a conditional role.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إِلَّا أَنَّ قَوْلَ صَاحِبِ الْعُمْدَةِ (۲) مِنْهُمْ - يَعْنِي الْحَنَفِيَّةَ: الْإيمَانُ هُوَ التَّصْدِيقُ؛ فَمَنْ صَدَّقَ الرَّسُولَ فِيمَا جَاءَ بِهِ فَهُوَ مُؤْمِنٌ بَيْنَهُ وَبَيْنَ اللَّهِ تَعَالَى، وَالْإقْرَارُ شَرْطُ إِجْرَاءِ الْأَحْكَامِ هُوَ بِعَيْنِهِ الْقَوْلُ الْمُخْتَارُ عِنْدَ الْأَشَاعِرَةِ، وَالْمُرَادُ (۳) أَحْكَامُ الدُّنْيَا (٤) مِنَ الصَّلَاةِ خَلْفَهُ وَعَلَيْهِ وَدَفْنِهِ فِي مَقَابِرِ الْمُسْلِمِينَ وَغَيْرِ ذَلِكَ، وَاتَّفَقَ الْقَائِلُونَ بِعَدَمِ اعْتِبَارِ الْإقْرَارِ عَلَى أَنْ يَعْتَقِدَ (ه) أَنَّهُ مَتَى طُولِبَ بِهِ أَتَى بِهِ ؛ فَإِنْ طُولِبَ بِهِ فَلَمْ يُقِرَّ فَهُوَ كُفْرُ عِنَادٍ، وَهَذَا مَا قَالُوا: إِنَّ تَرْكَ الْعِنَادِ شَرْطٌ، وَفَسَّرُوهُ بِهِ، وَبِالْجُمْلَةِ فَقَدْ ضُمَّ إِلَى التَّصْدِيقِ بِالْقَلْبِ أَوْ بِهِمَا فِي تَحَقُّقِ الْإيمَانِ وَإِثْبَاتِهِ أُمُورٌ الْإخْلَالُ بِهَا إخْلَالٌ بِالْإيمَانِ اتِّفَاقًا؛ كَتَرْكِ السُّجُودِ لِلصَّنَمِ وَكَقَتْلِ نَبِيٍّ أَوِ الِاسْتِخْفَافِ بِهِ أَوْ بِالْمُصْحَفِ وَالْكَعْبَةِ، وَكَذَا مُخَالَفَةُ مَا أُجْمِعَ عَلَيْهِ وَإِنْكَارُهُ بَعْدَ الْعِلْمِ بِهِ؛ قَالَ الْإمَامُ أَبُو الْقَاسِمِ الْإسْفَرَايِينِي (٦) بَعْدَ ذِكْرِهَا : إِذَا وُجِدَ ذَلِكَ دَلَّنَا عَلَى أَنَّ التَّصْدِيقَ الَّذِي يَكُونُ فِي الْقَلْبِ لَيْسَ بِصَحِيحٍ
Except that the statement of the author of al-Umda (2) among them - meaning the Hanafis: iman is tasdiq; whoever believes in the Messenger regarding what he brought is a believer between him and Allah, exalted be He, and iqrar is a condition for the application of rulings, and this is exactly the chosen opinion according to the Ash'aris. What is meant (3) is the rulings of this world (4), such as performing prayer behind him and over him, burying him in Muslim cemeteries, and other matters. And those who hold that iqrar is not a condition agreed that he must believe (5) that whenever he is required to do so, he will do it; if he is required and does not affirm, then it is kufr of obstinacy. This is what they said: that abandoning obstinacy is a condition, and they interpreted it accordingly. In summary, to the tasdiq of the heart or to both [heart and tongue] in the realization and confirmation of iman, there are added matters, the violation of which is a violation of iman by consensus, such as leaving prostration to an idol, killing a prophet, or showing disrespect to him, or to the Mus'haf, or to the Ka'bah, as well as opposing what is agreed upon by consensus and denying it after knowing it. Imam Abu al-Qasim al-Isfarayini (6) said after mentioning these: 'If that is found, it indicates to us that the tasdiq that is in the heart is not sound.'
Source pages p. 127

Commentary
This passage continues the discussion of iman by presenting the Hanafi view as represented by the author of al-Umda (Abu al-Mu'in al-Nasafi). According to him, iman is essentially tasdiq (belief in the heart), and iqrar is a condition for the application of worldly rulings, not a component of iman itself. This is the same view chosen by the Ash'aris. The worldly rulings include praying behind a person, praying over him, burying him in Muslim cemeteries, etc. Those who do not consider iqrar a necessary component of iman still agree that if a person is required to affirm and refuses out of obstinacy, that refusal is kufr of obstinacy. Thus, abandoning obstinacy is a condition for soundness of iman. Finally, the passage lists external actions that, by consensus, violate iman: prostrating to an idol, killing a prophet, disrespecting a prophet, the Qur'an, or the Ka'bah, or opposing and denying matters of consensus after knowing them. Imam al-Isfarayini states that the presence of such actions indicates that the heart's tasdiq is not genuine.

Key Terms
التَّصْدِيقُ
الإقْرَارُ
شَرْطُ إِجْرَاءِ الْأَحْكَامِ
كُفْرُ عِنَادٍ
الْحَنَفِيَّة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think iqrar is irrelevant for iman and can be omitted without consequence.
Correction: Iqrar is a condition for worldly rulings, and obstinate refusal to affirm is kufr 'inad.

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi view presented, what is the role of iqrar?
A) It is a component of iman
B) It is a condition for the application of worldly rulings
C) It is unnecessary and has no effect
D) It is required only for the afterlife

Key Takeaway
For the Hanafis, iman is heartfelt belief, but verbal affirmation (iqrar) is required for the application of Islamic rulings in this world, and obstinate refusal to affirm is considered disbelief.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You claim to have iman in your heart, but do you live as though your iqrar matters? If you were put in a situation where denying your faith would save your life, would your tongue reflect what is in your heart? This lesson forces you to consider the seriousness of obstinate refusal. Are you prepared for such a test?
?
The passage stipulates that if you are required to affirm and you refuse out of obstinacy, it becomes kufr. Have you ever, even in a small way, felt too proud to declare your faith? Reflect on a moment when your inner belief did not match your outward expression—what does that reveal about the state of your iman?
?
The Hanafis teach that iman is tasdiq alone, yet they still require iqrar for worldly rulings. Do you cherish your iqrar as part of your Muslim identity in this world, or do you take it for granted? What concrete step will you take today to consciously affirm your belief in public, even if only in your home or with a friend?

Actions Indicating False Tasdiq
Lists actions that violate iman by consensus and concludes they indicate unsound tasdiq.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that certain external actions, by consensus, show that a person's inner belief (tasdiq) is not genuine, as explained by Imam al-Isfarayini.

Core Idea
Outward violations reveal an unsound heart.

After establishing the Hanafi view, the commentator adds that certain actions are universally considered violations of iman. These actions, if committed, indicate that the person's tasdiq is not sound. Imam al-Isfarayini's statement summarizes this principle.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify the actions listed
Read the Arabic and translation, focusing on the actions mentioned: prostrating to an idol, killing a prophet, disrespecting the Prophet, the Mus'haf, or the Ka'bah, and opposing or denying consensus.
These are all major violations, not minor sins.
2
Understand the consensus
The passage says that violating these matters is 'a violation of iman by consensus'. Reflect on the weight of this statement.
Consensus (ijma') is a strong evidence in Islamic law.
3
Analyze al-Isfarayini's conclusion
Imam al-Isfarayini states that if these actions occur, they indicate that the tasdiq in the heart is not sound. This is the key point: external actions reveal inner reality.
The passage uses this as a proof that tasdiq without external compliance is not genuine.

إِلَّا أَنَّ قَوْلَ صَاحِبِ الْعُمْدَةِ (۲) مِنْهُمْ - يَعْنِي الْحَنَفِيَّةَ: الْإيمَانُ هُوَ التَّصْدِيقُ؛ فَمَنْ صَدَّقَ الرَّسُولَ فِيمَا جَاءَ بِهِ فَهُوَ مُؤْمِنٌ بَيْنَهُ وَبَيْنَ اللَّهِ تَعَالَى، وَالْإقْرَارُ شَرْطُ إِجْرَاءِ الْأَحْكَامِ هُوَ بِعَيْنِهِ الْقَوْلُ الْمُخْتَارُ عِنْدَ الْأَشَاعِرَةِ، وَالْمُرَادُ (۳) أَحْكَامُ الدُّنْيَا (٤) مِنَ الصَّلَاةِ خَلْفَهُ وَعَلَيْهِ وَدَفْنِهِ فِي مَقَابِرِ الْمُسْلِمِينَ وَغَيْرِ ذَلِكَ، وَاتَّفَقَ الْقَائِلُونَ بِعَدَمِ اعْتِبَارِ الْإقْرَارِ عَلَى أَنْ يَعْتَقِدَ (ه) أَنَّهُ مَتَى طُولِبَ بِهِ أَتَى بِهِ ؛ فَإِنْ طُولِبَ بِهِ فَلَمْ يُقِرَّ فَهُوَ كُفْرُ عِنَادٍ، وَهَذَا مَا قَالُوا: إِنَّ تَرْكَ الْعِنَادِ شَرْطٌ، وَفَسَّرُوهُ بِهِ، وَبِالْجُمْلَةِ فَقَدْ ضُمَّ إِلَى التَّصْدِيقِ بِالْقَلْبِ أَوْ بِهِمَا فِي تَحَقُّقِ الْإيمَانِ وَإِثْبَاتِهِ أُمُورٌ الْإخْلَالُ بِهَا إخْلَالٌ بِالْإيمَانِ اتِّفَاقًا؛ كَتَرْكِ السُّجُودِ لِلصَّنَمِ وَكَقَتْلِ نَبِيٍّ أَوِ الِاسْتِخْفَافِ بِهِ أَوْ بِالْمُصْحَفِ وَالْكَعْبَةِ، وَكَذَا مُخَالَفَةُ مَا أُجْمِعَ عَلَيْهِ وَإِنْكَارُهُ بَعْدَ الْعِلْمِ بِهِ؛ قَالَ الْإمَامُ أَبُو الْقَاسِمِ الْإسْفَرَايِينِي (٦) بَعْدَ ذِكْرِهَا : إِذَا وُجِدَ ذَلِكَ دَلَّنَا عَلَى أَنَّ التَّصْدِيقَ الَّذِي يَكُونُ فِي الْقَلْبِ لَيْسَ بِصَحِيحٍ
Except that the statement of the author of al-Umda (2) among them - meaning the Hanafis: iman is tasdiq; whoever believes in the Messenger regarding what he brought is a believer between him and Allah, exalted be He, and iqrar is a condition for the application of rulings, and this is exactly the chosen opinion according to the Ash'aris. What is meant (3) is the rulings of this world (4), such as performing prayer behind him and over him, burying him in Muslim cemeteries, and other matters. And those who hold that iqrar is not a condition agreed that he must believe (5) that whenever he is required to do so, he will do it; if he is required and does not affirm, then it is kufr of obstinacy. This is what they said: that abandoning obstinacy is a condition, and they interpreted it accordingly. In summary, to the tasdiq of the heart or to both [heart and tongue] in the realization and confirmation of iman, there are added matters, the violation of which is a violation of iman by consensus, such as leaving prostration to an idol, killing a prophet, or showing disrespect to him, or to the Mus'haf, or to the Ka'bah, as well as opposing what is agreed upon by consensus and denying it after knowing it. Imam Abu al-Qasim al-Isfarayini (6) said after mentioning these: 'If that is found, it indicates to us that the tasdiq that is in the heart is not sound.'
Source pages p. 127

Commentary
This passage continues the discussion of iman by presenting the Hanafi view as represented by the author of al-Umda (Abu al-Mu'in al-Nasafi). According to him, iman is essentially tasdiq (belief in the heart), and iqrar is a condition for the application of worldly rulings, not a component of iman itself. This is the same view chosen by the Ash'aris. The worldly rulings include praying behind a person, praying over him, burying him in Muslim cemeteries, etc. Those who do not consider iqrar a necessary component of iman still agree that if a person is required to affirm and refuses out of obstinacy, that refusal is kufr of obstinacy. Thus, abandoning obstinacy is a condition for soundness of iman. Finally, the passage lists external actions that, by consensus, violate iman: prostrating to an idol, killing a prophet, disrespecting a prophet, the Qur'an, or the Ka'bah, or opposing and denying matters of consensus after knowing them. Imam al-Isfarayini states that the presence of such actions indicates that the heart's tasdiq is not genuine.

Key Terms
التَّصْدِيقُ
إجْمَاع
السُّجُودُ لِلصَّنَمِ
تَرْكِ السُّجُودِ
مُخَالَفَةُ مَا أُجْمِعَ عَلَيْهِ

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that external actions do not reflect inner faith; a person can have true iman while committing major sins without it affecting the heart's belief.
Correction: The passage states that certain actions, by consensus, indicate that the heart's tasdiq is not sound.

Checkpoint
What did Imam al-Isfarayini say about the presence of actions like prostrating to an idol in a person?
A) It shows he is still a believer in his heart
B) It indicates his heart's tasdiq is not sound
C) It is excused if done under coercion
D) It is a minor sin that does not affect iman

Key Takeaway
Certain actions, by consensus, invalidate the claim of genuine belief because they indicate the heart's tasdiq is not sound.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever caught yourself belittling a command of Allah that the scholars agree upon? What does this passage say about the state of your heart when you do that? Will you repent and correct your heart today?
?
Imagine you saw someone prostrating to an idol. Would you consider them a believer? Why? Now apply that same standard to your own life: is there any action you excuse in yourself that this passage would call a sign of unsound tasdiq?
?
This lesson says that violating matters of consensus indicates unsound tasdiq. Is there any matter of consensus you have knowingly opposed? If so, what does your heart need to change so that your actions align with genuine belief?

Definition of Iman: Tasdiq and Iqrar
Maydani defines iman as tasdiq and clarifies iqrar's role.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the nuanced relationship between inner affirmation (tasdiq) and verbal confession (iqrar) in the definition of iman, and how both Ash'ari and Hanafi schools converge on this issue.

Core Idea
Iman is primarily inner affirmation; verbal confession is a condition for worldly rulings.

This lesson examines a key passage from Imam Maydani's commentary on the Tahawiyyah, where he clarifies the definition of iman (faith) in light of the Quranic verse on coerced disbelief. The discussion centers on the roles of tasdiq (heartfelt affirmation) and iqrar (verbal profession), and how the Hanafi and Ash'ari schools, despite apparent differences, reach a common understanding. By engaging with this text, you will appreciate the precision of classical kalam reasoning about faith.

Guided Path
1
Read the Quranic evidence
Start by reading the verse cited (Nahl 106) and Maydani's commentary on how the coerced person is considered a disbeliever by tongue but believer by heart.
This sets the foundation for the distinction between inner and outer.
2
Compare the Hanafi and Ash'ari positions
Notice how Maydani presents the Hanafi view (iman = tasdiq, iqrar = condition for rulings) and equates it with the Ash'ari chosen view.
This shows the practical agreement between schools.
3
Understand the 'inad condition
Read about unwavering stubbornness: if someone refuses to confess when demanded, it indicates kufr of stubbornness.
This explains why iqrar is not part of the essence but still necessary in practice.
4
Identify external indicators of kufr
Review the list of actions (idol prostration, killing prophets, etc.) that indicate absence of true tasdiq, as per Imam Isfarayini.
These are signs, not the essence.
5
Synthesize the lesson
Reflect on how the passage maintains a balanced definition of iman that is both inner and outwardly manifest.
This is a key example of Sunni theological methodology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن قوله تعالى: (مَن كَفَرَ بِاللهِ مِنْ بَعْدِ إِيمَانِهِ إِلَّا مَنْ أُكْرِهَ .... الآية [سورة النحل آية: ١٠٦] جعل المتكلم كافرًا مع أن قلبه مطمئن بالإيمان ولكن عفي عنه، وإذا كان كافرًا باعتبار اللسان يكون مؤمنا باعتباره لاتحاد مورد الإيمان والكفر، وصرح في الآية بإثبات الإيمان للقلب والكفر أيضا له بقوله: وَقَلْبُهُ مُطْمَئِنٌ بِالْإِيمَانِ وَلَكِن مَنْ شَرَحَ بِالْكُفْرِ صَدْرًا) [سورة النحل آية: ١٠٦] وهو محل اتفاق بين الفريقين؛ فوجب كون الإيمان بهما وهو الاحتياط، إلا أن قول صاحب العمدة منهم - يعني الحنفية: الإيمان هو التصديق؛ فمن صدق الرسول فيما جاء به فهو مؤمن بينه وبين الله تعالى، والإقرار شرط إجراء الأحكام هو بعينه القول المختار عند الأشاعرة، والمراد أحكام الدنيا من الصلاة خلفه وعليه ودفنه في مقابر المسلمين وغير ذلك، واتفق القائلون بعدم اعتبار الإقرار على أن يعتقد أنه متى طولب به أتى به؛ فإن طولب به فلم يقر فهو كفر عناد، وهذا ما قالوا: إن ترك العناد شرط، وفسروه به، وبالجملة فقد ضُمَّ إلى التصديق بالقلب أو بهما في تحقق الإيمان وإثباته أمور الإخلال بها إخلال بالإيمان اتفاقا؛ كترك السجود للصنم وكقتل نبي أو الاستخفاف به أو بالمصحف والكعبة، وكذا مخالفة ما أجمع عليه وإنكاره بعد العلم به؛ قال الإمام أبو القاسم الإسفراييني بعد ذكرها: إذا وجد ذلك دلنا على أن التصديق الذي هو الإيمان مفقود من قلبه اهـ بحروفه.
And from His saying, the Exalted: (Whoever disbelieves in Allah after his belief – except for one who is compelled ... the verse [Surah An-Nahl, verse 106] – He made the coerced speaker a disbeliever even though his heart is tranquil with faith, but he is pardoned. And if he is a disbeliever by consideration of the tongue, he is a believer by consideration of [the heart] due to the unity of the locus of faith and disbelief. And He explicitly stated in the verse the affirmation of faith for the heart and also disbelief for it by His saying: “while his heart is tranquil with faith, but whoever opens his breast to disbelief” [Surah An-Nahl, verse 106]. And this is a point of agreement between the two groups. So it is necessary that faith be with both [heart and tongue] – that is the precaution. Except that the statement of the author of al-‘Umdah among them – meaning the Hanafis – is: faith is affirmation (tasdiq); whoever affirms the Messenger in what he brought is a believer between himself and Allah the Exalted, and confession (iqrar) is a condition for the execution of rulings. And this is exactly the chosen view of the Ash‘aris. And what is meant is the rulings of this world, such as praying behind him and over him, burying him in Muslim cemeteries, and other matters. And those who say that iqrar is not considered agree that he must believe that when he is demanded [to confess] he will bring it; if he is demanded and does not confess, then it is kufr of stubbornness. And this is what they said: abandoning stubbornness is a condition, and they explained it as such. In summary, there are attached to affirmation by the heart or by both [heart and tongue] in the realization and establishment of faith, matters whose violation is a violation of faith by consensus, such as abandoning prostration to an idol, killing a prophet, belittling him or the mushaf or the Ka‘bah, and likewise opposing that which is agreed upon and denying it after knowledge of it. Imam Abu al-Qasim al-Isfarayini said after mentioning them: 'When that occurs, it indicates to us that the affirmation which is faith is absent from his heart.' End quote, verbatim.
Source pages p. 127

Commentary
This passage is a detailed discussion of the definition of faith (iman) and the roles of inner affirmation (tasdiq) and verbal confession (iqrar). The author begins by citing Surah An-Nahl 106, which deals with a person coerced into uttering disbelief while his heart remains firm in faith. The verse considers the coerced speaker a disbeliever in terms of the tongue's pronouncement, but a believer in the heart, showing that the locus of iman and kufr can differ. The author notes that both Ash‘aris and Hanafis agree on this scenario. Then he presents the Hanafi position as articulated by the author of al-‘Umdah (Abu al-Ma‘in al-Nasafi): iman is solely tasdiq (affirmation in the heart), and iqrar is only a condition for the application of worldly legal rulings (like inheritance, prayer over the deceased, burial in Muslim cemeteries). This, he says, is identical to the chosen view of the Ash‘aris. Next, the author explains that even those who do not include iqrar in the essence of iman require that the believer be willing to confess if called upon; refusal out of stubbornness (‘inad) is considered kufr. Finally, the passage lists actions that are taken as evidence that inner tasdiq is missing, such as idol worship, killing prophets, disrespecting sacred symbols, or denying agreed-upon matters after knowledge. A quote from Abu al-Qasim al-Isfarayini reinforces this: such actions indicate the absence of true iman in the heart.

Key Terms
الإيمان
التصديق
الإقرار
الكفر
الأحكام
العناد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Verbal confession (iqrar) is an essential part of iman without which one is not a believer.
Correction: While verbal confession is required for legal rulings, the essence of iman is inner affirmation (tasdiq); refusal to confess out of stubbornness indicates absence of iman.

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafis as quoted in this passage, what is the definition of iman?
A) Affirmation with the heart and confession with the tongue.
B) Affirmation with the heart only.
C) Confession with the tongue only.
D) Actions of the limbs.

Key Takeaway
Iman is fundamentally tasdiq of the heart; iqrar is necessary for worldly legal rulings and an externally coerced utterance does not negate inner faith.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever verbally expressed something against your faith due to fear or social pressure, while your heart remained firm? How does this lesson's treatment of the coerced speaker give you hope or challenge you to be more courageous? What is one specific situation this week where you can choose to speak your faith even if it costs you?
?
The passage warns that stubborn refusal to confess the truth after being called to it is kufr. Is there any truth about Islam you know in your heart but resist outwardly affirming due to pride or convenience? What step will you take this week to publicly affirm that truth, no matter how small?
?
Consider the external actions listed (idol worship, killing a prophet, belittling sacred symbols) as indicators of absent faith. Are there any actions in your life, even small ones, that betray a weakness in your inner tasdiq? What will you do to realign your actions with your heart's affirmation?

The Unity and Equality of Iman in Essence
The author defines Iman as one and equal in its essence among all believers.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that Iman is one in essence, all believers are equal in that essence, and distinction comes only through taqwa and actions.

Core Idea
Iman is one and equal in its essence; difference lies in piety, not in faith.

This passage from the Sharh al-Tahawiyyah establishes a foundational principle: the essence of Iman is indivisible and the same for all believers. Before we can discuss its increase or decrease, we must understand this unity.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the literal translation to grasp the author's flow.
Notice the repeated emphasis on 'one' and 'equal'.
2
Identify the definition of Iman
The author defines Iman as 'tasdiq baligh hadd al-jazm wa al-idh'ān'. Understand this definition and why it is indivisible.
3
Understand the distinction between essence and actions
The author says all believers are equal in the essence of Iman, but distinguish by taqwa. Ask yourself how this reconciles apparent differences in faith.
This distinction is key to the later debate on increase and decrease.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَالإِيمَانُ وَاحِدٌ وَأَهْلُهُ فِي أَصْلِهِ سَوَاءٌ وَالتَّفَاضُلُ بَيْنَهُمْ بِالتَّقْوَى وَمُخَالَفَةِ الهَوَى. (و) نقول: (الإيمان) وكذلك الإسلام لتلازمهما مفهوما؛ فقد اتفق أهل الحق أنه لا إيمان بلا إسلام وعكسه الجميع الأنام من أهل الأرض والسماء (واحد) لأنه التصديق البالغ حد الجزم والإذعان الذي لا يقبل التشكيك (وأهله) من الملائكة والأنبياء والأولياء وسائر المؤمنين الأبرار والفجار ( في أصله) الذي هو التصديق كلهم فيه (سواء)؛ أي لا تفاضل فيه من حيث ذاته، ولا يزيد ولا ينقص (و) إنما التفاضل بينهم والزيادة والنقص (بالتقوى ومخالفة الهوى) وفي المسايرة: «قال أبو حنيفة وأصحابه: "لا يزيد الإيمان ولا ينقص، واختاره من الأشاعرة إمام الحرمين وكثير، وذهب عامتهم إلى زيادته ونقصانه، قيل: والخلاف مبني على أخذ الطاعات في مفهوم الإيمان وعدمه، فعلى الأول يزيد بزيادتها وينقص بنقصانها، وعلى الثاني لا؛ لأنه اسم للتصديق الجازم مع الإذعان وهذا لا يتغير بضم الطاعات ولا ضم المعاصي وفيه نظر؛ بل قال بزيادته ونقصانه كثير ممن صرح بأنه مجرد التصديق لظواهر؛ كقوله تعالى: (زَادَهُمْ إِيمَنًا) [سورة الأنفال آية: ٢]، وعن ابن عمر قلنا: يا رسول الله: إن الإيمان يزيد وينقص؟ قال: نَعَمْ يَزِيدُ حَتَّى يُدْخِلَ صَاحِبَهُ الجَنَّةَ وَيَنقُصُ حَتَّى يُدْخِلَ صَاحِبَهُ النَّارَ (۱)، وقالوا: لا مانع عقلا من ذلك، بل اليقين الذي هو
And faith is one and its people are in its essence equal, and distinction among them is by piety and opposing desires. And we say: Faith, and likewise Islam due to their mutual entailment in meaning; for the people of truth have agreed that there is no faith without Islam and vice versa, all people of earth and sky. (It is) one because it is the affirmation reaching the level of certainty and submission which does not admit doubt. And its people, from the angels, prophets, saints, and the rest of the believers, both righteous and wicked, in its essence which is the affirmation, all of them are equal in it; i.e., there is no superiority in it in terms of its essence, and it does not increase nor decrease. Rather, distinction among them and the increase and decrease are by piety and opposing desires. And in al-Musayara: 'Abu Hanifa and his companions said: "Faith does not increase nor decrease." And chosen from the Ash'aris by Imam al-Haramayn and many, and the majority of them went to its increase and decrease. It was said: The disagreement is based on including acts of obedience in the concept of faith or not. On the first, it increases with their increase and decreases with their decrease; on the second, no, because it is a name for decisive affirmation with submission, and this does not change with the inclusion of acts of obedience nor with the inclusion of sins. And there is consideration in this; rather, many who stated that it is mere affirmation said it increases and decreases due to apparent evidences, such as His saying the Exalted: (It increased them in faith) [Surah al-Anfal verse 2], and from Ibn 'Umar: We said: O Messenger of Allah, does faith increase and decrease? He said: Yes, it increases until it enters its companion into Paradise, and it decreases until it enters its companion into the Fire. And they said: There is no intellectual impediment to that, rather the certainty which is...'
Source pages p. 129

Commentary
This passage is a doctrinal exposition and a discussion of a debated issue. It begins with the matn's statement that Iman is one and its people are equal in its essence, with distinction only by taqwa and opposing desires. The commentary then explains that Iman and Islam are mutually entailing. It defines Iman as tasdiq (affirmation) that reaches the level of jazm (certainty) and idh'ān (submission), which is not subject to doubt. It then emphasizes that the essence of Iman – this affirmation – is the same for all believers, from angels to prophets to ordinary believers, both righteous and sinful. In its essence, Iman does not increase or decrease. The increase and decrease, along with distinction among people, are due to taqwa (piety) and opposing desires, i.e., actions. The commentary then cites al-Musayara, which presents the debate: Abu Hanifa and his followers hold that Iman does not increase or decrease; this was also chosen by Imam al-Haramayn (al-Juwayni) and many Ash'aris, though the majority of Ash'aris hold that it does. The basis of the disagreement is whether acts of obedience (ta'at) are included in the definition of Iman. If they are, then Iman increases and decreases; if not, it doesn't. The commentary notes that there is consideration (nazar) in this view, and many who define Iman as mere affirmation still affirm increase and decrease based on textual evidences like the verse from Surah al-Anfal and the hadith from Ibn 'Umar. They argue that there is no rational obstacle to Iman increasing or decreasing, and at the point the text cuts off, it is discussing that certainty (yaqin) itself... The passage shows the richness of the debate and that even within the same definition, scholars can differ on whether Iman can increase and decrease.

Key Terms
الإيمان
التصديق
الجزم
الإذعان
التقوى

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that if Iman is one and equal, then all believers are equal in all aspects.
Correction: The author clarifies that distinction is by taqwa and actions, not by the essence of Iman.

Checkpoint
According to this passage, what is the basis for superiority among believers?
A) Their level of Iman
B) Their taqwa and opposing desires
C) Their knowledge
D) Their lineage

Key Takeaway
Iman's essence is one and unchanging; differences among believers are due to piety and actions, not the essence of faith.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If the essence of your iman is the same as that of the greatest prophets and angels, what excuse do you have for your negligence in taqwa and opposing your desires?
?
Knowing that your increase in rank with Allah comes only through taqwa and not through any increase in the essence of iman, how will you change your daily priorities starting today?
?
When you feel spiritually stagnant, do you complain about your iman being weak, or do you honestly examine your taqwa and your struggle against your desires? What will you actually do about it tomorrow?

The Debate on Increase and Decrease of Iman
The author presents the debate on increase and decrease of Iman, citing authorities and evidences.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the classical debate on whether Iman increases and decreases, the key positions, and the basis for disagreement.

Core Idea
The debate on increase/decrease hinges on whether actions are part of Iman's definition.

Having established that Iman's essence is one and does not change, the commentator now delves into a major theological debate: can Iman increase or decrease? This passage presents the views of Abu Hanifa and the Ash'aris, and shows how the disagreement is rooted in the definition of Iman.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage carefully. Notice the citation of al-Musayara and the different scholarly opinions.
The passage is cut off at the end; focus on the presented material.
2
Identify the two positions
Find the position of Abu Hanifa and his followers (no increase/decrease) and that of the majority Ash'aris (increase/decrease). Also note that some Ash'aris agreed with Abu Hanifa.
3
Understand the basis of disagreement
The passage explains that the disagreement is based on whether acts of obedience are part of the definition of Iman. Reflect on why this matters.
This is the core of the lesson.
4
Examine the textual evidences
The passage cites Quran and hadith as evidence for increase and decrease. Notice how even those who define Iman as mere affirmation use these texts.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَالإِيمَانُ وَاحِدٌ وَأَهْلُهُ فِي أَصْلِهِ سَوَاءٌ وَالتَّفَاضُلُ بَيْنَهُمْ بِالتَّقْوَى وَمُخَالَفَةِ الهَوَى. (و) نقول: (الإيمان) وكذلك الإسلام لتلازمهما مفهوما؛ فقد اتفق أهل الحق أنه لا إيمان بلا إسلام وعكسه الجميع الأنام من أهل الأرض والسماء (واحد) لأنه التصديق البالغ حد الجزم والإذعان الذي لا يقبل التشكيك (وأهله) من الملائكة والأنبياء والأولياء وسائر المؤمنين الأبرار والفجار ( في أصله) الذي هو التصديق كلهم فيه (سواء)؛ أي لا تفاضل فيه من حيث ذاته، ولا يزيد ولا ينقص (و) إنما التفاضل بينهم والزيادة والنقص (بالتقوى ومخالفة الهوى) وفي المسايرة: «قال أبو حنيفة وأصحابه: "لا يزيد الإيمان ولا ينقص، واختاره من الأشاعرة إمام الحرمين وكثير، وذهب عامتهم إلى زيادته ونقصانه، قيل: والخلاف مبني على أخذ الطاعات في مفهوم الإيمان وعدمه، فعلى الأول يزيد بزيادتها وينقص بنقصانها، وعلى الثاني لا؛ لأنه اسم للتصديق الجازم مع الإذعان وهذا لا يتغير بضم الطاعات ولا ضم المعاصي وفيه نظر؛ بل قال بزيادته ونقصانه كثير ممن صرح بأنه مجرد التصديق لظواهر؛ كقوله تعالى: (زَادَهُمْ إِيمَنًا) [سورة الأنفال آية: ٢]، وعن ابن عمر قلنا: يا رسول الله: إن الإيمان يزيد وينقص؟ قال: نَعَمْ يَزِيدُ حَتَّى يُدْخِلَ صَاحِبَهُ الجَنَّةَ وَيَنقُصُ حَتَّى يُدْخِلَ صَاحِبَهُ النَّارَ (۱)، وقالوا: لا مانع عقلا من ذلك، بل اليقين الذي هو
And faith is one and its people are in its essence equal, and distinction among them is by piety and opposing desires. And we say: Faith, and likewise Islam due to their mutual entailment in meaning; for the people of truth have agreed that there is no faith without Islam and vice versa, all people of earth and sky. (It is) one because it is the affirmation reaching the level of certainty and submission which does not admit doubt. And its people, from the angels, prophets, saints, and the rest of the believers, both righteous and wicked, in its essence which is the affirmation, all of them are equal in it; i.e., there is no superiority in it in terms of its essence, and it does not increase nor decrease. Rather, distinction among them and the increase and decrease are by piety and opposing desires. And in al-Musayara: 'Abu Hanifa and his companions said: "Faith does not increase nor decrease." And chosen from the Ash'aris by Imam al-Haramayn and many, and the majority of them went to its increase and decrease. It was said: The disagreement is based on including acts of obedience in the concept of faith or not. On the first, it increases with their increase and decreases with their decrease; on the second, no, because it is a name for decisive affirmation with submission, and this does not change with the inclusion of acts of obedience nor with the inclusion of sins. And there is consideration in this; rather, many who stated that it is mere affirmation said it increases and decreases due to apparent evidences, such as His saying the Exalted: (It increased them in faith) [Surah al-Anfal verse 2], and from Ibn 'Umar: We said: O Messenger of Allah, does faith increase and decrease? He said: Yes, it increases until it enters its companion into Paradise, and it decreases until it enters its companion into the Fire. And they said: There is no intellectual impediment to that, rather the certainty which is...'
Source pages p. 129

Commentary
This passage is a doctrinal exposition and a discussion of a debated issue. It begins with the matn's statement that Iman is one and its people are equal in its essence, with distinction only by taqwa and opposing desires. The commentary then explains that Iman and Islam are mutually entailing. It defines Iman as tasdiq (affirmation) that reaches the level of jazm (certainty) and idh'ān (submission), which is not subject to doubt. It then emphasizes that the essence of Iman – this affirmation – is the same for all believers, from angels to prophets to ordinary believers, both righteous and sinful. In its essence, Iman does not increase or decrease. The increase and decrease, along with distinction among people, are due to taqwa (piety) and opposing desires, i.e., actions. The commentary then cites al-Musayara, which presents the debate: Abu Hanifa and his followers hold that Iman does not increase or decrease; this was also chosen by Imam al-Haramayn (al-Juwayni) and many Ash'aris, though the majority of Ash'aris hold that it does. The basis of the disagreement is whether acts of obedience (ta'at) are included in the definition of Iman. If they are, then Iman increases and decreases; if not, it doesn't. The commentary notes that there is consideration (nazar) in this view, and many who define Iman as mere affirmation still affirm increase and decrease based on textual evidences like the verse from Surah al-Anfal and the hadith from Ibn 'Umar. They argue that there is no rational obstacle to Iman increasing or decreasing, and at the point the text cuts off, it is discussing that certainty (yaqin) itself... The passage shows the richness of the debate and that even within the same definition, scholars can differ on whether Iman can increase and decrease.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the debate is purely semantic without practical implications.
Correction: The debate affects how one understands the relationship between faith and actions, and whether Iman can be weakened by sins.

Key Takeaway
The debate on increase/decrease of Iman centers on whether actions are part of its definition; textual evidences suggest that Iman does increase and decrease.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

The source mentions that the debate hinges on whether acts are part of Iman. Consider your own daily actions: do you treat your prayers and good deeds as separate from your faith, or as integral to it? How would your sense of accountability change if you believed every sin directly decreases your Iman? What one sin will you commit to abandoning this week to prevent that decrease?

The Unity and Origin of Faith
Definition and explanation of the nature of iman

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that faith (iman) is a single, unchanging act of certain affirmation, and that all believers are equal in its essence.

Core Idea
Faith is one: a certain affirmation that does not increase or decrease.

Imam Tahawi begins by stating that faith is one and its people are equal in its origin. But what does 'one' mean? Imam Maydani clarifies that faith is the affirmation that reaches certainty and submission, and that this core does not vary among believers. This lesson unpacks that foundational statement.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Start by reading the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice how the matn (bold statement) is followed by the sharh (commentary).
2
Identify the definition of faith
Find where the commentator defines 'one' and what faith is in its essence. Note the terms 'tasdiq', 'jazzm', and 'idh'ān'.
3
Understand equality in origin
The passage says all believers—angels, prophets, saints, righteous and wicked—are equal in the origin of faith. Consider what this means for how we view others.
This does not mean they are equal in rank or piety.
4
Reflect on increase and decrease
The passage explicitly states that faith in its essence does not increase or decrease. Think about why this is important for understanding the nature of iman.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَالإِيمَانُ وَاحِدٌ وَأَهْلُهُ فِي أَصْلِهِ سَوَاءٌ وَالتَّفَاضُلُ بَيْنَهُمْ بِالتَّقْوَى وَمُخَالَفَةِ الهَوَى.
(و) نقول: (الإيمان) وكذلك الإسلام لتلازمهما مفهوما؛ فقد اتفق أهل الحق أنه لا إيمان بلا إسلام وعكسه الجميع الأنام من أهل الأرض والسماء (واحد) لأنه التصديق البالغ حد الجزم والإذعان الذي لا يقبل التشكيك (وأهله) من الملائكة والأنبياء والأولياء وسائر المؤمنين الأبرار والفجار ( في أصله) الذي هو التصديق كلهم فيه (سواء)؛ أي لا تفاضل فيه من حيث ذاته، ولا يزيد ولا ينقص.
Faith is one and its people in its origin are equal, and differentiation among them is by piety and opposing desires. (And) we say: Faith, and likewise Islam due to their inseparability in concept; for the people of truth have agreed that there is no faith without Islam and vice versa all people from the inhabitants of earth and sky. (One) because it is affirmation reaching the limit of certainty and submission that does not accept doubt. (And its people) from the angels, prophets, saints, and all believers, righteous and wicked, (in its origin) which is affirmation, all of them in it are (equal); meaning no differentiation in it from its essence, and it does not increase nor decrease.
Source pages p. 129

Commentary
This passage is a definition and explanation of the nature of iman (faith). It begins by quoting the matn of Imam Tahawi: 'Faith is one and its people in its origin are equal, and differentiation among them is by piety and opposing desires.' The commentator then explains each part. First, he notes that faith and Islam are inseparable in concept. Then he defines 'one' (واحد): faith is the affirmation (tasdiq) that reaches the level of certainty (jazzm) and submission (idh'ān) which does not admit doubt. Next, he explains 'its people' (أهله): all believers, from angels to prophets to saints to ordinary believers, righteous or wicked, are equal in the origin (aṣl) of faith, which is that very affirmation. He emphasizes that in its essence (dhāt), there is no differentiation, no increase, and no decrease. The passage thus establishes that the core of faith is a single, unchanging act of certain affirmation.

Correction: This passage clarifies that faith is a single state of affirmation that does not admit increase or decrease; differences are in taqwa, not in the essence of iman.

The Two Positions on Increase and Decrease of Faith
Maydani presents the two positions on faith's increase and their foundation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two main positions on whether faith increases and decreases, and the underlying disagreement about the definition of faith.

Core Idea
The dispute over faith's increase hinges on whether acts are part of faith.

This passage introduces a key historical disagreement in Islamic theology: does faith (iman) increase and decrease? The answer depends on how we define faith. Some scholars define it as mere affirmation, while others include acts of obedience. This lesson presents the two positions and their logical basis.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once, then its translation. Notice the two positions mentioned.
2
Identify the two groups
Find where Abu Hanifa and the Ash'ari majority are mentioned, and note their respective views.
3
Understand the basis
The text says the disagreement is based on whether obedient acts are included in the concept of faith. Reflect on why that matters.
4
Ask yourself
If faith is mere affirmation, can it change? If it includes acts, can it change? Which view seems more plausible based on the passage?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإنما التفاضل بينهم والزيادة والنقص (بالتقوى ومخالفة الهوى) وفي المسايرة: «قال أبو حنيفة وأصحابه: "لا يزيد الإيمان ولا ينقص، واختاره من الأشاعرة إمام الحرمين وكثير، وذهب عامتهم إلى زيادته ونقصانه، قيل: والخلاف مبني على أخذ الطاعات في مفهوم الإيمان وعدمه، فعلى الأول يزيد بزيادتها وينقص بنقصانها، وعلى الثاني لا؛ لأنه اسم للتصديق الجازم مع الإذعان وهذا لا يتغير بضم الطاعات ولا ضم المعاصي وفيه نظر؛ بل قال بزيادته ونقصانه كثير ممن صرح بأنه مجرد التصديق لظواهر؛ كقوله تعالى: (زَادَهُمْ إِيمَنًا) [سورة الأنفال آية: ٢]، وعن ابن عمر قلنا: يا رسول الله: إن الإيمان يزيد وينقص؟ قال: نَعَمْ يَزِيدُ حَتَّى يُدْخِلَ صَاحِبَهُ الجَنَّةَ وَيَنقُصُ حَتَّى يُدْخِلَ صَاحِبَهُ النَّارَ (۱)، وقالوا: لا مانع عقلا من ذلك.
قال في المسامرة (۲۱۷/۲): «رواه أبو إسحاق الثعلبي في تفسيره من رواية علي بن عبد العزيز عن حبيب بن عيسى بن فروخ عن إسماعيل بن عبد الرحمن عن مالك عن نافع عن ابن عمر، قال ابن القيم: كل حديث فيه أن الإيمان لا يزيد ولا ينقص كذب مختلق، وقابل من وضعها طائفة أخرى فوضعوا أحاديث على رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم أن الإيمان يزيد وينقص، وهذا كلام صحيح وهو إجماع السلف، حكاه الشافعي وغيره، ولكن هذا اللفظ كذب على رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم، المنار المنيف ص (۱۱۹).
And differentiation among them and increase and decrease (is by piety and opposing desires). And in al-Musayarah: "Abu Hanifa and his companions said: 'Faith does not increase nor decrease', and it was chosen by Imâm al-Haramayn and many among the Ash'aris, and the majority of them held that it increases and decreases. It is said: The disagreement is based on whether obedient acts are included in the concept of faith or not. On the first view, it increases with their increase and decreases with their decrease; on the second, no, because it is the name for decisive affirmation with submission, and this does not change by adding obedient acts nor adding sinful acts. And there is consideration in this; rather, many who explicitly stated that it is mere affirmation held it increases and decreases due to apparent evidences, such as His statement: 'He increased them in faith' (Surah al-Anfal, 2), and from Ibn 'Umar: We said, O Messenger of Allah, does faith increase and decrease? He said: 'Yes, it increases until it brings its possessor into Paradise, and it decreases until it brings its possessor into the Fire.' (1) And they said: There is no rational impediment to that.
He said in al-Musamarah (217/2): 'It was narrated by Abu Ishaq al-Tha'labi in his tafsir from the narration of Ali ibn Abd al-Aziz from Habib ibn Isa ibn Farukh from Isma'il ibn Abd al-Rahman from Malik from Nafi from Ibn Umar. Ibn al-Qayyim said: Every hadith that faith does not increase nor decrease is a fabricated lie. And another group responded by fabricating hadiths upon the Messenger of Allah that faith increases and decreases. This speech is correct and it is the consensus of the Salaf, narrated by al-Shafi'i and others. But this wording is a lie upon the Messenger of Allah. Al-Manar al-Munif, p. 119.'
Source pages p. 129

Commentary
This passage presents the historical dispute regarding whether iman can increase and decrease. After quoting the matn's statement that differentiation is by piety, the commentator cites the work al-Musayarah, which records that Abu Hanifa and his followers held that faith does not increase or decrease, a position also chosen by Imam al-Haramayn (al-Juwayni) among the Ash'aris. In contrast, the majority of Ash'aris held that it does increase and decrease. The underlying reason for the disagreement is said to be whether obedient acts (ṭā'āt) are included in the concept of faith or not. If they are included, then faith increases with more acts and decreases with fewer; if not, then faith as decisive affirmation with submission remains unchanged. The passage notes that many who considered faith mere affirmation still held it increases due to apparent evidences, such as the Quranic verse 'He increased them in faith' (8:2) and a hadith from Ibn Umar in which the Prophet reportedly said faith increases until entering Paradise and decreases until entering Hell. The commentator then adds a critical footnote citing Ibn al-Qayyim, who declares that any hadith claiming faith does not increase or decrease is fabricated, and that the reported hadith about increase is also a fabrication, though the principle of increase and decrease is correct and was the consensus of the Salaf.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If your faith is defined merely as 'affirmation and submission' that does not change with your actions, then what is at stake when you sin? Does this view reduce the urgency of obedience or deepen your reliance on Allah's mercy? Look at your own life: do you treat your sins as affecting your relationship with Allah, or do you separate them from your 'real' faith? This lesson forces you to choose a definition—which one actually drives you to repent?
?
The passage says that if acts are part of faith, then faith increases and decreases. But in your own experience, have you ever felt your faith 'increase' after a good deed? Or have you used a decrease as an excuse for complacency? The disagreement here is not academic—it shapes how you view every action. Will you examine your own heart and see whether your deeds truly change your conviction or merely reflect it?
?
You now know that the basis of the disagreement is whether actions are included in the definition of faith. So ask yourself: when you pray, do you believe you are adding to your faith, or are you only expressing what is already there? Is your prayer a growth or a demonstration? The answer dictates whether you feel closer to Allah after worship or simply satisfied. Which feeling aligns with the position you now hold? And is that position making you more diligent or more careless?

Evidences for Increase and Decrease of Faith and Their Critique
Maydani presents the evidence for increase and decrease of faith and a critical hadith assessment.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the textual evidence cited for faith's increase and decrease, and the critical assessment of the hadith used.

Core Idea
Both Quran and hadith are cited, but the hadith is critically examined as possibly fabricated.

In this passage, Maydani presents the arguments of those who affirm increase and decrease of faith even though they define faith as mere affirmation. They cite the Quranic verse 'He increased them in faith' and a hadith from Ibn Umar. However, the commentator adds a critical note from Ibn al-Qayyim, who states that the hadith reporting the Prophet's words is fabricated, though the principle of increase and decrease is correct.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage

2
Identify the evidences
Find the Quranic verse and the hadith. What are they?
3
Understand the critique
The commentator adds a footnote citing Ibn al-Qayyim. What does he say about the hadith?
4
Reflect
Why does this critique matter? Does it undermine the position that faith increases?

قال في المسامرة (۲۱۷/۲): «رواه أبو إسحاق الثعلبي في تفسيره من رواية علي بن عبد العزيز عن حبيب بن عيسى بن فروخ عن إسماعيل بن عبد الرحمن عن مالك عن نافع عن ابن عمر، قال ابن القيم: كل حديث فيه أن الإيمان لا يزيد ولا ينقص كذب مختلق، وقابل من وضعها طائفة أخرى فوضعوا أحاديث على رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم أن الإيمان يزيد وينقص، وهذا كلام صحيح وهو إجماع السلف، حكاه الشافعي وغيره، ولكن هذا اللفظ كذب على رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم، المنار المنيف ص (۱۱۹).
And differentiation among them and increase and decrease (is by piety and opposing desires). And in al-Musayarah: "Abu Hanifa and his companions said: 'Faith does not increase nor decrease', and it was chosen by Imâm al-Haramayn and many among the Ash'aris, and the majority of them held that it increases and decreases. It is said: The disagreement is based on whether obedient acts are included in the concept of faith or not. On the first view, it increases with their increase and decreases with their decrease; on the second, no, because it is the name for decisive affirmation with submission, and this does not change by adding obedient acts nor adding sinful acts. And there is consideration in this; rather, many who explicitly stated that it is mere affirmation held it increases and decreases due to apparent evidences, such as His statement: 'He increased them in faith' (Surah al-Anfal, 2), and from Ibn 'Umar: We said, O Messenger of Allah, does faith increase and decrease? He said: 'Yes, it increases until it brings its possessor into Paradise, and it decreases until it brings its possessor into the Fire.' (1) And they said: There is no rational impediment to that.
He said in al-Musamarah (217/2): 'It was narrated by Abu Ishaq al-Tha'labi in his tafsir from the narration of Ali ibn Abd al-Aziz from Habib ibn Isa ibn Farukh from Isma'il ibn Abd al-Rahman from Malik from Nafi from Ibn Umar. Ibn al-Qayyim said: Every hadith that faith does not increase nor decrease is a fabricated lie. And another group responded by fabricating hadiths upon the Messenger of Allah that faith increases and decreases. This speech is correct and it is the consensus of the Salaf, narrated by al-Shafi'i and others. But this wording is a lie upon the Messenger of Allah. Al-Manar al-Munif, p. 119.'
Source pages p. 129

Commentary
This passage presents the historical dispute regarding whether iman can increase and decrease. After quoting the matn's statement that differentiation is by piety, the commentator cites the work al-Musayarah, which records that Abu Hanifa and his followers held that faith does not increase or decrease, a position also chosen by Imam al-Haramayn (al-Juwayni) among the Ash'aris. In contrast, the majority of Ash'aris held that it does increase and decrease. The underlying reason for the disagreement is said to be whether obedient acts (ṭā'āt) are included in the concept of faith or not. If they are included, then faith increases with more acts and decreases with fewer; if not, then faith as decisive affirmation with submission remains unchanged. The passage notes that many who considered faith mere affirmation still held it increases due to apparent evidences, such as the Quranic verse 'He increased them in faith' (8:2) and a hadith from Ibn Umar in which the Prophet reportedly said faith increases until entering Paradise and decreases until entering Hell. The commentator then adds a critical footnote citing Ibn al-Qayyim, who declares that any hadith claiming faith does not increase or decrease is fabricated, and that the reported hadith about increase is also a fabrication, though the principle of increase and decrease is correct and was the consensus of the Salaf.

Key Terms
إيمان
زيادة
نقصان
سورة الأنفال
حديث ابن عمر
وضع

Correction: Ibn al-Qayyim states that this wording is a lie upon the Messenger, though the principle of increase and decrease is correct.

Checkpoint
According to Ibn al-Qayyim as cited in the passage, what is the status of the hadith that faith increases and decreases?
A) It is authentic
B) It is fabricated

D) It is not mentioned

Key Takeaway
While the Quranic verse is accepted as evidence, the specific hadith on increase and decrease is considered fabricated by Ibn al-Qayyim, though the principle itself is sound.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
This lesson teaches that a fabricated hadith can still contain a true principle. Have you ever blindly accepted a religious statement because it sounded comforting or widely repeated? How can you train yourself to verify the authenticity of what you believe, even when it feels true?
?
If faith can truly increase and decrease, when was the last time you honestly evaluated your own īmān? Do you take concrete steps to increase it, or do you assume it remains static? What one action will you commit to today to actively seek an increase in your faith?
?
The passage shows that even the consensus of the Salaf is not enough to make a fabricated hadith authentic. Are you willing to accept that some cherished narrations might be weak or fabricated, even if they support a correct belief? How does that affect your trust in the books you read and the scholars you follow?

Increase in Clarity, Not in Essence
Maydani explains the Hanafi/Imam al-Haramayn position that increase is in clarity, not essence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Hanafi/Imam al-Haramayn position that faith increases in clarity and speed of certainty, not in its essence.

Core Idea
Faith's increase is in clarity, not essence: believers vary in certainty's speed and vividness.

This lesson examines a key theological distinction: when we speak of faith increasing, what exactly increases? The Hanafis and Imam al-Haramayn argue that the variation lies in the clarity and speed of conviction, not in the essence of faith itself. The passage explores this through the example of Prophet Abraham and a narration from Abu Hanifa.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify the main claim
Read the Arabic passage once and note the opening statement about certainty varying from clearest self-evident to most hidden theoretical propositions.
The key term is "يقين" (certainty), which is the content of affirmation (تصديق).
2
Study the example of Prophet Abraham
Consider why Abraham asked for reassurance despite having faith. This illustrates that certainty can have degrees without the essence of faith changing.
The verse is from Surah al-Baqarah 260.
3
Analyze Abu Hanifa's statement
Notice the distinction between 'like' (كـ) and 'similar' (مثل). Abu Hanifa says his faith is like Gabriel's but not similar, emphasizing that variation is not in essence.
Similarity implies equality in all attributes, while likeness does not.
4
Understand the explanation of variation
The passage argues that apparent variation in strength of certainty is actually due to clarity (جلاء) and speed of conviction. Reflect on the example of certainty about the world's origin vs. that one is half of two.
The footnote classifies propositions into self-evident and theoretical, supporting the point about differing clarity.
