وروي عن أبي حنيفة أنه قال: «أقول: إيماني كإيمان جبريل، ولا أقول مثل إيمان جبريل؛ لأن المثلية تقتضي المساواة في كل الصفات والتشبيه لا يقتضيه؛ فلا أحد يسوي بين إيمان آحاد الناس وإيمان الملائكة والأنبياء بل يتفاوت، غير أن ذلك التفاوت بزيادة ونقص في نفس الذات أو بأمور زائدة عليها؛ فمنعوا - يعني الحنفية وموافقيهم الأول، وقالوا: ما يتخايل من أن القطع يتفاوت قوة إنما هو راجع إلى جلائه؛ فإذا ظهر القطع بحدوث العالم بعد ترتب مقدماته كان الجزم الكائن فيه كالجزم في قولنا الواحد نصف الاثنين، وإنما تفاوتها باعتبار أنه إذا لوحظ هذا كان سرعة الجزم فيه ليس كالسرعة التي في الآخر؛ خصوصا مع عزوب (۳) النظر فيتخيل أنه [ أقوى ) وإنما هو أجلى عند العقل؛ فنحن لو

(۱) النظريات القطعية ككون العالم حادثا المسامرة. فالتصديق هو المركب التام الذي يحتمل الصدق والكذب لذاته، وقد يسمى قضية، وهو ينقسم إلى بديهي ونظري؛ فالبديهي ما لا يحتاج إلى نظر وهو على ضريين: جلي وهو أولي كقولنا: "الكل أعظم من الجزء"، وفطري كـ" الأربعة زوج"، وتجريبي كـ "الماء يطفئ حرارة العطش"، ومشترك بين عامة الناس وهو حسي كـ الشمس مضيئة" ووجداني كـ"الخوف عارض يعرض للإنسان". وخفي وهو حدسي كـ" القمر يستفيد نوره من الشمس"، ومتواتر كـ"مكة موجودة" . والنظري: كل قضية لا يجزم العقل فيها بثبوت المحمول للموضوع إلا بعد النظر فيها والاستدلال عليها. انظر: رسالة الآداب ص (٩٦-١٠٣).
(۲) أي ذات التصديق المسامرة.
(۳) قال الشيخ محمد البيطار في الحاشية: قوله: "عزوب" بالعين المهملة والزاي المعجمة، مصدر عزب أي بعد وغاب وبابه دخل وجلس، وفي الحديث: «من قرأ القرآن في أربعين ليلة فقد عرب بالتشديد ؛ أي بعد عهده بيا ابتدأ منه. اهـ مختاره . مادة (عزب).
Rather, certainty which is the content of affirmation varies in strength in itself from the clearest of self-evident truths to the most hidden of certain theoretical propositions (1); hence Abraham peace be upon him said when addressed with His words: 'Have you not believed?' He said: 'Yes, but so that my heart may be at ease' (Surah al-Baqarah, 260). And the Hanafis, along with Imâm al-Haramayn and others, do not forbid increase and decrease considering aspects other than the essence itself (2), rather by its variance the believers vary.

And it is narrated from Abu Hanifa that he said: 'I say: my faith is like the faith of Gabriel, and I do not say similar to the faith of Gabriel; because similarity requires equality in all attributes, and likeness does not necessitate it; so no one equates the faith of ordinary people with the faith of angels and prophets, rather they vary, except that that variation is by increase and decrease in the essence itself or by matters additional to it; so they prevented – meaning the Hanafis and their first supporters – and they said: What is imagined that certainty varies in strength is only due to its clarity; so if certainty about the occurrence of the world appears after the arrangement of its premises, the conviction present in it is like the conviction in our saying: one is half of two, and their variance is only considered because when this is observed, the speed of conviction in it is not like the speed in the other; especially with the absence (3) of reflection, so it is imagined that it is [stronger] but rather it is clearer to the intellect; so we would...

(1) The certain theoretical propositions, such as the world being originated – al-Musamarah. Affirmation is the complete compound which can be true or false in itself, and may be called a proposition, and it is divided into the self-evident (badihī) and the theoretical (naẓarī). The self-evident is that which does not require reflection, and it is of two types: clear (jaliyy) which is primary (awwaliyy) like 'the whole is greater than the part', and innate (fiṭrī) like 'four is even', and experiential (tajrībī) like 'water extinguishes the heat of thirst', and commonly known among the general public which is sensory (ḥissī) like 'the sun is luminous' and intuitive (wijdānī) like 'fear is an accident that occurs to man'. And hidden (khafiyy) which is conjectural (ḥadsī) like 'the moon derives its light from the sun', and recurrent (mutawātir) like 'Mecca exists'. And the theoretical: every proposition about which the intellect cannot assert the predication of the attribute to the subject except after reflection and inference. See: Risālat al-Ādāb, pp. 96-103.
(2) i.e., the essence of affirmation – al-Musamarah.
(3) Shaykh Muhammad al-Baytār said in the margin: his saying 'absence' ('uzūb) with the unpointed 'ayn and pointed zāy, is the source of 'azaba meaning to be distant and absent, its paradigm is dakhala and jalasa. In the hadith: 'Whoever recites the Quran in forty nights has become distant' ('azaba with tashdīd), i.e., his covenant with its beginning has become distant. End of his summary. Root (عزب).
Source pages p. 130

Commentary
This passage is a continuing argument from the commentator explaining the Hanafi and Imām al-Haramayn position on the increase of faith. It begins by stating that certainty (yaqīn), which is the content of affirmation (tasdiq), varies in strength in itself, from the clearest self-evident truths (badīhiyyāt) to the most hidden certain theoretical propositions (naẓariyyāt qaṭ'iyya). The commentator then provides the example of Prophet Abraham (AS) who, despite having faith, asked for reassurance from God, showing that certainty can have degrees. The Hanafis and Imām al-Haramayn do not forbid increase and decrease when considered from aspects other than the essence of faith; rather, believers vary in these aspects. A narration from Abu Hanifa is cited: he says his faith is like (ka) that of Gabriel, not similar (mithl) because similarity implies full equality in all attributes, but likeness does not. The variation among believers is not due to increase or decrease in the essence of faith itself, nor to additional matters; rather, the apparent variation in the strength of certainty is actually due to its clarity (jalā'). For example, if certainty about the origination of the world appears after arranging premises, the conviction in it is like the conviction that one is half of two. The difference is in the speed of conviction and the absence of reflection, so it is imagined to be stronger, but it is merely clearer to the intellect. The passage then includes a lengthy footnote (1) that classifies propositions (qadiyya) into self-evident (badīhī) and theoretical (naẓarī), with subdivisions of the self-evident into clear/primary, innate, experiential, sensory, intuitive, hidden/conjectural, and recurrent. This classification supports the argument that certainty varies in clarity. Another footnote explains 'essence of affirmation' and a third defines the word 'uzūb (absence).

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think the Hanafis deny any variation in faith, but they affirm variation in clarity and speed of certainty, not in the essence.
Correction: The Hanafis affirm that faith does not increase in its essence but rather in its clarity and the speed of conviction, as the passage states: 'ما يتخايل من أن القطع يتفاوت قوة إنما هو راجع إلى جلائه'.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafis maintain that faith's increase is in the clarity and speed of certainty, not in its essence, reconciling scriptural descriptions of varying faith with theological consistency.

?
Prophet Abraham, a prophet, asked for a sign to increase his heart's ease, not because he doubted. Are you humble enough to admit when your certainty needs strengthening through evidence and reflection? What specific step will you take this week to move from theoretical certainty to vivid clarity?

The Variation of Faith and the Hanafi Position
The author states that tasdiq varies in strength and explains the Hanafi position on faith's increase and decrease.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that according to the Hanafis, faith does not increase or decrease in its essence but in its clarity and strength.

Core Idea
Faith's variation is in clarity, not essence.

This passage addresses a key question in Islamic theology: does faith increase and decrease? The author explains that the content of assent (tasdiq) varies in strength, and the Hanafis along with others affirm variation but not in the essence of faith. Instead, the variation is due to clarity (jala') and accompanying factors. This lesson will unpack the argument and the famous statement of Imam Abu Hanifa.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the literal translation. Notice the flow of the argument and the use of technical terms.
Pay attention to the footnote markers; they indicate references.
2
Understand the range of tasdiq
The author states that tasdiq varies from the most evident necessary truths (badihiyyat) to the most hidden certain theoretical propositions (nazariyyat qat'iyya). Reflect on what these terms mean.
Badihiyyat are self-evident truths, like 'the whole is greater than the part'. Nazariyyat require proof.
3
Consider the example of Ibrahim (AS)
Prophet Ibrahim asked for reassurance despite having faith. This shows that even prophets can experience different levels of certainty.
This is a proof that tasdiq can vary in strength.
4
Examine the Hanafi position
The Hanafis, along with Imam al-Haramayn, do not deny increase or decrease in faith, but they say it occurs in aspects other than the essence. Read Abu Hanifa's statement about his faith being 'like' but not 'the same' as Jibril's.
The distinction between 'like' (ka-) and 'same' (mithl) is crucial.
5
Grasp the role of clarity (jala')
The Hanafis explain that the perceived variation in certainty is actually due to clarity, not the essence. For example, certainty about the world's creation is as strong as knowing that one is half of two; the difference is in speed and vividness.
This resolves the apparent contradiction of faith increasing and decreasing.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مضمون التصديق يتفاوت قوة في نفسه من أجلى البديهيات إلى أخفى النظريات القطعية (۱)؛ ولذا قال إبراهيم عليه السلام حين خوطب بقوله: (أَوَلَمْ تُؤْمِن قَالَ بَلَى وَلَكِن لِيَطْمَين قلبي ﴾ [سورة البقرة آية: ٢٦٠] ، والحنفية ومعهم إمام الحرمين وغيره لا يمنعون الزيادة والنقصان باعتبار جهان هي غير نفس الذات (٢)، بل بتفاوته يتفاوت المؤمنون - وروري عن أبي حنيفة أنه قال: «أقول: إيماني كإيمان جبريل، ولا أقول مثل إيمان جبريل؛ لأن المثلية تقتضي المساواة في كل الصفات والتشبيه لا يقتضيه؛ فلا أحد يسوي بين إيمان آحاد الناس وإيمان الملائكة والأنبياء بل يتفاوت، غير أن ذلك التفاوت بزيادة ونقص في نفس الذات أو بأمور زائدة عليها؛ فمنعوا - يعني الحنفية وموافقيهم الأول، وقالوا: ما يتخايل من أن القطع يتفاوت قوة إنما هو راجع إلى جلائه؛ فإذا ظهر القطع بحدوث العالم بعد ترتب مقدماته كان الجزم الكائن فيه كالجزم في قولنا الواحد نصف الاثنين، وإنما تفاوتها باعتبار أنه إذا لوحظ هذا كان سرعة الجزم فيه ليس كالسرعة التي في الآخر؛ خصوصا مع عزوب النظر (۳) فيتخيل أنه [ أقوى ) وإنما هو أجلى عند العقل.
The content of assent varies in strength in itself from the most evident necessary truths to the most hidden certain theoretical propositions (1); therefore Ibrahim, peace be upon him, said when addressed by His statement: "Did you not believe? He said: Yes, but so that my heart may be reassured" [Surah Al-Baqara, verse 260]. And the Hanafis, along with Imam al-Haramayn and others, do not deny increase and decrease with respect to aspects other than the essence itself (2), but rather by its variation the believers vary. And it is narrated from Abu Hanifa that he said: "I say: my faith is like the faith of Jibril, and I do not say it is the same as the faith of Jibril; because 'same' (mithliyya) entails equality in all attributes, whereas 'like' (tashbih) does not entail it. So no one equates the faith of individual people with the faith of angels and prophets; rather it varies, except that this variation is by increase and decrease in the essence itself or in matters additional to it. So they—meaning the Hanafis and their followers—denied the first, and said: what appears that certainty (qat') varies in strength is only due to its clarity (jala'); for when certainty about the world being created appears after its premises are arranged, the conviction in it is like the conviction in our statement 'one is half of two'. And their difference is only by considering that when this is observed, the speed of conviction in it is not like the speed in the other, especially when the reflection is absent, so it appears that it is stronger, whereas it is only clearer to the mind.
Source pages p. 130

Commentary
This passage defines the nature of tasdiq (assent) and addresses the issue of whether faith can increase or decrease. The author begins by stating that the content of assent (tasdiq) varies in strength, ranging from the most evident necessary truths (badihiyyat) to the most hidden certain theoretical propositions (nazariyyat qat'iyya). He cites the verse of Ibrahim (AS) where he asks for reassurance, showing that even prophets seek increased certainty. The Hanafis, along with Imam al-Haramayn and others, hold that increase and decrease in faith occur with respect to aspects other than the essence of faith itself. The author then quotes Abu Hanifa: 'I say my faith is like the faith of Jibril, but I do not say it is the same as the faith of Jibril.' This is because 'like' (ka-) does not imply equality in all attributes, whereas 'same' (mithl) would. So no one equates the faith of ordinary people with that of angels and prophets; it varies. However, the variation is not in the essence of faith itself but in its clarity and strength. The Hanafis say that the perceived variation in certainty (qat') is due to its clarity (jala') rather than its essence. For example, certainty about the world being created is as strong as the certainty that one is half of two; the difference is in the speed of conviction and the ease of mental presence, especially when the reasoning is absent from thought. Thus, what appears to be a difference in strength is actually a difference in clarity for the mind.

قطع (qat')

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Faith increases and decreases in its essence.
Correction: The Hanafis hold that faith varies only in its clarity and accompanying factors, not in its essential reality.

Checkpoint

A) In its essence and reality
B) In its clarity and accompanying aspects
C) In the number of articles of faith
D) In the intention of the believer

Key Takeaway
Faith varies in strength and clarity, but not in its essential reality.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

Faith and Disbelief

Increase of Faith Through New Obligations
Explains Quranic verses on increase of faith via Abu Hanifa's interpretation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Abu Hanifa interpreted Quranic verses about increase of faith and why this interpretation is limited to the Prophet's era.

Core Idea
Faith increases by believing in new obligations, not by intensity.

The Quran speaks of faith increasing, but what does that mean? Abu Hanifa offers a precise interpretation: the increase comes from new obligations (farāʾiḍ) that were revealed to the Prophet's Companions, not from a change in conviction. This lesson examines the evidence and the reasoning behind this view, including a later scholar's critique.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice that it opens with a 'note' (tanbīh) and then lists several Quranic verses.
Focus on how Abu Hanifa ties faith increase to new obligations.
2
Identify the Quranic verses
The passage cites five verses that seem to indicate increase of faith. List them and note their common theme.
3
Understand Abu Hanifa's interpretation
According to Abu Hanifa, the Companions had general faith, and each new obligation required them to believe in that specific command. Thus faith increases in its objects, not in strength.
This interpretation limits the increase to the prophetic era.
4
Examine al-Sa'd's objection
Al-Sa'd argues that even after the Prophet, one can acquire detailed knowledge of obligations, so the increase could still occur. Consider how this challenges Abu Hanifa's view.
The author presents this objection neutrally, leaving it for the reader to ponder.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تنبيه ما ورد من الآيات الدالة على زيادة الإيمان كقوله تعالى: ﴿وَإِذَا تُلِيَتْ عَلَيْهِمْ آيَاتُهُ زَادَهُمْ إِيمَانًا﴾ [سورة الأنفال آية: ٢]، وقوله: ﴿فَأَمَّا الَّذِينَ آمَنُوا فَزَادَتْهُمْ إِيمَانًا﴾ [سورة التوبة آية: ١٢٤]، وقوله: ﴿وَيَزْدَادَ الَّذِينَ آمَنُوا إِيمَانًا﴾ [سورة المدثر آية: ٣١]، وقوله: ﴿وَالَّذِينَ اهْتَدَوْا زَادَهُمْ هُدًى﴾ [سورة محمد آية: ١٧]، وقوله: ﴿لِيَزْدَادُوا إِيمَانًا مَعَ إِيمَانِهِمْ﴾ [سورة الفتح آية: ٤] محمولة على ما ذكره أبو حنيفة أنهم كانوا آمنوا في الجملة ثم يأتي فرض بعد فرض فكانوا يؤمنون بكل فرض، وحاصله أنه كان يزيد بزيادة ما يجب الإيمان به، وهذا لا يتصور في غير عصر النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم، قال السعد: وفيه نظر؛ لأن الاطلاع على تفاصيل الفرائض ممكن.
Note: What has come of verses indicating increase of faith, such as His statement, 'And when His verses are recited to them, it increases them in faith' [Surah al-Anfal: 2], and His statement, 'As for those who believe, it has increased them in faith' [Surah al-Tawba: 124], and His statement, 'And the believers will increase in faith' [Surah al-Muddathir: 31], and His statement, 'And those who are guided, He increases them in guidance' [Surah Muhammad: 17], and His statement, 'That they may increase in faith along with their faith' [Surah al-Fath: 4], are interpreted in accordance with what Abu Hanifa mentioned: that they had believed in general, then an obligation after an obligation came, and they would believe in each obligation. Its gist is that it increased by increase of what must be believed in, and this is not conceivable in other than the era of the Prophet ﷺ. Al-Sa'd said: There is consideration in this, because the knowledge of the details of obligations is possible.
Source pages p. 132

Commentary
This passage addresses the Quranic verses that speak of increase in faith (إيمان), which might suggest that faith is not equal for all believers or that it can increase. The author explains these verses according to the view of Abu Hanifa: the Companions had basic faith in the general message, but as new obligations (فرائض) were revealed, they would affirm belief in each new obligation. Thus the increase is not in the strength of conviction but in the number of things believed. This interpretation restricts the increase to the prophetic era, since after the Prophet's death no new obligations come. The author then notes al-Sa'd's criticism: one could still increase in knowledge of the details of obligations even after the Prophet, so the interpretation is open to question. This discussion shows the careful approach to reconciling Quranic texts with theological principles about the nature of faith.

Key Terms
إيمان
زيادة
فرض
أبو حنيفة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that faith can increase in intensity or strength for any believer at any time.
Correction: According to Abu Hanifa's interpretation of these verses, the increase is in the objects of belief (new obligations) and is limited to the Prophet's era.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, how does faith increase according to Abu Hanifa?
A) By increase of conviction
B) By increase of obligations to believe
C) By increase of spiritual states
D) By decrease of doubts

Key Takeaway
Abu Hanifa teaches that faith increases by believing in new obligations, not by intensity, and this only happened during the Prophet's lifetime.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you learn a new Islamic ruling that you were unaware of before, does your faith feel any different? Do you actively believe in that ruling as part of your iman, or do you remain passive?
?
Abu Hanifa says that faith increased only during the Prophet's time through new obligations. But if you could live in that era, would your faith truly be more? What prevents you from embracing the obligations you already know with the same conviction?
?
Al-Sa'd suggests that knowledge of obligations can still increase faith. Think of one obligation you understand but have not fully implemented. What would it take for you to believe in it so deeply that your faith actually increases?

Faith and Disbelief
intermediate
8 min
Why the Debate on Faith's Increase Is Verbal
Presents Quranic evidence and scholarly arguments on increase of faith, concluding the dispute is verbal.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the dispute over whether faith increases or decreases is considered a verbal disagreement, and how scholars distinguish between the essence of faith and its descriptions.

Core Idea
Faith's essence is affirmation; its increase is only in strength, not in itself.

The question of whether faith can increase or decrease has been debated among Muslim scholars, with Quranic verses appearing to support increase. To resolve the apparent conflict, later scholars analyzed the nature of faith itself. This lesson presents the key arguments and the conclusion that the disagreement is ultimately about terminology.

Guided Path
1
Read the Quranic evidence and initial interpretation
Start by reading the Quranic verses that seem to indicate increase of faith, and then consider Abu Hanifah's interpretation that these refer to the era of revelation when new obligations came.
2
Understand al-Sa'd's objection and the author's response
Al-Sa'd objects that detailed knowledge is possible outside the Prophet's era, so increase is still conceivable. The author responds that moving from general to specific knowledge is not an increase in essence.
3
Study the analogy from al-Matalib al-Wafiyya
The analogy compares faith to humanity: just as a sick and healthy person share the same humanity but differ in description, so faith's essence remains the same while its strength varies.
4
Grasp the final conclusion
The disagreement is verbal: those who say faith increases refer to its descriptions (strength/weakness), while those who deny look at its essence (mere affirmation). The latter is preferred.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تنبيه

ما ورد من الآيات الدالة على زيادة الإيمان كقوله تعالى: ﴿وَإِذَا تُلِيَتْ عَلَيْهِمْ آيَاتُهُ زَادَتْهُمْ إِيمَانًا﴾ [سورة الأنفال آية: ٢]، وقوله: ﴿فَأَمَّا الَّذِينَ آمَنُوا فَزَادَتْهُمْ إِيمَانًا﴾ [سورة التوبة آية: ١٢٤]، وقوله: ﴿وَيَزْدَادَ الَّذِينَ آمَنُوا إِيمَانًا﴾ [سورة المدثر آية: ٣١]، وقوله: ﴿وَالَّذِينَ اهْتَدَوْا زَادَهُمْ هُدًى﴾ [سورة محمد آية: ١٧]، وقوله: ﴿لِيَزْدَادُوا إِيمَانًا مَعَ إِيمَانِهِمْ﴾ [سورة الفتح آية: ٤] محمولة على ما ذكره أبو حنيفة أنهم كانوا آمنوا في الجملة ثم يأتي فرض بعد فرض فكانوا يؤمنون بكل فرض، وحاصله أنه كان يزيد بزيادة ما يجب الإيمان به، وهذا لا يتصور في غير عصر النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم. قال السعد: وفيه نظر؛ لأن الاطلاع على تفاصيل الفرائض ممكن في غير عصر النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم، والإيمان واجب إجمالا فيهما علم إجمالا وتفصيلا فيها علم تفصيلا، ولا خفاء في أن التفصيلي أزيد بل أكمل من الإجمالي اهـ.

أقول: لا يخفى أن تلك التفاصيل لما كان الإيمان بها برمتها إجمالا فالاطلاع على تفاصيلها لم يقلب الإيمان من النقصان إلى الزيادة بل من الإجمال إلى التفصيل بخلاف ما في عصر النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم، فإن الإيمان لما كان عبارة عن التصديق بكل ما جاء به من ربه فكلما ازدادت تلك الجملة ازداد التصديق المتعلق به لا محالة. وأما قوله: «فلا خفاء في أن التفصيلي أزيد بل أكمل» فكونه أكمل مسلم إلا أنه غير مفيد، وأما كونه أزيد فممنوع.

ففي المطالب الوفية: ولا يخفى أن مثل هذه الزيادة في الاعتقاد وإن تفاوتت كما ذكر ليست زيادة في أصل الإيمان وإنما هي زيادة في وصفه؛ كالإنسان المريض والإنسان القوي صاحب العافية؛ فإن الإنسانية فيهما على السواء من غير تفاوت وإنما القوة والضعف في أوصافها لا في ذاتهما، والزيادة في وصف الشيء ليست زيادته في ذاته وإلا لكان المؤمنون كافرين بالنسبة إلى الأنبياء عليهم الصلاة والسلام لزيادة إيمان الأنبياء بالنسبة إلى إيمانهم ونقصان إيمانهم عن إيمان الأنبياء عليهم السلام؛ فقد كفروا بتلك الزيادة لعدم وجودها في إيمانهم وهو باطل، بل زيادة إيمان الأنبياء عليهم السلام من حيث القوة، وقد علمت أنها زيادة في الوصف لا في أصل الإيمان فليست زيادة في الإيمان؛ فلا يزيد الإيمان ولا ينقص وإنما يقوى ويضعف؛ فلا عليك مما ذكر ابن قاضي عجلون تبعا لنظم الشيبانية حيث قال: "وفي كون حقيقة التصديق لا تقبل الزيادة والنقص كلام لبعض المحققين مبسوط في المطولات"، وتبعه الشيخ علوان الحموي... وساق عبارتهما ونظر فيها إلى أن قال: والحاصل أن الخلاف لفظي؛ فمن قال بالزيادة والنقصان في الإيمان اعتبر زيادة أوصافه ونقصانها كفوته وضعفه، ومن نفى الزيادة والنقصان عنه نظر إلى ذاته التي هي مجرد التصديق في نفسه، وهو الأولى بالاعتبار عند أولي الأبصار أهـ.
A notice: The verses that have come indicating the increase of faith, such as His statement: 'And when His verses are recited to them, they increase them in faith' [Surah Al-Anfal 2], and His statement: 'As for those who believed, it increased them in faith' [Surah At-Tawbah 124], and His statement: 'And that those who believe may increase in faith' [Surah Al-Muddaththir 31], and His statement: 'And those who are guided, He increases them in guidance' [Surah Muhammad 17], and His statement: 'That they may increase in faith with their faith' [Surah Al-Fath 4], are to be interpreted according to what Abu Hanifah mentioned: that they had believed in general, then an obligation came after another obligation, so they would believe in each obligation. The summary is that it increased by the increase of what must be believed in, and this is inconceivable outside the era of the Prophet (peace be upon him). As-Sa'd said: There is consideration in this, because access to the details of obligations is possible outside the era of the Prophet, and faith is obligatory in general in what is known in general and in detail in what is known in detail. There is no doubt that the detailed is more, indeed more complete, than the general. End.
I say: It is not hidden that those details, since faith in them was entirely in general, becoming aware of their details does not turn faith from deficiency to increase, but from general to specific, unlike in the era of the Prophet, for faith was an affirmation of everything he brought from his Lord; so whenever that totality increased, the affirmation related to it inevitably increased. As for his statement: 'There is no doubt that the detailed is more, indeed more complete' – that it is more complete is accepted, but it is not beneficial; as for it being more, it is denied.
For in al-Matalib al-Wafiyya: And it is not hidden that such an increase in belief, even if it varies as mentioned, is not an increase in the essence of faith, but rather an increase in its description; like the sick human and the strong healthy human: humanity in both is equal without disparity, only strength and weakness are in their descriptions, not in their essences. And an increase in the description of a thing is not an increase in its essence, otherwise the believers would be disbelievers relative to the prophets (peace be upon them) due to the increase of the prophets' faith relative to their faith and the deficiency of their faith relative to the prophets' faith; they would have disbelieved due to that increase because it is not present in their faith, which is false. Rather, the increase in the prophets' faith is in terms of strength, and you have known that it is an increase in description, not in the essence of faith, so it is not an increase in faith. Thus faith does not increase nor decrease; rather it becomes strong and weak. So there is nothing upon you from what Ibn Qadi 'Ajlun mentioned following the poetry of ash-Shaybaniyya where he said: 'On the fact that the reality of affirmation does not accept increase or decrease, there is speech from some verifiers, detailed in the lengthy works.' And Sheikh Alwan al-Hamawi followed him... and he quoted their statements and considered them until he said: The conclusion is that the disagreement is verbal; whoever says increase and decrease in faith considers the increase and decrease of its description like its strength and weakness, and whoever denies increase and decrease looks to its essence which is mere affirmation in itself, and it is more worthy of consideration by the people of insight. End.
Source pages p. 132

Commentary
This passage is a comprehensive discussion on the issue of whether faith (iman) can increase or decrease. It begins as a 'notice' (tanbih) pointing to several Quranic verses that seemingly indicate that faith increases. The author then presents Abu Hanifah's interpretation: these verses refer to the era of revelation when new obligations came, so faith increased by believing in each new obligation. As-Sa'd (al-Taftazani) objects that this only applies in the Prophet's time because outside of it, people can still learn details of obligations, and detailed knowledge is more complete than general knowledge. The author ('I say') responds: the shift from general to detailed knowledge is not an increase in the essence of faith but a change from general to specific. In the Prophet's time, faith was affirmation of everything brought; as new matters came, the affirmation increased. Then the author quotes al-Matalib al-Wafiyya which uses the analogy of a sick person and a healthy person: humanity is the same, but strength and weakness are descriptions. Similarly, increase in faith is in description (strength/weakness), not essence. If increase were in essence, believers would be disbelievers relative to prophets because their faith is less. The conclusion, from Ibn Qadi 'Ajlun, is that the disagreement is verbal: those who say faith increases refer to its descriptions, and those who deny it refer to its essence (mere affirmation). The latter view is preferred.

ذات

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Faith increases and decreases in its essence.
Correction: Faith's essence (affirmation) does not change; only its strength (description) varies.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the final conclusion regarding the increase of faith?
A) Faith increases and decreases in its essence
B) The disagreement is verbal, based on whether one considers essence or description
C) Faith never changes at all
D) Only prophets experience increase in faith

Key Takeaway
The dispute over faith's increase is verbal; the essence of faith (affirmation) does not change, only its strength.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you experience moments of weak faith, do you ever doubt the very foundation of your iman? According to this lesson, your affirmation (tasdiq) remains intact. How does this knowledge change the way you respond to spiritual lows? Will you now see them as a call to strengthen what you already have, rather than to question if you truly believe?
?
The lesson claims that faith's essence is unchanging. But have you ever felt that your faith has actually grown—as if you believe more deeply? If so, how would you describe that change now: a change in essence or a change in strength? Be honest with yourself. What practical steps can you take to strengthen your faith's description without doubting its essence?
?
Consider the prophets: their iman is perfect, yet according to this lesson, the difference is not in the essence but in description. Does that challenge your assumption that some people are simply 'more faithful'? How might this understanding affect your view of others' faith and your own? Will you now be more patient with yourself and others when faith feels weak, knowing the core is intact?

Faith and Disbelief
intermediate
6 min
Does Faith Increase? Understanding Maydani's Distinction
Maydani argues that detailed knowledge does not increase the essence of faith.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maydani's argument that the essence of faith (tasdiq) does not increase, only its description (strength/weakness).

Core Idea
Faith's essence is like humanity – it cannot increase, only its strength changes.

In this passage, Maydani addresses a key theological question: does the faith of a believer increase when they learn more details? He distinguishes between the essence of faith (affirmation) and its description (strength). Through the analogy of a sick and healthy person, he shows that increase in description is not increase in essence. He also addresses a potential objection regarding the faith of prophets, concluding that the disagreement is merely verbal.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis. Then read the literal translation to grasp the overall argument.
Pay attention to terms like إيمان, تصديق, إجمال, تفصيل.
2
Identify the two eras
Notice how Maydani distinguishes between the Prophet's era, where faith increased with new revelations, and later times, where faith is obligatory in general and learning details does not increase its essence.
3
Understand the analogy
The analogy of a sick man and a strong healthy man illustrates that humanity is the same in both; the difference is in strength/weakness (descriptions), not essence. Apply this to faith.
This is central to the argument.
4
Grasp the conclusion
Maydani concludes that the disagreement is verbal: those who say faith increases refer to its descriptions (strength/weakness), while those who deny increase consider its essence (mere affirmation). The latter is preferred.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
في غير عصر النبي ، والإيمان واجب إجمالا فيهما علم إجمالا وتفصيلا فيها علم تفصيلا، ولا خفاء في أن التفصيلي أزيد بل أكمل من الإجمالي (۱) اهـ. أقول: لا يخفى أن تلك التفاصيل لما كان الإيمان بها برمتها إجمالا فالاطلاع على تفاصيلها لم يقلب الإيمان من النقصان إلى الزيادة بل من الإجمال إلى التفصيل بخلاف ما في عصر النبي وعليه فإن الإيمان لما كان عبارة عن التصديق بكل ما جاء به من ربه فكلما ازدادت تلك الجملة ازداد التصديق المتعلق به لا محالة. وأما قوله: «فلا خفاء في أن التفصيلي أزيد بل أكمل فكونه أكمل مسلم إلا أنه غير مفيد، وأما كونه أزيد فممنوع؛ ففي المطالب الوفية: ولا يخفي أن مثل هذه الزيادة في الاعتقاد وإن تفاوتت كما ذكر ليست زيادة في أصل الإيمان وإنما هي زيادة في وصفه؛ كالإنسان المريض والإنسان القوي صاحب العافية؛ فإن الإنسانية فيهما على السواء من غير تفاوت وإنها القوة والضعف في أوصافها لا في ذاتهما، والزيادة في وصف الشيء ليست زيادته في ذاته وإلا لكان المؤمنون كافرين بالنسبة إلى الأنبياء عليهم الصلاة والسلام لزيادة إيمان الأنبياء بالنسبة إلى إيمانهم ونقصان إيمانهم عن إيمان الأنبياء عليهم السلام؛ فقد كفروا بتلك الزيادة لعدم وجودها في إيمانهم وهو باطل، بل زيادة إيمان الأنبياء عليهم السلام من حيث القوة، وقد علمت أنها زيادة في الوصف لا في أصل الإيمان فليست زيادة في الإيمان؛ فلا يزيد الإيمان ولا ينقص وإنما يقوى ويضعف؛ فلا عليك مما ذكر ابن قاضي عجلون تبعا لنظم الشيبانية حيث قال: "وفي كون حقيقة التصديق لا تقبل الزيادة والنقص كلام لبعض المحققين مبسوط في المطولات"، وتبعه الشيخ علوان الحموي... وساق عبارتهما ونظر فيها إلى أن قال: والحاصل أن الخلاف لفظي؛ فمن قال بالزيادة والنقصان في الإيمان اعتبر زيادة أوصافه ونقصانها كفوته وضعفه، ومن نفى الزيادة والنقصان عنه نظر إلى ذاته التي هي مجرد التصديق في نفسه، وهو الأولى بالاعتبار عند أولي الأبصار أهـ.
In other than the era of the Prophet, faith is obligatory in general (ijmal) in both, knowledge in general and detailed (tafsil) in them is detailed knowledge, and there is no hiddenness in that the detailed is more and more complete than the general. (1) End. I say: It is not hidden that those details, since faith in them as a whole is general, then becoming acquainted with their details does not turn faith from deficiency to increase but from general to detailed, contrary to what is in the era of the Prophet and upon him, for faith was expression of affirmation (tasdiq) of everything he brought from his Lord, so whenever that total increased, the affirmation related to it necessarily increased. And as for his statement: 'There is no hiddenness in that the detailed is more, rather more complete': that it is more complete is conceded but it is not beneficial; as for it being more, it is prevented. For in al-Matalib al-Wafiyyah: And it is not hidden that such an increase in belief, even if it differs as mentioned, is not an increase in the essence of faith but rather an increase in its description; like a sick man and a strong healthy man: humanity in both is equal without variation, and [the difference] is strength and weakness in their descriptions, not in their essences. And the increase in the description of something is not an increase in its essence, otherwise the believers would be disbelievers relative to the prophets, peace be upon them, due to the increase of the faith of the prophets relative to their faith and the deficiency of their faith from the faith of the prophets, peace be upon them; for they would have disbelieved by that increase due to its absence in their faith, and that is false. Rather, the increase of faith of the prophets, peace be upon them, is in terms of strength, and you have known that it is an increase in description, not in the essence of faith, so it is not an increase in faith. Thus faith does not increase or decrease, but rather it strengthens and weakens. So do not mind what Ibn Qadi Ajlun mentioned following Nazm al-Shaybaniyyah where he said: 'Concerning whether the reality of affirmation does not admit increase or decrease, there is speech of some verifiers spread out in the lengthy works.' And Sheikh Alwan al-Hamawi followed him ... and he quoted their statements and considered them until he said: The summary is that the disagreement is verbal. So whoever said increase and decrease in faith considered the increase of its descriptions and their decrease like its strength and weakness, and whoever denied increase and decrease considered its essence which is mere affirmation in itself, and it is the more appropriate for consideration in the sight of those of insight. End.
Source pages p. 133

Commentary
This passage is a theological argument about the nature of faith (iman). The author, Maydani, begins by distinguishing between the era of the Prophet (where faith increased with new revelations) and later times, where faith is obligatory in general. He then addresses a quote stating that detailed knowledge (tafsili) is more and more complete than general knowledge (ijmali). The author comments that in the Prophet's time, faith was affirmation of everything he brought, so it increased as revelation increased. But in later times, learning details does not increase the essence of faith; it only changes it from general to detailed. He quotes al-Matalib al-Wafiyyah to argue that such increase is in description, not essence, using the analogy of humanity being equal in sick and healthy people — the difference is in strength/weakness, not the essence. If increase in description were increase in essence, believers would be considered disbelievers compared to prophets because their faith is weaker; this is absurd. Thus faith does not increase or decrease in its essence; it only strengthens or weakens. The author then dismisses the view of Ibn Qadi Ajlun and others, concluding that the disagreement is verbal: those who affirm increase and decrease consider the descriptions (strength/weakness), while those who deny it consider the essence (mere affirmation). The latter view is preferred.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that the essence of faith increases when one acquires more detailed religious knowledge.
Correction: The passage clarifies that only the description (strength) increases, not the essence. Faith's essence is mere affirmation (tasdiq) and does not change.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what happens to the essence of faith when a believer learns more details?
A) It increases.
B) It decreases.
C) It remains the same.
D) It changes from general to detailed but does not increase in essence.

Key Takeaway
Faith (iman) as affirmation (tasdiq) is a single essence that does not increase or decrease; only its strength and weakness, which are descriptions, can vary.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you feel your faith is weak, do you believe you have less faith than others, or that your faith is simply weaker? How does Maydani's distinction change how you assess yourself and your spiritual state?
?
If the essence of faith is identical in every believer—from the newest Muslim to the greatest scholar—how should that affect your view of others? Are you tempted to judge based on the strength of their practice rather than the reality of their iman?
?
The passage concludes the disagreement is verbal. Are you willing to adopt the view that focuses on the essence, even if it means you cannot claim to have 'more faith' but only 'stronger faith'? How does this shape the way you strive to strengthen your faith without worrying about its quantity?

All Believers Are Saints of Allah
Explanation of the Tahawiyyah statement on universal sainthood

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that every believer is a saint (wali) of Allah, the two possible meanings of wali, and the criterion for the most honorable believer.

Core Idea
Every believer is a friend of God; the best is the most obedient and most Quran-following.

The Tahawiyyah Creed asserts that all believers are awliya of the Most Merciful. This lesson unpacks what 'wali' means—whether it is one cared for by God or one who worships God—and identifies the truly honorable believer. We will explore the linguistic analysis and the scriptural proofs.

Guided Path
1
Read the statement and its Quranic proof
Begin by reading the Arabic statement 'Wa al-mu'minoon kulluhum awliya' al-Rahman' and the supporting verse from Surat al-Anfal.
Notice the link between faith and sainthood.
2
Understand the morphological analysis of wali
Examine the two possible meanings of 'wali' (active vs. passive participle) and Ibn Abd al-Salam's preference for the active meaning.
3
Study the two definitions from Sa'd and Sayyid Sharif
Compare the definitions: al-Sa'd emphasizes constant worship and knowledge; al-Sayyid al-Sharif emphasizes annihilation of the self (fana').
Each definition aligns with one of the two meanings.
4
Grasp the criterion for the most honorable believer
Learn that honor is based on obedience (taqwa) and following the Quran, with proofs from Surat al-Hujurat and the hadith of Ibn Abbas.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والمؤمنون كلهم أولياء الرحمن، وأكرمهم أطوعهم وأتبعهم للقرآن. (والمؤمنون) بالتقوى كما في بعض نسخ المتن (كلهم أولياء الرحمن) جل وعلا؛ قال تعالى: (إِن أَوْلِيَاؤُهُ إِلَّا الْمُتَّقُونَ) [سورة الأنفال آية: ٣٤]، والأولياء جمع ولي بوزن فعيل بمعنى مفعول كقتيل بمعنى مقتول، أو بمعنى فاعل كعليم بمعنى عالم؛ قال ابن عبد السلام وكونه بمعنى فاعل أرجح؛ لأن الإنسان لا يمدح إلا على فعل نفسه، وقد مدحهم الله تعالى اهـ؛ فعلى الأول يكون الولي من تولى الله رعايته وحفظه فلا يكله إلى نفسه كما قال تعالى: (وَهُوَ يَتَوَلّى الصَّلِحِينَ) [سورة الأعراف آية: ١٩٦]، وعلى الثاني يكون الولي من تولى عبادة الله وطاعته فهو يأتي بها على التوالي آناء الليل وأطراف النهار، ويجنح إلى هذا ما عرَّفه به السعد في شرح العقائد حيث قال: هو العارف بالله حسب ما يمكن، المواظب على الطاعات المتجنب للمعاصي المعرض عن الانهماك باللذات والشهوات، وإلى الأول ما عرف به السيد الشريف حيث قال: «الولاية هي قيام العبد بالحق عند الفناء عن نفسه». وأكرمهم) عنده تعالى (أطوعهم) وأتقاهم له؛ قال تعالى: ﴿إِنَّ أَكْرَمَكُمْ عِندَ اللَّهِ أَتْقَاكُمْ) [سورة الحجرات آية: ۱۳] (وأتبعهم للقرآن)؛ قال تعالى: (فِيهِ هُدًى لِلْمُتَّقِينَ ) (سورة البقرة آية: ٢]، وعن ابن عباس : تكفل الله تعالى لمن قرأ القرآن وعمل بما فيه بألا يضل في الدنيا ولا يشقى في العقبي ثم قرأ: (فَمَنِ اتَّبَعَ هُدَايَ فَلَا يَضِلُّ وَلَا يَشْقَى ) [سورة طه آية: ۱۲۳].
And the believers, all of them, are the friends (awliya) of the Most Merciful, and the most honorable of them are the most obedient and the most followed of the Quran. 'And the believers' (with taqwa) as in some copies of the text, 'all of them are the friends of the Most Merciful', Exalted and Glorified; He said: 'His friends are only the righteous' [Quran 8:34]. And 'awliya' is the plural of 'wali' on the pattern of fa'eel, meaning the object of the action, like qateel meaning killed, or meaning the doer, like 'aleem meaning knowledgeable. Ibn Abd al-Salam said that its meaning as doer is more preponderant because a person is only praised for his own action, and God praised them, end. So according to the first meaning, the wali is the one for whom God undertakes care and protection, so He does not leave him to himself, as He said: 'And He undertakes the care of the righteous' [Quran 7:196]. And according to the second meaning, the wali is the one who undertakes the worship and obedience of God, so he performs them continuously night and day. And al-Sa'd in his commentary on al-Aqa'id inclined toward this meaning when he said: 'He is the one who knows God as much as possible, persists in acts of obedience, avoids sins, and turns away from immersion in pleasures and desires.' And al-Sayyid al-Sharif defined it according to the first meaning when he said: 'Sainthood (wilaya) is the servant's standing by the Truth when he is annihilated from himself.' 'And the most honorable of them' with Him, Exalted, 'are the most obedient' and the most pious to Him; He said: 'Indeed the most honorable of you with God is the most pious of you' [Quran 49:13]. 'And the most followed of the Quran'; He said: 'In it is guidance for the pious' [Quran 2:2]. And from Ibn Abbas: God Almighty guarantees for the one who recites the Quran and acts according to it that he will not go astray in this world nor be wretched in the Hereafter, then he recited: 'And whoever follows My guidance will not go astray and will not be wretched' [Quran 20:123].
Source pages p. 135

Commentary
This passage explains the Tahawiyyah statement that all believers are awliya (friends/saints) of Allah. The commentary begins by noting that the word 'believers' here refers to those with taqwa (piety). It then analyzes the term 'wali' morphologically: it is on the pattern fa'eel, which can be either an active participle (doer) or a passive participle (one done to). The passive meaning: the one whom God takes care of. The active meaning: the one who worships God constantly. Ibn Abd al-Salam prefers the active meaning because praise is for one's own actions. Two definitions are quoted: Al-Sa'd's definition (from his commentary on al-Aqa'id al-Nasafiyya) emphasizes constant worship, knowledge of God, and avoidance of sins—this aligns with the active meaning. Al-Sayyid al-Sharif's definition emphasizes annihilation of the self (fana'), aligning with the passive meaning as God's care. The passage then explains that the most honorable believer is the one most obedient and most pious, citing Quran 49:13. Additionally, the most honorable is the one most followed of the Quran, meaning they follow its guidance, and a hadith from Ibn Abbas promises safety from misguidance and misery for those who recite and act upon the Quran.

Key Terms
ولي
الولاية
التقوى
الفناء

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Only special saints are awliya of Allah.
Correction: The Tahawiyyah states that all believers are awliya of the Most Merciful; the difference is in degree of honor based on piety and following the Quran.

Checkpoint
According to the commentary, which interpretation of 'wali' does Ibn Abd al-Salam consider more preponderant?
A) The passive meaning (the one cared for by God)
B) The active meaning (the one who worships God)
C) The meaning as a friend
D) The meaning as a disciple

Key Takeaway
All believers are awliya of Allah; the best among them are the most obedient and the most follower of the Quran.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If every believer is a friend of Allah, then you are one of them. Do you live with the awareness that you are under Allah's care and that He is watching your obedience? What would change if you truly believed this today?
?
The most honorable among you are the most obedient and most follower of the Quran. Which of these two is weaker in your life? What is one concrete action you will take starting now to strengthen that area?
?
The wali turns away from desires and pleasures. Examine your heart: is there a pleasure or habit you cling to that contradicts your claim to be a friend of Allah? Will you surrender it today?

All Believers Are Friends of the Merciful
Explanation that all believers are awliya' and honor is by obedience and Quranic adherence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that all believers are awliya' of Allah and that their honor is based on obedience and adherence to the Quran.

Core Idea
Every believer is a friend of Allah; honor comes from obedience and following the Quran.

This passage from the Tahawiyyah creed affirms that every believer is a wali (friend) of Allah, countering the notion that awliya' are only a special elite. The author explains the linguistic meaning of 'wali' and clarifies that the most honored among believers are those most obedient and most devoted to the Quran.

Guided Path
1
Understand the universal claim
The passage begins by stating that all believers are awliya' of Allah. Read the opening sentence and note the inclusivity.
This counters any idea that awliya' are only a select few.
2
Explore the two meanings of 'wali'
The author explains that 'wali' can mean either one whose care Allah undertakes (passive) or one who undertakes worship of Allah (active). See how each interpretation is supported by Quran and scholars.
Ibn Abd al-Salam favors the active sense because praise is for one's own action.
3
Identify the criteria for honor
The passage then states that the most honored believers are the most obedient and the most followers of the Quran. Note the Quranic evidence and the tradition from Ibn Abbas.
Honor is not by lineage or worldly status, but by obedience and Quranic adherence.

And the believers, all of them, are the friends of the Merciful, and the most honored of them are the most obedient and the most followers of the Quran. (The believers) with piety, as in some copies of the text (all of them are the friends of the Merciful) – may He be glorified and exalted; He, the Exalted, said: 'Indeed, His friends are but the righteous' [Quran 8:34]. And 'awliya'' is the plural of 'wali', on the pattern of 'fa'il' meaning 'maf'ul' like 'qatil' meaning 'maqtul', or meaning 'fa'il' like 'alim' meaning 'alim'. Ibn Abd al-Salam said: its being in the sense of 'fa'il' is more preponderant, because a person is only praised for his own action, and Allah the Exalted has praised them. On the first interpretation, the wali is one whose care and protection Allah undertakes, so He does not entrust him to himself, as He, the Exalted, said: 'And He is the protector of the righteous' [Quran 7:196]. On the second interpretation, the wali is one who undertakes the worship and obedience of Allah, so he performs them continually in the watches of the night and the ends of the day. This is supported by what al-Sa'd defined it in his commentary on the 'Aqa'id, where he said: 'He is the knower of Allah as much as possible, persistent in obedience, avoiding sins, turning away from indulgence in pleasures and lusts.' And the first interpretation is supported by what al-Sayyid al-Sharif defined it, where he said: 'Al-Wilaya is the servant's standing with the Truth at the annihilation of himself.' (And the most honored of them) with Him, the Exalted, (are the most obedient) and the most pious towards Him; He, the Exalted, said: 'Indeed, the most honored of you with Allah is the most righteous' [Quran 49:13]. (And the most followers of the Quran); He, the Exalted, said: 'In it is guidance for the righteous' [Quran 2:2]. And from Ibn 'Abbas: Allah the Exalted guaranteed for whoever recites the Quran and acts according to it that he will not go astray in this world nor be wretched in the Hereafter, then he recited: 'And whoever follows My guidance will neither go astray nor be wretched' [Quran 20:123]. (1) Commentary on al-'Aqa'id al-Nasafiyyah, p. 131. (2) Al-Ta'rifat, p. 227.
Source pages p. 135

Commentary
This passage explains the statement from the Tahawiyyah creed that all believers are awliya' of Allah, and that the most honored among them are the most obedient and those who follow the Quran most. The author first clarifies the meaning of 'wali' linguistically: it can be either passive (one who is protected and cared for by Allah) or active (one who undertakes obedience of Allah). Ibn Abd al-Salam favours the active sense because praise is based on one's own action, and Allah praised the believers. Two definitions from later scholars support each interpretation: al-Sa'd gives a definition emphasizing active obedience, while al-Sayyid al-Sharif defines wilaya as self-annihilation in the Truth, which leans toward the passive sense. The author then explains that the most honored believers are those most obedient and God-fearing, citing Quran 49:13 and 2:2. A tradition from Ibn Abbas is quoted to show the reward for following the Quran: safety from misguidance in this world and wretchedness in the next. The passage thus reinforces that all believers share the status of awliya', but their honor varies according to their degree of obedience and adherence to the Quran.

Correction: The passage explicitly says 'the believers, all of them, are the friends of the Merciful,' indicating that wilaya is not restricted to a few but is a general status for believers.

Definition of Iman and Belief in Allah
Definition of iman and its application to belief in Allah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the comprehensive definition of iman as verbal confession, inner affirmation, and submission, and how it applies specifically to belief in Allah's existence and attributes.

Core Idea
Iman is wholehearted acceptance, not just lip service.

This lesson establishes the foundational definition of iman according to the Tahawiyyah. Imam al-Tahawi first enumerates the articles of faith, then defines iman itself as a combination of verbal confession, inner conviction, and submission. He then applies this to belief in Allah, affirming His existence with His necessary attributes.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic and translation once to get the overall flow.
Notice the list of articles at the beginning.
2
Identify the three components of iman
Find where the author defines iman and note the three key terms: iqrar, tasdiq, idhan.
These are essential for understanding iman.
3
Understand belief in Allah
See how iman in Allah requires affirming His necessary attributes and negating impossibilities.
This is the first article of iman.
4
Connect to the overall list
Recognize that this definition applies to all six articles.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَالإِيمَانُ هُوَ الإِيمَانُ بِاللهِ وَمَلَائِكَتِهِ وَكُتُبِهِ وَرُسُلِهِ وَالْيَوْمِ الْآخِرِ وَالْبَعْثِ بَعْدَ المَوْتِ وَالقَدَرِ خَيْرِهِ وَشَرِّهِ وَحُلْوِهِ وَمُرِّهِ مِنَ الله تَعَالَى، وَنَحْنُ مُؤْمِنُونَ بِذَلِكَ كُلِّهِ، وَلَا نُفَرِّقُ بَيْنَ أَحَدٍ مِنْ رُسُلِهِ وَنُصَدِّقُهُمْ كُلَّهُمْ عَلَى مَا جَاءُوا بِهِ.
(والإيمان) المطلوب من المكلف (هو (الإيمان) أي الإقرار (۱) مع التصديق والإذعان (بالله تعالى بأنه موجود بصفاته الواجبة له منزها عما يستحيل عليه. ( وملائكته) بأنهم عباد الله المكرمون لا يعصون الله ما أمرهم ويفعلون ما يؤمرون، وبأنهم سفر الله بينه وبين خلقه يتصرفون فيهم كما أذن، صادقون فيها أخبروا به، وأنهم بالغون في الكثرة ما لا يعلمه إلا الله تعالى؛ قال تعالى: ﴿وَمَا يَعْلَمُ جُنُودَ رَبِّكَ إِلَّا هُوَ) [سورة المدثر آية: (٣١]، وقال عليه الصلاة والسلام «أَطَّتِ (٢) السَّمَاءُ وَحُقٌّ لَهَا أَنْ تَيْطُ مَا مِنْ مَوْضِع قَدَم إِلَّا وَفِيهِ مَلَكٌ سَاجِدًا أَوْ رَاكِعاه (۳).
(وكتبه) بأنها كلام الله تعالى الأزلي القديم المنزه عن الحروف والأصوات (۱)
And faith is faith in Allah, His angels, His books, His messengers, the Last Day, the resurrection after death, and the decree, its good and its evil, its sweet and its bitter, from Allah the Exalted. And we are believers in all of that. And we do not differentiate between anyone of His messengers, and we affirm them all upon what they brought.
(Faith) required of the accountable person is (faith), i.e., verbal confession (1) with affirmation and submission (in Allah the Exalted) – that He exists with His attributes obligatory for Him, transcendent above what is impossible for Him. (And His angels) – that they are the honored servants of Allah, they do not disobey Allah in what He commands them and they do what they are commanded, and that they are the messengers of Allah between Him and His creation, acting among them as He has permitted, truthful in what they report, and that they are beyond count in multitude such that none knows them except Allah the Exalted; He, the Exalted, said: 'And none knows the soldiers of your Lord except Him' [Quran 74:31]. And he, peace be upon him, said: 'The heaven groaned, and it has the right to groan – there is no space of a foot except that in it is an angel prostrating or bowing.' (3)
(And His books) – that they are the eternal, pre-eternal speech of Allah the Exalted, transcendent above letters and sounds. (1)
Source pages p. 136

Commentary
This passage defines the articles of iman as mentioned in the Tahawiyyah and then expounds the meaning of belief in Allah, His angels, and His books. The definition of iman itself is given as 'iqrar (verbal confession) accompanied by tasdiq (affirmation) and idhan (submission). This emphasizes that iman is not merely outward speech but requires inner conviction and acceptance. Belief in Allah is described as affirming His existence with His necessary attributes and negating what is impossible for Him. Belief in angels includes that they are honored servants who never disobey, act as messengers between Allah and creation, are truthful, and are immense in number, as evidenced by the hadith about the heaven groaning due to the density of angels prostrating and bowing. Belief in books is introduced with the statement that they are the eternal, pre-eternal speech of Allah, free from letters and sounds, indicating the Ash'ari position on the divine attribute of speech (kalam nafsi). The passage thus establishes the foundational elements of iman and clarifies key doctrinal points.

Key Terms
إيمان
إقرار
تصديق
إذعان

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think iman is only verbal confession without inner conviction.
Correction: The author explicitly adds tasdiq and idhan, showing iman requires inner acceptance.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what are the three components of iman?
A) Iqrar, tasdiq, and idhan
B) Iqrar, tasdiq, and amal
C) Iqrar only
D) Tasdiq and amal

Key Takeaway
Iman is a composite of verbal confession, inner affirmation, and submission, and it begins with sincere belief in Allah and His perfect attributes.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You say 'I believe in the decree, its good and bad' — but when difficulty strikes, does your heart truly submit or does it complain? What would change if your idhan were real?
?
Look at the gap between your tongue's iqrar and your heart's idhan: where do you feel the greatest resistance to surrendering to Allah's command? Will you name it and repent today?
?
If your iman were to be tested by losing something sweet and receiving something bitter, would your tasdiq hold? How can you strengthen your inner affirmation before that test comes?

Belief in Angels
Detailed exposition of belief in angels.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Islamic belief concerning angels: they are honored servants, messengers of Allah, sinless, and innumerable.

Core Idea
Angels are obedient servants of Allah, carrying out His commands.

This lesson explains the second article of faith: belief in angels. The author describes their nature as honored servants who never disobey, their role as intermediaries, their truthfulness, and their vast numbers, supported by Quranic verse and hadith.

Guided Path
1
Read the description of angels
Read the Arabic and translation, focusing on the characteristics of angels.
Notice the four key descriptions.
2
Understand their role
Angels are both servants and messengers (sufara') of Allah.
They act as intermediaries.
3
Reflect on the proofs
The Quranic verse and hadith demonstrate the countless number of angels.
Consider the imagery of the hadith.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَالإِيمَانُ هُوَ الإِيمَانُ بِاللهِ وَمَلَائِكَتِهِ وَكُتُبِهِ وَرُسُلِهِ وَالْيَوْمِ الْآخِرِ وَالْبَعْثِ بَعْدَ المَوْتِ وَالقَدَرِ خَيْرِهِ وَشَرِّهِ وَحُلْوِهِ وَمُرِّهِ مِنَ الله تَعَالَى، وَنَحْنُ مُؤْمِنُونَ بِذَلِكَ كُلِّهِ، وَلَا نُفَرِّقُ بَيْنَ أَحَدٍ مِنْ رُسُلِهِ وَنُصَدِّقُهُمْ كُلَّهُمْ عَلَى مَا جَاءُوا بِهِ.
(والإيمان) المطلوب من المكلف (هو (الإيمان) أي الإقرار (۱) مع التصديق والإذعان (بالله تعالى بأنه موجود بصفاته الواجبة له منزها عما يستحيل عليه. ( وملائكته) بأنهم عباد الله المكرمون لا يعصون الله ما أمرهم ويفعلون ما يؤمرون، وبأنهم سفر الله بينه وبين خلقه يتصرفون فيهم كما أذن، صادقون فيها أخبروا به، وأنهم بالغون في الكثرة ما لا يعلمه إلا الله تعالى؛ قال تعالى: ﴿وَمَا يَعْلَمُ جُنُودَ رَبِّكَ إِلَّا هُوَ) [سورة المدثر آية: (٣١]، وقال عليه الصلاة والسلام «أَطَّتِ (٢) السَّمَاءُ وَحُقٌّ لَهَا أَنْ تَيْطُ مَا مِنْ مَوْضِع قَدَم إِلَّا وَفِيهِ مَلَكٌ سَاجِدًا أَوْ رَاكِعاه (۳).
(وكتبه) بأنها كلام الله تعالى الأزلي القديم المنزه عن الحروف والأصوات (۱)
And faith is faith in Allah, His angels, His books, His messengers, the Last Day, the resurrection after death, and the decree, its good and its evil, its sweet and its bitter, from Allah the Exalted. And we are believers in all of that. And we do not differentiate between anyone of His messengers, and we affirm them all upon what they brought.
(Faith) required of the accountable person is (faith), i.e., verbal confession (1) with affirmation and submission (in Allah the Exalted) – that He exists with His attributes obligatory for Him, transcendent above what is impossible for Him. (And His angels) – that they are the honored servants of Allah, they do not disobey Allah in what He commands them and they do what they are commanded, and that they are the messengers of Allah between Him and His creation, acting among them as He has permitted, truthful in what they report, and that they are beyond count in multitude such that none knows them except Allah the Exalted; He, the Exalted, said: 'And none knows the soldiers of your Lord except Him' [Quran 74:31]. And he, peace be upon him, said: 'The heaven groaned, and it has the right to groan – there is no space of a foot except that in it is an angel prostrating or bowing.' (3)
(And His books) – that they are the eternal, pre-eternal speech of Allah the Exalted, transcendent above letters and sounds. (1)
Source pages p. 136

Commentary
This passage defines the articles of iman as mentioned in the Tahawiyyah and then expounds the meaning of belief in Allah, His angels, and His books. The definition of iman itself is given as 'iqrar (verbal confession) accompanied by tasdiq (affirmation) and idhan (submission). This emphasizes that iman is not merely outward speech but requires inner conviction and acceptance. Belief in Allah is described as affirming His existence with His necessary attributes and negating what is impossible for Him. Belief in angels includes that they are honored servants who never disobey, act as messengers between Allah and creation, are truthful, and are immense in number, as evidenced by the hadith about the heaven groaning due to the density of angels prostrating and bowing. Belief in books is introduced with the statement that they are the eternal, pre-eternal speech of Allah, free from letters and sounds, indicating the Ash'ari position on the divine attribute of speech (kalam nafsi). The passage thus establishes the foundational elements of iman and clarifies key doctrinal points.

Key Terms
ملائكة
عباد الله المكرمون
سفر الله

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think angels are divine or can disobey.
Correction: The passage states they are honored servants who never disobey.

Checkpoint
What does the passage say about the number of angels?
A) They are few in number
B) They are countless, known only to Allah
C) There are exactly 100,000
D) They are limited to ten types

Key Takeaway
Angels are countless, sinless servants of Allah who faithfully execute His commands and convey His messages.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If angels fill every foot of heaven in constant worship, what does your daily worship look like in comparison? Will you today increase your remembrance of Allah, even by a single extra prostration?
?
Angels are truthful in everything they report. When was the last time you spoke a lie, even a small one? What step will you take to align your speech with their standard of truth?
?
The angels are countless, yet each knows his purpose without deviation. You have a unique purpose created by Allah. Are you living it, or are you drifting? What concrete change will you make this week to fulfill your role as His servant?

Belief in the Divine Books: The Attribute of Speech
Definition of belief in books as eternal speech.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Sunni doctrine that the divine books are the eternal, pre-eternal speech of Allah, transcending letters and sounds.

Core Idea
Allah's speech is an eternal attribute, not created.

This lesson introduces the belief in the revealed books, focusing on the attribute of divine speech. The author states that the books are the eternal, pre-eternal speech of Allah, free from the limitations of letters and sounds. This establishes the Ash'ari position on the nature of the Quran.

Guided Path
1
Read the statement about books
Read the Arabic and translation carefully. Note the key descriptors: 'eternal', 'pre-eternal', 'transcendent above letters and sounds'.
This is a concise but profound doctrinal statement.
2
Understand 'kalam nafsi'
The phrase refers to Allah's inner, eternal speech, which is not composed of letters or sounds.
This distinguishes it from created human speech.
3
Appreciate the transcendence
By negating letters and sounds, the author emphasizes that Allah's speech is unlike any created thing.
This guards against anthropomorphism.

?

Affirmation of Faith in All Messengers and Books
Imam Maydani affirms belief in all messengers and books without distinction.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that true faith requires belief in all of Allah's messengers and books without making any distinction among them.

Core Idea
Faith demands accepting every messenger and book without exception.

This passage is a concluding affirmation of faith, emphasizing the believer's duty to accept all of Allah's messengers and books equally. It directly counters the tendency to selectively believe in some prophets while rejecting others. Let's see how the Imam states this principle clearly.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the inclusive language: 'kull' (all) and 'lā nufarriqu' (we do not differentiate).
The passage is short but packs a crucial creedal point.
2
Identify the two categories mentioned
The passage mentions messengers and books. Observe that the same ruling applies to both: no differentiation.
3
Reflect on the common mistake
Many people think it's acceptable to accept some prophets and reject others. The passage explicitly forbids this. Ask yourself why this is a matter of faith.
This connects to the misconception field below.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ونحن مؤمنون بذلك كله ولا نفرق بين أحد من رسله وكذا كتبه ونصدقهم كلهم على ما جاءوا به من ربهم.
And we believe in all of that, and we do not differentiate between any of His messengers, and similarly His books, and we affirm them all in what they brought from their Lord.
Source pages p. 138

Commentary
This short passage is a concluding affirmation of faith. It declares that believers accept all the previously mentioned matters (including divine decree, the Last Day, etc.) and, more specifically, they believe in all of Allah's messengers without making any distinction among them, meaning they do not accept some and reject others. The same applies to Allah's books—they believe in all of them. They also affirm the truthfulness of every messenger regarding what they conveyed from their Lord.

Key Terms
إيمان
رسل
كتب
تصديق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: It is acceptable to believe in some prophets and reject others, or to accept some scriptures while denying others.
Correction: This passage teaches that true faith requires believing in all of Allah's messengers and books without any differentiation. Accepting some and rejecting others is a form of disbelief.

Checkpoint
What does the passage say about differentiating among the messengers?
A) We differentiate based on their rank.
B) We do not differentiate between any of them.
C) We differentiate between prophets and messengers.
D) We only believe in the final prophet.

Key Takeaway
Faith in Allah requires believing in all of His messengers and books without any distinction or exception.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly believe in all the prophets and books equally, or do you find yourself feeling more connected to some than others? What does this passage demand of you regarding your heart's attachment to each messenger and scripture? Will you actively seek to learn about the prophets you know less about to remove any hidden differentiation?
?
The passage says we affirm the messengers 'in what they brought from their Lord.' Are you living according to the core teachings brought by all prophets, such as tawheed and prayer, or do you selectively follow only those commands that suit your desires? If you were to honestly audit your life today, which prophetic message do you neglect the most, and what will you do about it starting now?

Praying for Rulers and Following the Saved Sect
Maydani urges prayer for rulers' reform and describes the way of Ahl al-Sunnah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the proper attitude of Ahl al-Sunnah towards rulers, the importance of following the saved sect, and the criterion for love and hate that perfects faith.

Core Idea
Love and hate for Allah complete faith.

This passage from Imam Maydani's commentary on Tahawiyyah outlines three essential elements of the Ahl al-Sunnah creed: our duty to pray for rulers for their rectitude, success, and well-being; our obligation to follow the Prophetic community and avoid deviation; and the principle that perfect faith is shown by loving and hating for Allah's sake. Let's study these key teachings.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once through, then read the translation. Notice the three distinct sections: prayer for rulers, following the saved sect, and the hadith on love and hate.
The passage uses a clear structure with 'and' (و) to connect each part.
2
Understand the prayer for rulers
Identify the three things we are told to pray for: صلاح (rectitude), نجاح (success), and معافاة (well-being). Reflect on why these are important for rulers according to Ahl al-Sunnah.
The commentator explains each term briefly.
3
Define the saved sect
Note the description: 'أهل السنة المحمدية والجماعة المرضية' and the command to avoid شذوذ (deviation) and فرقة (division). What does it mean to be upon the path of the true sect?
This echoes the hadith about 73 sects, one saved.
4
Analyze the hadith on love and hate
Read the hadith cited at the end. The author says it is 'حقيقة المحبة والبغض' (the reality of love and hate). How does loving and hating for Allah complete faith?
The passage ties love to people of justice and trustworthiness, and hate to injustice and treachery.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(و) ينبغي لنا أن ندعو لهم بالصلاح أي إصلاح نيتهم وسلامة طويتهم، (والنجاح) أي نجاح طلبتهم في قهر مخالف ملتهم، (والمعافاة) مما هم فيه من ظلم رعيتهم وسيئ سيرتهم. (ونتبع أهل السنة المحمدية والجماعة المرضية) ونجتنب الشذوذ أي الانفراد والخلاف والفرقة عما عليه الفرقة المحقة. (ونحب الله تعالى أهل العدل والأمانة) لكونهم بذي الصفة من الديانة، (ونبغض ضدهم أهل الجور والخيانة) لكونهم كذلك من الظلم والضلالة وهذه حقيقة المحبة والبغض المنوه بشأنهما من صاحب الرسالة بقوله : مَنْ أَحَبَّ اللَّهِ وَأَبْغَضَ اللَّهِ وَأَعْطَى اللهُ ومَنَعَ اللهِ فَقَدِ اسْتَكْمَلَ الإِيمَانَ (٢) .
And it is proper for us to pray for them for rectitude—meaning the rectification of their intention and soundness of their conscience—and for success—meaning the success of their undertaking in subduing the opponents of their creed—and for well-being from what they are in of oppression of their subjects and evil of their conduct. And we follow the Prophetic Ahl al-Sunnah and the pleasing community, and we avoid deviation—meaning isolation, disagreement, and division—from what the true sect is upon. And we love, for the sake of Allah Almighty, the people of justice and trustworthiness because they are of this quality of religiosity, and we hate their opposites, the people of injustice and treachery, because they are likewise of oppression and misguidance. And this is the reality of love and hate whose importance has been alluded to by the author of the Message in his words: 'Whoever loves for Allah and hates for Allah and gives for Allah and withholds for Allah has completed faith.'
Source pages p. 149

Commentary
This passage enumerates the proper attitude of Ahl al-Sunnah towards rulers and the defining characteristics of the saved sect. It begins with the duty to pray for rulers—not against them—asking for three things: rectitude (sincerity and sound intention), success (victory over their enemies), and well-being (freedom from oppressing subjects and evil conduct). Then it states that Ahl al-Sunnah follow the creed and communal practice of the Prophet's Companions and the early community, and they avoid deviant paths such as isolation from the community, disagreement with it, and sectarian division—remaining steadfast upon the path of the true sect. Finally, it defines love and hate for Allah's sake as the essence of faith: loving those who are just and trustworthy because of their religious conduct, and hating those who are unjust and treacherous because of their sin and misguidance. The author supports this with a hadith where the Prophet (peace be upon him) states that whoever loves, hates, gives, and withholds for Allah has perfected his iman. This passage thus integrates political loyalty with religious principle and clarifies that love and hate must be based on the person's adherence to or violation of divine commands.

Key Terms
صلاح
نجاح
معافاة
أهل السنة والجماعة
شذوذ
فرقة
حب
بغض
إيمان

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some believe that loving for Allah means indiscriminately loving all Muslims regardless of sin, without differentiating based on their character.
Correction: The passage clarifies that love and hate should be based on the person's justice, trustworthiness, or their opposite: injustice and treachery. Love is for those who embody good religious qualities, and hate for those who embody oppression and misguidance.

Checkpoint
What does the hadith cited in this passage state about loving and hating for Allah?
A) It is a supererogatory act.
B) It completes faith.
C) It is required only for scholars.
D) It applies only to rulers.

Key Takeaway
The saved sect prays for rulers, follows the Prophetic community, and bases love and hate on religious character, perfecting faith.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you pray for your rulers, is your prayer sincere for their rectitude and well-being, or do you harbor resentment and secretly desire their downfall? Can you ask Allah to reform them even when they have wronged you?
?
Think of someone you love and someone you hate. Is your love for them because of their justice and trustworthiness for Allah's sake, or is it mixed with personal benefit? Is your hate because of their injustice and treachery, or because of a personal grudge? How can you purify your heart to love and hate only for Allah?
?
The Prophet said that loving for Allah and hating for Allah completes faith. Examine your heart right now: which emotion dominates your relationships? If you had to stand before Allah today, could you honestly say your loves and hates are for Him alone? What is one relationship you need to recalibrate?

Loving and Hating for Allah's Sake
Explanation of duties towards rulers, community, and love/hate for Allah's sake.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Islamic duty to love and hate for Allah's sake, based on religious merit, and how this relates to following the Sunnah and avoiding sectarianism.

Core Idea
Love and hate for Allah's sake perfects faith.

This passage from the Tahaawiyyah explains the proper attitude towards people based on their religious character. It also instructs us to follow the prophetic Sunnah and the community, avoiding division. The key teaching is the reality of love and hate in Islam, as affirmed by a prophetic hadith.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once, then the English translation. Notice the sequence of instructions.
2
Identify the three main actions
The passage commands three things: praying for rulers, following the Sunnah and community, and loving/hating for Allah. Note the criteria for each.
3
Understand the basis for love and hate
We love 'people of justice and trustworthiness' and hate 'people of injustice and treachery' because of their religious character, not personal likes.
This is the 'reality of love and hate' mentioned in the text.
4
Reflect on the prophetic hadith
The hadith states that loving, hating, giving, and withholding for Allah completes faith. Consider how this applies to daily life.
