(ونتبع) أهل السنة) المحمدية (والجماعة) المرضية (ونجتنب الشذوذ أي الانفراد والخلاف والفرقة) عما عليه الفرقة المحقة. (ونحب) الله تعالى (أهل العدل والأمانة لكونهم بذي الصفة من الديانة (ونبغض) ضدهم (أهل الجور والخيانة لكونهم كذلك من الظلم والضلالة وهذه حقيقة المحبة والبغض المنوه بشأنهما من صاحب الرسالة بقوله: مَنْ أَحَبَّ اللَّهِ وَأَبْغَضَ اللَّهِ وَأَعْطَى اللهُ ومَنَعَ اللهِ فَقَدِ اسْتَكْمَلَ الإِيمَانَ.
(And) we should pray for them with righteousness, meaning the reform of their intention and soundness of their inner self, (and success) meaning success in overcoming those who oppose their religion, (and well-being) from the oppression of their subjects and the evil of their conduct. (And we follow) the people of the prophetic Sunnah (and the community) that is pleasing (and we avoid deviance, meaning isolation, disagreement, and division) from what the true sect adheres to. (And we love), by Allah the Exalted, (the people of justice and trustworthiness, because they possess this quality from their religion, and we hate) their opposite (the people of injustice and treachery, because they are likewise of oppression and misguidance. And this is the reality of love and hate referred to by the master of the message (Muhammad) in his saying: 'Whoever loves for Allah, hates for Allah, gives for Allah, and withholds for Allah has indeed perfected faith.'
Source pages p. 149

Commentary
This passage explains the duties towards rulers and the community, and the proper disposition based on religious merit. The commentary begins by stating that we should pray for the rulers' righteousness, success, and well-being. It then declares that we follow the Sunnah and the consensus of the community, avoiding sectarianism. Finally, it discusses love and hate for Allah's sake: we love those who are just and trustworthy because of their religious character, and we hate the unjust and treacherous. This encapsulates the true meaning of love and hate in Islam, as affirmed by a prophetic hadith that such a person has completed their faith.

Key Terms
أهل العدل
أهل الجور
حقيقة المحبة والبغض

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: It is permissible to love and hate for personal reasons.
Correction: The passage ties love and hate to religious merit, not personal inclinations. Love is for the just and trustworthy; hate is for the unjust and treacherous.

Checkpoint
Who are the subjects of love according to this passage?
A) All Muslims without distinction
B) Those who are just and trustworthy
C) The rulers only

Key Takeaway
Loving and hating for Allah's sake is a fundamental aspect of perfected faith, based on religious merit.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When was the last time you prayed for your leaders—truly, from your heart—for their righteousness and well-being? If you cannot remember, what does that reveal about your understanding of duty towards them? Will you commit to making this a weekly habit?
?
Think of someone you dislike. Is your dislike rooted in their injustice and misguidance as defined by the religion, or is it a personal grudge? How can you purify your heart to hate only for Allah's sake?
?
The passage commands following the 'pleasing community' and avoiding isolation. Are you actively part of a community that upholds the Sunnah, or do you stand alone? What one step can you take this week to strengthen your connection with Ahl al-Sunnah?

Wiping over Leather Socks: Evidence and Sunnī Position
Affirmation of wiping over khuffayn with hadith and consensus.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why wiping over khuffayn is a confirmed sunna and how it is supported by textual evidence and consensus of the Salaf.

Core Idea
Wiping over khuffayn is a mutawātir sunna, central to the Sunnī identity.

The issue of wiping over leather socks (khuffayn) during ablution was a matter of dispute among early sects, but Ahl al-Sunna firmly affirm it based on overwhelming evidence. In this passage, the author presents the creedal statement and then marshals multiple proofs from the Companions, the imams, and the consensus of the Salaf. Understanding this demonstrates how practical rulings are grounded in transmitted authority.

Guided Path
1
Read the creedal statement
Begin by reading the opening line: 'We consider wiping over the leather socks in travel and residence as has come in the tradition.' Note that it covers both travel and residence.
This phrase sets the standard Sunnī position.
2
Identify the supporting evidences
The passage then lists several proofs: the testimony of seventy Companions via al-Ḥasan al-Baṣrī, the forty ḥadīth mentioned by Imam Aḥmad, the statement of al-Karkhī about tawātur, and the stance of Abū Ḥanīfa who required clear evidence.
Each evidence reinforces the authenticity of the practice.
3
Connect to the definition of Ahl al-Sunna
Read the final part where Abū Ḥanīfa includes wiping over khuffayn as one of three pillars of the Sunnī madhhab. Reflect on how this practice became a litmus test for orthodoxy.
This shows the issue's theological importance.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ونرى المسح على الخفين في السفر والحضر كما جاء في الأثر.
ونرى المسح على الخفين) جائزا (في السفر والحضر كما جاء فعل الشارع لـه (في الأثر)؛ روي عن الحسن البصري (١) أنه قال: حدثني سبعون رجلا من أصحاب النبي أنه مسح على الخفين، وعن الإمام أحمد: ليس في قلبي من المسح شيء، فيه أربعون حديثًا عن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم ما رفعوا وما وقفوا، وقال الكرخي: أخاف الكفر على من لم ير المسح على الخفين؛ لأن الآثار جاءت فيه في حيز التواتر»، وعن أبي حنيفة: ما قلت حتى جاءني فيه مثل ضوء النهار، «ما وروي عنه أنه سئل عن مذهب أهل السنة والجماعة فقال: هو أن تفضل الشيخين (۲) وأن تحب الختنين (۳) وأن ترى المسح على الخفين». كذا في شرح المنية، وروي نحوه عن الإمام مالك.
(۱) الحسن بن أبي الحسن يسار البصري، أبو سعيد من سادات التابعين وكبرائهم، ولد لتين بقيتا من خلافة عمر ورأى عثمان وطلحة والكبار وروى عن الصحابة وروى عنه خلق كثير وجمع كل فن من علم وزهد وورع وعبادة، توفي سنة ١١٠ هـ.
انظر ترجمته في طبقات الحفاظ ص (٣٥)، سير أعلام النبلاء (٥٦٣/٤).
(۲) هما أبو بكر وعمرية.
(۳) هما عثمان وعلي .
And we consider wiping over the leather socks (al-khuffayn) in travel and residence as has come in the tradition (al-athar). And we consider wiping over the leather socks permissible in travel and residence as the action of the Lawgiver came for it in the tradition. It is narrated from al-Hasan al-Basri (1) that he said: seventy men from the companions of the Prophet narrated to me that he wiped over the leather socks. And from Imam Ahmad: there is nothing in my heart concerning wiping; forty hadith on it from the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, whether raised (marfu') or stopped (mawquf). And al-Karkhi said: I fear disbelief (kufr) for one who does not consider wiping over the leather socks, because the traditions have come concerning it to the level of tawatur. And from Abu Hanifa: I did not speak until like the light of day came to me concerning it. And it is narrated that he was asked about the madhhab of Ahl al-Sunna wal-Jama'a and he said: it is that you give preference to the two shaykhs (2), and that you love the two sons-in-law (3), and that you consider wiping over the leather socks. Thus in Sharh al-Munya, and similar is narrated from Imam Malik. (1) al-Hasan ibn Abi al-Hasan Yasar al-Basri, Abu Sa'id, from the leaders of the Tabi'un and their great ones, born two years remaining from the caliphate of 'Umar, saw 'Uthman, Talha, and the great ones, narrated from the Companions, and many narrated from him, he combined every field of knowledge, asceticism, piety, and worship, died in the year 110 AH. See his biography in Tabaqat al-Huffaz p. 35, Siyar A'lam al-Nubala' 4/563. (2) They are Abu Bakr and 'Umar. (3) They are 'Uthman and 'Ali.
Source pages p. 150

Commentary
This passage is a definition and proof of the Sunni position on wiping over leather socks (khuffayn). It begins by citing the matn: 'We consider wiping over the leather socks in travel and residence as has come in the tradition.' The commentator explains that this means the practice is permissible, as established by the Prophet's action. Evidence is then marshalled: 1) Al-Hasan al-Basri reports from seventy Companions that the Prophet wiped over khuffayn. 2) Imam Ahmad notes there are forty hadith on the subject, both marfu' and mawquf. 3) Al-Karkhi states that denying it approaches kufr because the reports are mutawatir. 4) Abu Hanifa himself only ruled after clear evidence. 5) A statement attributed to Abu Hanifa defines the madhhab of Ahl al-Sunna as including preference for Abu Bakr and 'Umar, love for 'Uthman and 'Ali, and upholding wiping over khuffayn. The passage also notes a similar statement from Imam Malik. The footnotes provide brief biographies and identifications of the figures mentioned, confirming the scholarly chain of transmission.

Correction: The passage clearly states it is for both travel and residence and presents numerous hadith and consensus, making it a confirmed sunna.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
Al-Karkhi feared kufr for one who denies this practice based on tawatur. Does your heart tremble at the thought of dismissing a mutawātir sunna? Examine your own attitude towards the sunna—are you selective in following it based on convenience or peer approval?
?
Abu Hanifa said he did not speak until the evidence was like daylight. Do you speak about matters of the religion without such certainty? How can you increase your reliance on clear evidence from the Quran and sunna before forming opinions about religious practices?

Hajj and Jihad Are Obligations with Every Ruler
The author affirms that Hajj and jihad remain obligatory with just and unjust rulers.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that Hajj and jihad remain obligatory regardless of the ruler's moral character, based on consensus and prophetic evidence.

Core Idea
The ruler's piety is not a condition for the validity of Hajj and jihad.

The author of the Tahawiyyah affirms a crucial principle: the obligations of Hajj and jihad are not contingent on the ruler being just. This passage explains why these acts of worship remain valid and rewardable under any Muslim ruler, drawing on the practice of the Salaf and a prophetic hadith.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic matn and commentary together. Notice the strong affirmation: 'nothing invalidates them and nothing nullifies them.'
The passage includes both the core statement and its supporting evidence.
2
Identify the two main proofs
Locate the consensus (ijma') of the Salaf and the hadith about horses. Understand how each proof supports the ruling.
3
Reflect on the implication
Think about why this principle is important for the unity of the Muslim community and the continuity of religious obligations.
This connects to the broader Sunni position on obedience to rulers.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَالَجُ وَالجِهَادُ فَرْضَانِ مَاضِيَانِ مَعَ أُولِي الأَمْرِ مِنْ أَئِمَّةِ المُسْلِمِينَ بَرِّهِمْ وَفَاجِرِهِمْ لَا يُبْطِلُهُمَا شَيْءٌ وَلَا يَنْقُضُهُما .
(و) نقول: (الحج والجهاد في سبيل الله تعالى (فرضان ثابتان (ماضیان) مع الصحة (مع أولي الأمر من أئمة المسلمين برهم) أي عادلهم (وفاجرهم) أي ظالمهم (لا يبطلهما شيء من ذلك الظلم (ولا ينقضها)؛ لأن بر الإمام ليس بشرط لصحتها، وقد كان السلف من الصحابة والتابعين يحجون ويجاهدون مع كل إمام بر أو فاجر من غير نكير؛ فكان ذلك إجماعا، وفي صحيح البخاري في باب الجهاد ماضي مع البر والفاجر لقول النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم «الخَيْلُ مَعْقُودٌ بِنَوَاصِيها الخَيْرُ إِلَى يَومِ القِيَامَةِ (۱)۲۱(۳)، قال القسطلان (۳): وذكـر بـقـاء الخير في نــواصي الخيل إلى يوم القيامة وفرة بالأجر، والمغنم المقترن بالأجر إنما يكون بالجهاد، ولم يقيد ذلك بما إذا كان الإمام عادلا؛ فدل على أنه لا فرق في حصول هذا الفضل بين أن يكون الغزو مع الإمام العادل أو الجائر، وأن الإسلام باقي وأهله إلى يوم القيامة؛ لأن من لازم بقاء الجهاد بقاء المجاهدين وهم المسلمون.
(۱) متفق عليه؛ أخرجه البخاري في كتاب الجهاد والسير، باب الخيل معقود في نواصيها الخير حديث رقم (٢٨٥٠)، ومسلم في كتاب الإمارة، باب الخيل في نواصيها الخير حديث رقم (۱۸۷۳)، عن عروة بن الجعد، وعن غيره في أماكن أخر.
(۲) صحيح البخاري، كتاب الجهاد والسير .
(۳) أحمد بن محمد بن أبي بكر بن عبد الملك، أبو العباس شهاب الدين القسطلاني المصري الشافعي الإمام العلامة الحجة الفقيه المقرئ المسند أخذ عن الشيخ خالد الأزهري والشاوي وغيرهما، من تصانيفه: إرشاد الساري تشرح صحيح البخاري ولطائف الإشارات في علم القراءات والمواهب اللدنية، توفي سنة ٩٢٣هـ. انظر ترجمته في الضوء اللامع (١٠٣/٢-١٠٤) ، شذرات الذهب (١٦٩/١٠-١٧١).
And Hajj and jihad are two continuous obligations with those in authority from the Muslim rulers, their righteous and their sinful; nothing invalidates them and nothing nullifies them. (And) we say: (Hajj and jihad in the path of Allah the Exalted are two confirmed obligations (continuous) with validity, (with those in authority from the Muslim rulers, their righteous) i.e. their just, (and their sinful) i.e. their unjust; (nothing invalidates them) nothing of that injustice (and nothing nullifies them). Because the righteousness of the ruler is not a condition for their validity. And the Salaf from the Companions and the Followers used to perform Hajj and jihad with every ruler, righteous or sinful, without any objection; thus that was consensus. And in Sahih al-Bukhari, in the chapter of jihad being continuous with the righteous and the sinful, due to the saying of the Prophet, may Allah bless him and grant him peace: 'The horses have goodness tied to their forelocks until the Day of Resurrection.' (1) 2 1 (3). Al-Qastalani (3) said: The mention of the continuance of goodness in the forelocks of horses until the Day of Resurrection indicates an abundance of reward, and the spoils linked to the reward come only through jihad, and he did not restrict that to when the ruler is just. Thus it indicates that there is no difference in obtaining this virtue between fighting with a just ruler or an unjust one, and that Islam and its people remain until the Day of Resurrection, because from the necessities of the continuance of jihad is the continuance of the mujahideen, and they are the Muslims. (1) Agreed upon; al-Bukhari narrated it in the Book of Jihad and Military Expeditions, Chapter: Horses have goodness tied to their forelocks, hadith number 2850; Muslim in the Book of Leadership, Chapter: Horses have goodness tied to their forelocks, hadith number 1873, from 'Urwa ibn al-Ja'd, and from others in other places. (2) Sahih al-Bukhari, Book of Jihad and Military Expeditions. (3) Ahmad ibn Muhammad ibn Abi Bakr ibn 'Abd al-Malik, Abu al-'Abbas Shihab al-Din al-Qastalani al-Misri al-Shafi'i, the imam, the scholar, the proof, the jurist, the reciter, the musnid; he studied under Shaykh Khalid al-Azhari, al-Shawi, and others. Among his works are: Irshad al-Sari fi Sharh Sahih al-Bukhari, Lata'if al-Isharat fi 'Ilm al-Qira'at, and al-Mawahib al-Laduniyya. He died in the year 923 AH. See his biography in al-Daw' al-Lami' 2/103-104, Shadharat al-Dhahab 10/169-171.
Source pages p. 151

Commentary
This passage is a doctrinal declaration affirming that Hajj and jihad remain obligatory acts of worship regardless of the moral character of the Muslim ruler. It first presents the matn: 'Hajj and jihad are two continuous obligations with those in authority from the Muslim rulers, their righteous and their sinful; nothing invalidates them and nothing nullifies them.' The commentary then expands: the righteousness (birr) of the ruler is not a condition for the validity of these acts. The Salaf (Companions and Followers) consistently performed Hajj and jihad under both just and unjust rulers without objection, establishing consensus (ijma'). Evidence from Sahih al-Bukhari is cited: the hadith that 'the horses have goodness tied to their forelocks until the Day of Resurrection' – this hadith promises reward for jihad without conditioning it on the ruler's justice. Al-Qastalani's interpretation is then quoted to reinforce that the reward and virtue of jihad are not restricted to just leadership. The passage concludes that the permanence of jihad implies the permanence of Muslims, affirming the continuity of Islam. The footnotes provide hadith references and a biography of al-Qastalani.

Benefit of Prayer and Charity for the Dead
Affirms benefit of prayer and charity for the dead, refuting Mu'tazila

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the Sunni position holds that the living's prayer and charity benefit the dead, and how the evidence from hadith refutes the Mu'tazila objection.

Core Idea
The living can benefit the dead through supplication and charity.

The Mu'tazila argued that each soul is responsible only for its own deeds, so prayer and charity cannot help the dead. But the Sunni tradition, based on the Qur'an and hadith, affirms that Allah accepts intercession and charity on behalf of the deceased. This passage presents key evidence from the prophetic practice to establish this benefit.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Mu'tazila argument
Read the passage and note the three reasons the Mu'tazila give for denying benefit: the decree does not change, each soul is pledged, a person is rewarded only for their own deeds.
2
Examine the first evidence: funeral prayer
Notice that the author points to the practice of praying for the dead in the funeral prayer, which has been transmitted by the salaf. If there were no benefit, this practice would be meaningless.
This is a logical argument based on transmitted practice.
3
Study the hadith of one hundred intercessors
The Prophet said that if a hundred Muslims pray for a dead person, their intercession is accepted. This directly shows benefit.
4
Consider the story of Sa'd's well
When Sa'd asked which charity is best for his mother, the Prophet answered 'water'. Sa'd dug a well and dedicated it to her, showing that charity benefits the dead.
5
Appreciate the abundance of evidence
The author concludes that hadiths and traditions on this matter are too many to count, reinforcing the Sunni position.
This counters the Mu'tazila objection.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَفي دُعَاءِ الأَحْيَاءِ لِلأَمْوَاتِ وَصَدَقَتِهِمْ مَنْفَعَةٌ لِلأَمْوَاتِ، خلافًا للمعتزلة تمسكًا بأن القضاء لا يتبدل وكل نفس مرهونة بما كسبت والمرء مجزي بعمله لا بعمل غيره. ولنا ما روي في الصحاح من الدعاء للأموات خصوصا في صلاة الجنازة وقد توارثه السلف؛ فلو لم يكن للأموات نفع فيه لما كان له معنى، وقال عليه الصلاة والسلام: «مَا مِنْ ميّتٍ تُصَلِّي عَلَيهِ أُمَّةٌ مِنَ المُسْلِمِينَ يَبْلُغُونَ مَائَةً كُلُّهم يَشْفَعُونَ لَهُ إِلَّا شُفُعُوا فِيهِ. وعن سعد بن عبادة أنه قال: يا رسول الله إن أم سعد ماتت فأي صدقة أفضل؟ قال: «الماءُ» فحفر بثرًا وقال: هذه لأم سعد، والأحاديث والآثار في هذا الباب أكثر من أن تحصى. كذا في شرح العقائد.
And in the prayer of the living for the dead and their charity there is benefit for the dead, contrary to the Mu'tazila who cling to the fact that the decree does not change and every soul is pledged for what it earned and a person is rewarded for his own deeds not for others'. And our evidence is what is narrated in the Sahihs of prayer for the dead especially in the funeral prayer, and the salaf transmitted it; if there were no benefit for the dead in it, it would have no meaning. And he (peace be upon him) said: 'There is no deceased Muslim for whom a community of Muslims numbering one hundred prays, all interceding for him, except that their intercession is granted.' And from Sa'd ibn 'Ubada that he said: O Messenger of Allah, the mother of Sa'd died, so which charity is best? He said: 'Water.' So he dug a well and said: This is for the mother of Sa'd. And the hadiths and traditions in this chapter are too many to count. As in Sharh al-'Aqa'id.
Source pages p. 180

Commentary
This passage refutes the Mu'tazila position that prayer and charity of the living cannot benefit the dead. The Mu'tazila argue based on the decree being fixed and each soul being responsible only for its own deeds. The author presents evidence from the sunna: the practice of praying for the dead in the funeral prayer, which the salaf transmitted, would be meaningless if no benefit. Specific hadiths include the intercession of one hundred Muslims and the story of Sa'd ibn 'Ubada digging a well as charity for his mother. The author concludes that such evidence is abundant.

صَدَقَة
أَمْوَات
مُعْتَزِلَة
قَضَاء
شَفَاعَة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Only a person's own deeds can benefit them after death; the prayers and charity of others have no effect.
Correction: The Sunni tradition, based on hadith, affirms that the supplication and charity of the living can benefit the dead, as Allah accepts intercession and dedicates the reward.

Checkpoint
What is the primary evidence from the sunna that prayer for the dead benefits them?
A) The verse about the decree.
B) The hadith of intercession of one hundred Muslims and the story of Sa'd's well.
C) The Mu'tazila argument.
D) The consensus of later scholars.

Key Takeaway
Prayer and charity from the living do benefit the dead, as proven by the sunna and the consensus of the salaf.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
Have you ever felt that your charity for the dead is useless? This lesson proves otherwise. Which deceased relative can you give a sadaqa for this week? Write their name and commit.
?
The Mu'tazila argued that only one's own deeds count. Do you ever act as if your deeds are only for yourself? How can you intentionally link your actions to benefit others, living or dead, starting tomorrow?

Handling Reports About the Companions
The author explains how to treat reports about the Companions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the proper approach to reports about the Companions, distinguishing between false and authentic and interpreting the latter favorably while not letting doubt overturn certainty.

Core Idea
Authentic reports about the Companions must be interpreted favorably, following Divine praise.

Before we can discuss the virtue of the Companions, we must know how to handle reports about them that may seem negative. The author provides a clear principle: false reports are ignored, while authentic ones are interpreted favorably because of God's prior praise. Doubtful matters cannot overturn what is certainly known.

Guided Path
1
Read the first part
Read the opening section noting the differing reports about the Companions.
2
Identify the two categories
Notice how the author splits reports into false and authentic, and what action is prescribed for each.
3
Understand the principle
Reflect on why doubt cannot overturn certainty, and how prior Divine praise guides interpretation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واختلفوا فيه فمنه باطل وكذب فلا يلتفت إليه، وما كان صحيحا أولناه تأويلا حسنا؛ لأن الثناء عليهم من الله تعالى سابق وما نقل من الكلام اللاحق محتمل للتأويل، والمشكوك والموهوم لا يبطل المحقق والمعلوم اهـ. وبغير الحق لا نذكرهم؛ ففي صحيح الإمام مسلم: «لَا تَسُبُّوا أَصْحَابِ فَوَالَّذِي نَفْسِي بِيَدِهِ لَو أَنْفَقَ أَحَدُكُمْ مِثْلَ أُحُدٍ ذَهَبًا مَا بَلَغَ مُدَّ أَحَدِهِم وَلا نَصِيفَه، وعن ابن عباس: لا تسبوا أصحاب محمد فلمقام أحدهم ساعة يعني مع النبي خير من عمل أحدكم أربعين سنة، وفي رواية عمره. ونرى حبهم دينا وإيمانا وإحسانا ونرى بعضهم كفرًا وشقاقا ونفاقا وطغيانا؛ حيث كان حبهم من حبه وبعضهم من بغضه مع شهادته لهم بالخيرية.
And they differed concerning it, so some of it is false and lying and is not to be paid attention to, and whatever is correct we interpret it with a good interpretation; because praise of them from Allah most high is prior, and what is transmitted of later speech is susceptible to interpretation, and the doubtful and the illusory do not nullify the confirmed and known. End. And we do not mention them except with the truth; for in Sahih Imam Muslim: 'Do not revile my Companions, for by the One in whose hand is my soul, if one of you were to spend the equivalent of Uhud in gold, he would not reach the mudd of one of them, nor half of it.' And from Ibn Abbas: Do not revile the Companions of Muhammad, for the station of one of them for an hour—meaning with the Prophet—is better than the deed of one of you for forty years, and in a narration, his age. And we regard love of them as religion and faith and beneficence, and we regard hatred of them as disbelief and dissension and hypocrisy and transgression; because their love is from love of him and their hatred is from hatred of him, while he testified to their goodness.
Source pages p. 188

Commentary
This passage addresses how to handle reports about the Companions, then establishes the ruling on insulting them and the status of love and hate. The author first states that differing reports exist: some are false and should be ignored, while authentic ones are interpreted favorably because Divine praise of the Companions preceded any later criticism. Doubt does not overturn certainty. He then quotes a hadith from Sahih Muslim prohibiting reviling the Companions, emphasizing their unmatched virtue. A statement from Ibn Abbas reinforces that even an hour with the Prophet is better than forty years of ordinary worship. Finally, the author affirms a core creedal position: loving the Companions is an act of faith and righteousness, while hating them is disbelief, dissension, hypocrisy, and transgression. This is because love or hatred of them reflects love or hatred of the Prophet himself, who testified to their goodness.

التأويل
المشكوك

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that any negative report about a Companion should be accepted at face value or, conversely, that all reports about them are equally valid.
Correction: The author teaches that false reports are to be dismissed, and authentic reports must be interpreted favorably due to the prior divine praise, with doubtful matters not overturning certainty.

Checkpoint

B) Accept them literally without interpretation.
C) Interpret them favorably.
D) Suspend judgment entirely.

Key Takeaway
The correct approach to reports about Companions is to reject the false, interpret the authentic favorably, and not let doubt overturn certainty.

The author prohibits insulting the Companions and equates love with faith and hate with disbelief.

Learning Objective

Core Idea
Loving the Companions is faith; hating them is disbelief.

Then he states a foundational creed: love of the Companions is religion and faith, hatred is disbelief and hypocrisy, because it reflects one's relation to the Prophet himself.

The Ten Promised Paradise: Testimony Based on Revelation
Affirmation of ten Companions promised Paradise, listing them and citing prophetic testimony.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the Sunni tradition affirms the ten Companions' entry into Paradise based on the Prophet's infallible testimony.

Core Idea
The Prophet's testimony is revelation; we testify only because he testified.

In this lesson, we examine the Sunni doctrine affirming ten specific Companions as promised Paradise. The author cites the Prophet's own words as the basis, emphasizing that the Prophet does not speak from desire but from divine revelation. We'll see the list of names and the special status of Abu 'Ubayda as the trustee of the nation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation to grasp the author's straightforward affirmation. Notice the repeated phrase 'as the Messenger of God testified for them'.
The passage contains two nearly identical statements; the second adds the proof from Surah an-Najm.
2
Identify the ten names
List the ten Companions named by the Prophet. Observe the order and any honorifics used (e.g., al-Siddiq, al-Faruq).
The list includes Abu 'Ubayda with the special title 'trustee of this nation'.
3
Understand the basis of testimony
The author grounds our testimony in the Prophet's testimony, and in the second statement clarifies that the Prophet's words are revelation (Quran 53:3-4). This makes the testimony certain, not mere hope.
This refutes any notion that we only 'hope' for their Paradise.
4
Connect good speech to avoiding hypocrisy
The passage concludes that speaking well of the Companions, wives, and offspring absolves one from hypocrisy. Reflect on why this is a doctrinal marker.
This connects the affirmation of the ten to broader Sunni identity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
في العشرة المبشرون. وَإِنَّ العَشَرَةَ الَّذِينَ سَمَّاهُمْ رَسُولُ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم نَشْهَدُ لَهُمْ بِالجَنَّةِ كَمَا شَهِدَ لَهُمْ رَسُولُ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم وَقَوْلُهُ الحَقُّ وَهُمْ: أَبُو بَكْرٍ وَعُمَرُ وَعُثْمَانُ وَعَلِيٌّ وَطَلْحَةُ وَالزُّبَيْرُ وَسَعْدٌ وَسَعِيدٌ وَعَبْدُ الرَّحْمَنِ بْنُ عَوْفٍ وَأَبُو عُبَيْدَةَ بْنُ الجَرَّاحِ وَهُوَ أَمِينُ هَذِهِ الأُمَّةِ، رُضْوَانُ اللَّهِ عَلَيْهِمْ أَجْمَعِينَ، وَمَنْ أَحْسَنَ القَوْلَ فِي أَصْحَابِ النَّبِيِّ صلى الله عليه وسلم وَأَزْوَاجِهِ وَذُرِّيَّاتِهِ فَقَدْ بَرِئَ مِنَ النِّفَاقِ. (و) نَقُولُ: (إِنَّ العَشَرَةَ الَّذِينَ سَمَّاهُمْ رَسُولُ اللهِ مِنْ أَصْحَابِهِ نَشْهَدُ لَهُمْ بِالجَنَّةِ كَمَا شَهِدَ لَهُمْ رَسُولُ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم وَقَوْلُهُ الحَقُّ، فَإِنَّهُ لَا يَنْطِقُ عَنِ الهَوَى إِنْ هُوَ إِلَّا وَحْيٌ يُوحَى. وَهُمْ: أَبُو بَكْرٍ الصِّدِّيقُ وَعُمَرُ الفَارُوقُ وَعُثْمَانُ بْنُ عَفَّانَ وَعَلِيُّ بْنُ أَبِي طَالِبٍ وَطَلْحَةُ بْنُ عُبَيْدِ اللهِ وَالزُّبَيْرُ بْنُ العَوَّامِ وَسَعْدُ بْنُ أَبِي وَقَّاصٍ وَسَعِيدُ بْنُ زَيْدٍ وَعَبْدُ الرَّحْمَنِ بْنُ عَوْفٍ وَأَبُو عُبَيْدَةَ بْنُ الجَرَّاحِ وَهُوَ أَمِينُ هَذِهِ الأُمَّةِ كَمَا شَهِدَ لَهُ رَسُولُ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم بِذَلِكَ؛ رَوَى الإِمَامُ أَحْمَدُ فِي مُسْنَدِهِ عَنْ عُمَرَ بْنِ الخَطَّابِ قَالَ: قَالَ رَسُولُ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم: «إِنَّ لِكُلِّ نَبِيٍّ أَمِينًا وَأَمِينِي أَبُو عُبَيْدَةَ عَامِرُ بْنُ الجَرَّاحِ». وَفِي الجَامِعِ الصَّغِيرِ رَمَزًا لِلْبُخَارِيِّ عَنْ أَنَسٍ: «إِنَّ لِكُلِّ أُمَّةٍ أَمِينًا وَإِنَّ أَمِينَ هَذِهِ الأُمَّةِ أَبُو عُبَيْدَةَ بْنُ الجَرَّاحِ».
Regarding the ten given glad tidings [of Paradise]. And indeed, the ten whom the Messenger of God (peace be upon him) named, we testify for them [that they are in] Paradise just as the Messenger of God (peace be upon him) testified for them, and his statement is the truth. They are: Abu Bakr, 'Umar, 'Uthman, 'Ali, Talha, al-Zubayr, Sa'd, Sa'id, 'Abd al-Rahman ibn 'Awf, and Abu 'Ubayda ibn al-Jarrah, and he is the trustee of this nation. May God be pleased with them all. And whoever speaks well of the Companions of the Prophet (peace be upon him) and his wives and his offspring has absolved himself of hypocrisy. (And) we say: Indeed the ten whom the Messenger of God named from his Companions, we testify for them [that they are in] Paradise just as the Messenger of God (peace be upon him) testified for them, and his statement is the truth, for he does not speak from desire; it is but revelation revealed. They are: Abu Bakr al-Siddiq, 'Umar al-Faruq, 'Uthman ibn 'Affan, 'Ali ibn Abi Talib, Talha ibn 'Ubayd Allah, al-Zubayr ibn al-'Awwam, Sa'd ibn Abi Waqqas, Sa'id ibn Zayd, 'Abd al-Rahman ibn 'Awf, and Abu 'Ubayda ibn al-Jarrah, and he is the trustee of this nation, as the Messenger of God (peace be upon him) testified to that. Imam Ahmad narrated in his Musnad from 'Umar ibn al-Khattab who said: The Messenger of God (peace be upon him) said: 'Indeed, for every prophet there is a trustee, and my trustee is Abu 'Ubayda 'Amir ibn al-Jarrah.' And in al-Jami' al-Saghir, alluding to al-Bukhari, from Anas: 'Indeed for every nation there is a trustee, and indeed the trustee of this nation is Abu 'Ubayda ibn al-Jarrah.'
Source pages p. 191

Commentary
This passage is an affirmation of the ten Companions who were promised Paradise during their lifetime, based on the direct testimony of the Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him). The author begins by stating that we testify for them just as the Prophet testified, emphasizing that the Prophet's word is truth because he does not speak from desire but from divine revelation. He then lists the ten: Abu Bakr, 'Umar, 'Uthman, 'Ali, Talha, al-Zubayr, Sa'd, Sa'id, 'Abd al-Rahman ibn 'Awf, and Abu 'Ubayda ibn al-Jarrah. For Abu 'Ubayda, he adds a special honorific: 'the trustee of this nation,' and supports it with two hadiths: one from Ahmad's Musnad where the Prophet calls Abu 'Ubayda his trustee, and another from al-Jami' al-Saghir where the Prophet says every nation has a trustee and the trustee of this nation is Abu 'Ubayda. The passage concludes by stating that whoever speaks well of the Companions, the Prophet's wives, and his offspring has absolved himself of hypocrisy—indicating that speaking ill of them is a sign of hypocrisy. This lesson reinforces the Sunni position of venerating all Companions and accepting the explicit promise of Paradise for the ten as a matter of faith.

Speaking Well of the Prophet's Family and Companions
The author states that good speech about the Prophet's family and companions saves from hypocrisy and error.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the obligation to speak well of the Prophet's family and companions according to Sunni creed and why failing to do so constitutes error.

Core Idea
Good speech about the Prophet's family and companions is a safeguard against hypocrisy and misguidance.

The author emphasizes a central tenet of Sunni belief: the necessity of holding the Prophet's family, wives, and companions in high regard. This short passage not only states the doctrinal position but also provides scriptural evidence from the Quran. Let's explore how the author uses the logic of opposites to establish this obligation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic and English carefully to grasp the author's argument.
Notice the concise style.
2
Identify the key groups mentioned
The author lists three groups: the noble companions, the wives (mothers of the believers), and the purified descendants.
These are the Ahl al-Bayt and Sahaba.
3
Understand the logical proof
The author cites Quran 10:32 to argue that truth and error are opposites; therefore, failing to speak well (truth) leads to error.
The verse: 'Then what after truth is there except error?'
4
Reflect on the implication
Consider why speaking well is a requirement, not just a recommendation. It is tied to avoiding hypocrisy and misguidance.
5
Connect to broader creed
This ties into the Sunni emphasis on love and respect for Ahl al-Bayt and Sahaba as part of faith.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
و) نقول: (مَن أحسن القول في أصحاب النبي الأكرمين (وأزواجه) أمهات المؤمنين ( وذرياته) المطهرين فقد برئ من النفاق والضلال؛ لما ذكر الله لهم من المزايا الحميدة والخصال، وقد قال تعالى: (فَمَاذَا بَعْدَ الْحَقِّ إِلَّا الضَّلَالُ) [سورة يونس آية: ٣٢]؛ إذ هما ضدان، وبترك أحدهما يثبت الآخر، والحق ما جاء به الكتاب والسنة.
And we say: Whoever speaks well of the noble companions of the Prophet, and his wives the mothers of the believers, and his purified descendants, has been absolved of hypocrisy and error; because of the praiseworthy virtues and qualities Allah mentioned for them. And He, exalted, said: 'Then what after truth is there except error?' [Surah Yunus, verse 32]; for they are two opposites, and by abandoning one, the other is established. And the truth is what the Book and the Sunnah have brought.
Source pages p. 192

Commentary
This passage is a doctrinal statement about the status of the Prophet's companions, wives, and descendants. The author asserts that anyone who speaks well of them is free from hypocrisy and misguidance, because Allah Himself has praised them in the Quran. He then cites the verse from Surah Yunus to argue that truth and error are opposites—if one abandons truth, one falls into error. Therefore, failing to speak well of these revered figures would constitute error. The passage underscores the obligation to hold the Ahl al-Bayt and Sahaba in high regard as part of Sunni creed.

Key Terms

On Speaking Well of the Salaf and Scholars
The author states that the Salaf and later scholars are only to be mentioned with good, and evil speech about them indicates deviation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why speaking ill of the Salaf and later scholars is a sign of deviation and its severe consequences.

Core Idea
To speak ill of the Salaf is to leave the path of the believers.

This lesson addresses the respect owed to the early generations of Muslims. The author makes a strong statement that only good should be said about them. Anyone who speaks evil of them has strayed from the correct path. This is a key aspect of Ahl al-Sunnah's reverence for the Salaf.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis. Then read the literal translation. Allow the author's directness to sink in.
2

3

The command is clear: they must only be mentioned with good. The consequence for doing otherwise is being on 'other than the path' and ultimately hellfire.
The expansion emphasizes eternal punishment for those who deviate.
4

The passage equates speaking ill of scholars with being on a path other than that of the believers, leading to eternal damnation. This shows the gravity of respect for the Salaf.

Respect for the Scholars of the Salaf
Declaration that Salaf scholars must only be praised.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the scholars of the Salaf must be mentioned only with praise and the warning against speaking ill of them.

Core Idea
The Salaf scholars are to be honored; speaking evil of them is misguidance.

This passage from the Sharh Tahawiyyah emphasizes the duty of respect towards the early righteous scholars. It lists the categories of Salaf scholars and issues a stern warning against any negative mention. Let's explore the passage to understand its implications.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the literal translation to get a sense of the author's words.
Notice the rhythmic structure of the Arabic.
2
Identify the categories of scholars
The passage lists several groups among the Salaf. Find them: the righteous, the Followers, and those after them who are people of goodness, tradition, jurisprudence, and consideration.
This shows the broad scope of Salaf scholars.
3
Understand the warning
The passage ends with a strong warning: whoever mentions them with evil is 'upon other than the path'. Reflect on what this implies about the status of criticizing Salaf scholars.
This is a serious doctrinal point.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَعُلَماءُ السَّلَفِ مِنَ الصَّالِحِينَ وَالتَّابِعِينَ وَمَنْ بَعْدَهُمْ مِنْ أَهْلِ الخَيْرِ وَالأَثَرِ وَأَهْلِ الفِقْهِ وَالنَّظَرِ لَا يُذْكَرُونَ إِلَّا بِالجَمِيلِ، وَمَنْ ذَكَرَهُمْ بِسُوءٍ فَهُوَ عَلَى غَيْرِ السَّبِيلِ.

Source pages p. 193

Commentary
This passage is a declarative statement regarding the scholars of the Salaf. It lists the categories of Salaf scholars: the righteous (al-salihin), the Followers (al-tabi'in), and those after them who are known for goodness (ahl al-khayr), adherence to tradition (al-athar), and expertise in jurisprudence (al-fiqh) and reasoned judgment (al-nazar). The passage asserts that such scholars must only be spoken of in a positive manner (bi'l-jamil). It then delivers a warning: whoever mentions them with evil (bi-su') is on the wrong path (ghayr al-sabil), implying spiritual deviation. This underscores the high regard for the early Muslim scholars and the prohibition of criticizing them.

علماء السلف
الصالحين
التابعين
أهل الفقه والنظر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Constructive criticism of individual Salaf scholars is allowed if balanced with praise.
Correction: The passage states they are 'not mentioned except with goodness,' implying that any negative mention, regardless of intent, is prohibited. Speaking ill of them is a sign of being on the wrong path.

Disavowal of Soothsayers and Fortunetellers
Author defines soothsayer and fortuneteller and states the ruling on believing them.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Islamic ruling on soothsayers and fortunetellers and why believing them constitutes disbelief.

Core Idea
Believing a soothsayer's claim about the unseen is disbelief in divine revelation.

This lesson establishes the position of Ahl al-Sunnah regarding those who claim knowledge of the unseen through soothsaying or astrology. The author clearly states that we do not believe such individuals, then provides definitions and a decisive hadith showing the severity. It also connects to the broader principle of adhering to the Book, Sunnah, and consensus.

Guided Path
1
Read the original text and translation
Read the Arabic passage slowly, then read the literal translation. Notice the clear statement of disavowal at the beginning.
The text uses 'we' to indicate the collective creed of Ahl al-Sunnah.
2
Understand the definitions of kahin and 'arraf
The commentary explains that a kahin informs about hidden things, while an 'arraf is an astrologer or soothsayer; some say the 'arraf tells about the past and the kahin about the future.
These definitions help distinguish between different types of fortune-telling.
3
Reflect on the hadith about believing a soothsayer
The hadith quoted states that whoever goes to a soothsayer and believes him has disbelieved in what was revealed to Muhammad. This shows the gravity of the sin.
This hadith is found in several collections and is considered authentic.
4
Consider the broader hadith on straying from the sources
The second hadith lists those who are cursed: those who add to the Book, deny divine decree, tyrannize, make lawful the sacred, or abandon the Sunnah. This links the prohibition to general innovation.
This emphasizes the importance of adhering strictly to the primary sources.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَا نُصَدِّقُ كَاهِنًا وَلَا عَرَّافًا وَلَا مَنْ يَدَّعِي شَيْئًا بِخِلَافِ الكِتَابِ وَالسُّنَّةِ وَإِجْمَاعِ الأُمةِ. ولا نصدق كاهناً) من يخبر عن المغيبات ( ولا عرَّافًا بالتثقيل؛ بمعنى المنجم والكاهن ، وقيل العراف يخبر عن الماضي والكاهن يخبر عن الماضي والمستقبل ذكره في المصباح (١) ، وفي شرح العقائد وتصديق الكاهن بما يخبر عن الغيب كفر؛ لقوله : مَنْ أَتَى كَاهِنًا فَصَدَّقَهُ بِمَا يَقُولُ فَقَدْ كَفَرَ بِمَا أُنزِلَ عَلَى مُحَمَّدٍ (۲) اهـ (۳). ولا من يدعي شيئًا بخلاف الكتاب والسنة وإجماع الأمة أخرج الطبراني في الكبير وابن حبان والحاكم عن عائشة عنها أن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم قال: «تَةٌ لَعَنتُهُمْ وَلَعَنَهُمُ الله وَكُلَّ نَبِيٍّ مُجَابِ الدَّعْوَةِ الزَّائِدُ فِي كِتَابِ الله وَالمُكَذِّبُ بِقَدَرِ الله وَالمُتَسَلَّطُ عَلَى أُمَّتِي بِالجَبَرُوتِ لِيُذِلَّ مَنْ أَعَزَّ اللَّهُ وَيُعِزُّ مَنْ أَذَلَّ اللَّهُ وَالمُسْتَحِلُ حَرَمَ الله وَالمُسْتَحِلُّ مِنْ عِتْرَنِي مَا حَرَّمَ اللهُ وَالنَّارِكُ لِسُنَّتِي ). كذا في الطريقة المحمدية (٥).
And we do not believe a soothsayer nor a fortuneteller, nor anyone who claims something contrary to the Book, the Sunnah, and the consensus of the community. (And we do not believe a soothsayer) i.e., one who informs about hidden things, (nor a fortuneteller) with tashdid (shaddah), meaning the astrologer and the soothsayer, and it is said that the 'arraf informs about the past and the kahin informs about the past and the future, as mentioned in al-Misbah (1). And in Sharh al-'Aqa'id: Believing the soothsayer in what he reports about the unseen is disbelief, because of his saying: 'Whoever goes to a soothsayer and believes what he says has disbelieved in what was revealed to Muhammad' (2) end. (3). And (we do not believe) anyone who claims something contrary to the Book, the Sunnah, and the consensus of the community. Al-Tabarani in al-Kabir, Ibn Hibban, and al-Hakim narrated from 'A'ishah that the Messenger of Allah (ﷺ) said: '... cursed them, and Allah cursed them, and every prophet whose prayer is answered: the one who adds to the Book of Allah, the one who denies the decree of Allah, the one who dominates my community by tyranny to humiliate those whom Allah has honored and to honor those whom Allah has humiliated, the one who makes lawful the sacred things of Allah, and the one who makes lawful from my family what Allah has made unlawful, and the one who abandons my Sunnah.' Thus in al-Tariqah al-Muhammadiyyah (5).
Source pages p. 197

Commentary
This passage deals with the Islamic ruling on consulting and believing soothsayers (kahin) and fortunetellers ('arraf). The author first quotes the original text of Tahawiyyah: 'We do not believe a soothsayer nor a fortuneteller, nor anyone who claims something contrary to the Book, the Sunnah, and consensus.' In the commentary, he defines the kahin as one who informs about hidden things (al-mughayyabat). The 'arraf is defined with a shaddah (doubled letter), meaning the astrologer or soothsayer. He then mentions a distinction: some say the 'arraf tells about the past and the kahin tells about both the past and the future. He cites al-Misbah for these definitions. Then he quotes from Sharh al-'Aqa'id that believing a soothsayer in his claims about the unseen is kufr (disbelief), based on the hadith: 'Whoever goes to a soothsayer and believes what he says has disbelieved in what was revealed to Muhammad.' This hadith is well-known and indicates the severity of this sin. The text then continues with the phrase 'nor anyone who claims something contrary to the Book, the Sunnah, and the consensus of the community,' and the author provides a supporting hadith from various sources (al-Tabarani, Ibn Hibban, al-Hakim) narrated by 'Aishah, listing those who are cursed: the one who adds to Allah's Book, the one who denies divine decree, the one who tyrannizes the community, the one who makes lawful what Allah has made sacred, and the one who abandons the Prophet's Sunnah. This underscores the importance of adhering to the primary sources of Islam.

Key Terms

عراف
تصديق
الغيب
كفر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think consulting a soothsayer is permissible as long as one does not fully believe their claims.
Correction: The hadith states that merely going to a soothsayer and believing what he says constitutes disbelief, showing that even partial credence is prohibited.

Checkpoint

A) He is a sinner but remains a Muslim
B) He has disbelieved in what was revealed to Muhammad
C) He is considered a hypocrite
D) He is to be given a discretionary punishment

Key Takeaway
Believing a soothsayer or fortuneteller contradicts the very foundation of Islamic faith in Allah's exclusive knowledge of the unseen.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever caught yourself peeking at your horoscope or reading a fortune cookie with a flicker of curiosity? If that curiosity had led to belief, how would you have felt reciting 'Say, None in the heavens and earth knows the unseen except Allah' moments later? This lesson says that trusting anyone but Allah for unseen knowledge is kufr. Can you genuinely claim you never seek comfort from created predictors? What will you concretely do this week to redirect that reliance?
?

If you did, would you have the courage to delete those searches, throw away those books, and confess that you valued a human's guess over Allah's Word? What is stopping you from doing that right now?

Forbidden Belief in Soothsayers and Diviners
Maydani defines the terms kahin and arraf and states the ruling on believing them.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Islamic ruling on believing soothsayers and diviners, and the definitions of the terms kahin and arraf.

Core Idea
Believing a soothsayer is kufr; only revelation is reliable.

This passage from Maydani's commentary on al-Tahawiyyah explains why Muslims must reject any claim to knowledge of the unseen from human sources. It defines the key terms and presents a clear hadith that belief in a soothsayer is disbelief. Let's examine the text.

Guided Path
1

And we do not believe a soothsayer (kahin) nor a diviner (arraf) nor anyone who claims something contrary to the Book, the Sunnah, and the consensus of the community. And we do not believe a soothsayer: one who informs about hidden things, nor a diviner (with tashil): meaning an astrologer or soothsayer, and it is said the diviner informs about the past and the soothsayer informs about the past and future—mentioned in al-Misbah. And in Sharh al-Aqa'id: believing a soothsayer regarding what he informs about the unseen is disbelief because of his statement: 'Whoever comes to a soothsayer and believes what he says has disbelieved in what was revealed to Muhammad.' End. And not anyone who claims something contrary to the Book, the Sunnah, and the consensus of the community. Al-Tabarani in al-Kabir, Ibn Hibban, and al-Hakim narrated from Aisha that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'A [group] cursed them, and Allah cursed them, and every prophet whose supplication is answered: the one who adds to the Book of Allah, the one who denies Allah's decree, the one who dominates my community with tyranny to humiliate whom Allah honours and honour whom Allah humiliates, the one who makes lawful the sanctuary of Allah, the one who makes lawful from my family what Allah has forbidden, and the one who abandons my Sunnah.' Thus in al-Tariqa al-Muhammadiyya.
Source pages p. 197

Commentary
This passage from Maydani's commentary explains the Tahawiyyah creed regarding belief in soothsayers and fortune-tellers. It begins by defining the terms: a "kahin" is one who informs about hidden things; an "arraf" (with tashil) is an astrologer or soothsayer; some say the arraf tells about the past and the kahin about both past and future. Then it states the ruling from Sharh al-Aqa'id: believing a soothsayer is kufr (disbelief), as the hadith states: "Whoever comes to a soothsayer and believes what he says has disbelieved in what was revealed to Muhammad." Then it addresses the third part: not believing anyone who claims something contrary to the Quran, Sunnah, and consensus; and it cites a hadith from Aisha listing categories of people who are cursed, including those who add to Allah's book, deny destiny, etc. This underscores the importance of adhering to revelation and community.

Key Terms
كاهن
عراف
تصديق
تكذيب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Only believing major soothsayers is forbidden; minor fortune-telling is harmless.
Correction: The text makes clear that any claim to knowledge beyond revelation, including from soothsayers, diviners, or anyone contradicting scripture, is prohibited, and believing a soothsayer is outright kufr.

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on believing a soothsayer (kahin) according to Maydani?
A) Makruh (disliked)
B) Permissible
C) Kufr (disbelief)
D) Recommended

Key Takeaway
Believing a soothsayer or diviner regarding the unseen is an act of disbelief; Muslims must reject all claims that contradict the Quran, Sunnah, and community consensus.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever sought knowledge about your future or hidden matters from a fortune teller, astrology, or any other source besides Allah's revelation? If so, what does this lesson teach you about the seriousness of that action, and what will you do to repent and avoid it?
?
The hadith in this lesson curses six groups, including those who make lawful what Allah has made sacred. Examine your own life: are there any practices or beliefs you have adopted that contradict the Quran, Sunnah, or community consensus? How will you align yourself entirely with revelation starting today?
?
Believing a soothsayer is equated with disbelief in what was revealed to Muhammad. Do you truly trust that Allah's revelation is sufficient for all knowledge you need? What specific steps will you take to ensure you never turn to any source of 'hidden knowledge' again?

Clinging to the Community as Truth
Maydani defines jama'ah as truth and condemns division.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the importance of adhering to the united Muslim community (jama'ah) as truth and the severe consequences of division.

Core Idea
Unity is truth and mercy; division is deviation and punishment.

This lesson explores the classical Sunni position on the necessity of sticking with the jama'ah – the collective body of Muslims who follow the truth. Imam Maydani clarifies that the jama'ah is not merely a group but the consensus of the Muslims on correct belief and practice. The Prophet's warning about removing the noose of Islam underscores the gravity of leaving this community.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic and translation slowly. Notice the structure: a statement of belief, a definition, and a supporting hadith.
2
Understand the definition of jama'ah
Identify what the author means by jama'ah: it is what the Muslims have agreed upon as truth and correctness. This is the consensus of the ummah on core matters.
3
Contrast community and division
Notice the pairing: community is paired with truth and correctness; division with deviation and punishment. This highlights the moral and theological valuation.
The word for deviation (زَيْفًا) can also mean falsehood or crookedness.
4
Reflect on the hadith metaphor
The hadith uses the image of removing a noose (ربقة) from the neck. This symbolizes abandoning the bond of Islam. Consider how this emphasizes the gravity of separation.
The noose is a loop that holds something in place; removing it means letting go of Islam's hold.
5
Connect to broader theology
Understand that this teaching underpins the Sunni emphasis on communal unity and warns against sectarian division in matters of creed and practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَنَرَى الجَمَاعَةَ حَقًّا وَصَوَابًا وَالفُرْقَة زَيْفًا وَعَذَابًا. وترى الجماعة أي ما أجمع عليه المسلمون حقا وصوابًا، ونرى الفرقة عما هم عليه زيغا عن سواء الطريق وعذابًا؛ أي سببًا لاستحقاق العذاب روي عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم: «مَنْ فَارَقَ الجَمَاعَةَ فَقَدْ خَلَعَ رِبْقَةَ الإِسْلَامِ مِنْ عُنُقِهِ».

And we consider the community as that which the Muslims have agreed upon as truth and correctness, and we consider division from them as deviation from the straight path and punishment; that is, a cause for deserving punishment. It is reported from the Prophet (peace be upon him): 'Whoever separates from the community has removed the noose of Islam from his neck.'

Commentary
This passage explains the Tahawiyyah article on sticking to the community. It clarifies that "jama'ah" refers to the consensus of Muslims, and that leaving that consensus is a deviation that leads to punishment. The hadith warns that leaving the community is like removing the loop of Islam from one's neck, implying loss of faith or protection.

Correction: The passage specifically defines jama'ah as 'what the Muslims have agreed upon as truth and correctness,' emphasizing that the consensus is on core beliefs and practices that define the straight path, not on all subsidiary issues.

The Foundation of Islam: Submission Over Speculation
Imam Tahawi states the foundation of Islam and warns against seeking hidden knowledge.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Imam al-Tahawi places submission (taslim) as the sole foundation of Islam and how seeking knowledge beyond revelation leads to spiritual confusion.

Core Idea
Islam stands on submission, not speculation.

Imam al-Tahawi begins by laying the epistemological foundation of the Islamic creed. He asserts that true faith is not built on intellectual probing but on humble acceptance. This passage warns against the pursuit of hidden knowledge that can destabilize one's faith.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the English translation. Let the words settle before analysis.
2
Identify the core statement
Notice the first sentence: Islam's foot is established only on submission and surrender. This is the thesis.
The phrase 'on the back of submission' is a vivid metaphor.
3
Understand the warning
The second half describes what happens to those who seek knowledge of what is not established. They are veiled from pure tawhid and sound faith.
4
Reflect on the consequences
Such a person oscillates between belief and disbelief, ending in doubt and confusion. This shows the danger of abandoning submission.
Note the list of negative states: whisperer, lost, deviant, doubting.
5
Connect to your own faith
Ask yourself how submission applies to your understanding of Islamic teachings. How can you avoid the trap of excessive speculation?
This ties the lesson to personal practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَا يَثْبُتُ قَدَمُ الإِسْلَامِ إِلَّا عَلَى ظَهْرِ التَّسْلِيمِ وَالِاسْتِسْلَامِ؛ فَمَنْ رَامَ عِلْمَ مَا لَا يَثْبُتُ حُظِرَ عَلَيْهِ، وَلَمْ يَنْفَعْ بِالتَّسْلِيمِ فَهْمُهُ حَجَبَهُ مَرَامُهُ عَنْ خَالِصِ التَّوْحِيدِ وَصَافِي المَعْرِفَةِ وَصَحِيحِ الإِيمَانِ، فَيَتَذَبْذَبُ بَيْنَ الكُفْرِ وَالإِيمَانِ وَالتَّكْذِيبِ وَالإِقْرَارِ وَالإِنْكَارِ؛ مُوَسْوِسًا تَائِهًا زَائِغًا شَاكًّا، لَا مُؤْمِنًا مُصَدِّقًا وَلَا جَاحِدًا مُكَذِّبًا.
And the foot of Islam is not firmly established except on the back of submission (taslim) and surrender (istislam). So whoever seeks knowledge of what is not established is prevented from it, and his understanding does not benefit him. His quest veils him from pure tawhid, clear knowledge, and sound faith. So he oscillates between disbelief and faith, denial and affirmation, rejection and acceptance; he is a whisperer, lost, deviant, doubting, neither a believing confirmer nor a denying rejecter.
Source pages p. 217

Commentary
This passage describes the epistemological foundation of Islam: submission (التسليم والاستسلام). Imam Tahawi states that Islam's foothold is only established on submission. Then he warns about those who seek knowledge of things that are not established (علم ما لا يثبت) - referring to delving into matters beyond human comprehension. Such a person is prevented (حظر عليه) from true understanding, and his quest (مرامه) actually veils him from pure tawhid, clear knowledge, and sound faith. As a result, he becomes confused, oscillating between belief and disbelief, denial and affirmation. He ends up as a whisperer (موسوس), lost (تائه), deviant (زائغ), doubting (شاك), neither a true believer nor a outright denier. This passage emphasizes the importance of accepting revealed truths without excessive rational inquiry that leads to doubt.

Key Terms
التسليم
الاستسلام
التوحيد
المعرفة
الإيمان
الشك

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Intellectual probing into religious matters is always beneficial and strengthens faith.
Correction: The passage teaches that seeking knowledge of what is not established (i.e., delving into matters beyond revelation) without submission actually harms faith, leading to doubt and oscillation between belief and disbelief.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the result of seeking knowledge of what is not established without submission?
A) It strengthens one's faith.
B) It leads to oscillation between belief and disbelief.
C) It is rewarded if sincere.
D) It makes one a better Muslim.

Key Takeaway
Submission (taslim) is the foundation of sound faith; seeking hidden knowledge without it leads to doubt and confusion.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Where in your life are you seeking answers that Allah has not revealed, rather than submitting to what He has given? How is that quest actually veiling you from pure tawhid?
?
Are there any matters of faith where you demand rational proof before you will submit? In what way does that demand reveal a lack of trust in Allah's wisdom and revelation?
?
Have you ever caught yourself oscillating between belief and doubt because you wanted to fully understand the unseen? What would it cost you today to simply surrender those questions and embrace taslim?

The Middle Path Between Hope and Fear
Imam Tahawi defines the balanced approach to sin and faith.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Sunni position on sin and faith: that believers must maintain hope and fear, avoiding both false security and despair, and that true faith departs only through explicit denial.

Core Idea
Hope and fear are the two wings of the believer's heart.

This passage from Imam Tahawi establishes a crucial middle path. It rejects the extremists who claim sin never harms a believer, as well as those who make sinners despair of Allah's mercy. Instead, it teaches the balanced attitude of hope and fear, grounded in the Quran and Sunnah. Let's explore this foundational creedal point.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice that Tahawi uses a very compact style with multiple negations and affirmations.
2
Identify the two extremes rejected
The passage first rejects the view that sin never harms a believer (false security), and later warns against despair of Allah's mercy. Find both in the text.
These are two opposite errors: one makes sin light, the other makes repentance hopeless.
3
Understand the middle path
After rejecting extremes, Tahawi states the correct attitude: hope for the good, fear for the sinful, seeking forgiveness, and not testifying for Paradise. Then he defines the boundary of faith: only denial removes it.
This middle path is balanced between excessive hope and excessive fear.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَا نَقُولُ: لَا يَضُرُّ مَعَ الْإِسْلَامِ ذَنْبٌ مَنْ عَمِلَهُ، وَنَرْجُو لِلْمُحْسِنِينَ مِنَ الْمُؤْمِنِينَ وَلَا نَأْمَنُ عَلَيْهِمْ وَلَا نَشْهَدُ لَهُمْ بِالْجَنَّةِ، وَنَسْتَغْفِرُ لِمُسِيئِهِمْ وَنَخَافُ عَلَيْهِمْ وَلَا نُقَنِّطُهُمْ. وَالْأَمْنُ وَالْإِيَاسُ يَنْقُلَانِ عَنِ اللَّهِ، وَسَبِيلُ الْحَقِّ بَيْنَهُمَا لِأَهْلِ الْقِبْلَةِ، وَلَا يَخْرُجُ الْعَبْدُ مِنَ الْإِيمَانِ إِلَّا بِجُحُودِ مَا أَدْخَلَهُ فِيهِ.
And we do not say: No sin harms the one who commits it along with Islam. And we hope for the doers of good among the believers, and we do not feel secure for them, nor do we testify for them with Paradise. And we seek forgiveness for their wrongdoers, and we fear for them, and we do not cause them to despair. And security and despair remove from Allah, and the path of truth is between them for the people of the qibla. And the servant does not depart from faith except by denial of what admitted him into it.
Source pages p. 220

Commentary
This passage clarifies the Sunni position on sin and its effect on faith. The author first denies the Murji'ite statement that sin does not harm along with Islam. Instead, he says: we hope for the good doers but do not feel secure from Allah's punishment for them, nor do we testify that they are definitely in Paradise. For the wrongdoers, we seek forgiveness and fear for them, but we do not make them despair of Allah's mercy. Then he states that both extremes—security from Allah's punishment and despair of His mercy—lead away from Allah. The correct path is the middle one for the people of the qibla. Finally, he affirms that a person only leaves faith by denying what brought him into it (i.e., explicit disbelief). Sin does not remove one from faith completely.

Key Terms
إِسْلَام (Islam)
ذَنْب (sin)
رَجَاء (hope)
أَمْن (security)
إِيَاس (despair)
جُحُود (denial)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that believing in Allah's mercy means one can sin without consequence, while others think that sinning expels one from faith.
Correction: The passage avoids both extremes: sin is harmful, but it does not remove faith; hope and fear must coexist.

Checkpoint
According to this passage, what is the correct attitude towards believers who commit sins?
A) They are out of faith.
B) They are safe from punishment.
C) Have hope for them but also fear, and do not despair.
D) They are definitely doomed.

Key Takeaway
The balanced path is hope and fear; sin does not remove faith, only denial does.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you ever feel that your sins don't matter because you believe in Allah's mercy? How does this passage challenge that feeling? What will you do today to balance hope and fear?
?
Have you ever despaired of Allah's mercy after a major sin? How does this passage renew your hope without falling into false security? What one action will you take this week to embody the middle path?
?
Which extreme—false security or despair—do you lean towards more? What specific change can you make in your daily worship to stay on the path of truth?

Definition and Unity of Faith
Definition of faith and its unity with differentiation by piety

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the definition of faith as confession by the tongue and affirmation by the heart, its unity among believers, and the basis for superiority by piety.

Core Idea
Faith is one in essence, but believers differ in excellence through piety.

Imam Tahawi begins by giving the standard Sunni definition of faith: confession by the tongue and affirmation by the heart. He then affirms the truth of all revelation and authentic prophetic teachings. He emphasizes that faith is fundamentally one, yet believers differ in their piety and obedience, which determines their rank with Allah. This passage establishes both the essential equality of all believers and the basis for their distinction.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation once to get the full meaning before analysis.
Pay attention to the key terms: iqrar, tasdiq, lisan, janan.
2
Identify the definition of faith
Locate the exact definition: 'faith is confession by the tongue and affirmation by the heart.' Note that both components are required.
This is the standard definition of Ahl al-Sunnah.
3
Understand the unity of faith
Notice the statement 'faith is one, and its people are equal in its essence.' This means all believers share the same core faith.
The essence (asl) of faith is the same for all believers.
4
Grasp the basis for superiority
Read that superiority among believers is by piety (taqwa) and opposing desire. This explains how faith can be one yet believers have different ranks.
Piety is the measure of excellence in faith.
5
Reflect on the status of believers
Consider the final sentence: all believers are friends of Allah, and the most honorable are the most obedient and followers of the Quran.
This encourages striving in obedience and following the Quran.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَالإِيمَانُ هُوَ الإِقْرَارُ بِاللَّسَانِ وَالتَّصْدِيقُ بِالجَنَانِ، وَإِنَّ جَمِيعَ مَا أَنْزَلَ اللَّهُ فِي القُرْآنِ وَجَمِيعَ مَا صَحَّ عَنِ النَّبِيِّ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ مِنَ الشَّرْعِ وَالإِيمَانِ كُلُّهُ حَقٌّ. وَالإِيمَانُ وَاحِدٌ وَأَهْلُهُ فِي أَصْلِهِ سَوَاءٌ وَالتَّفَاضُلُ بَيْنَهُمْ بِالتَّقْوَى وَمُخَالَفَةِ الهَوَى. وَالمُؤْمِنُونَ كُلُّهُمْ أَوْلِيَاءُ الرَّحْمَنِ، وَأَكْرَمُهُمْ عِنْدَ اللَّهِ أَطْوَعُهُمْ وَأَتْبَعُهُمْ لِلْقُرْآنِ.
And faith is confession by the tongue and affirmation by the heart. And indeed all that Allah has revealed in the Qur'an and all that is authentic from the Prophet, peace and blessings be upon him, of the law and faith, all of it is truth. And faith is one, and its people are equal in its essence, and superiority among them is by piety and opposing desire. And all believers are friends of the Most Merciful, and the most honorable of them to Allah are the most obedient and the most following of the Qur'an.
Source pages p. 220

Commentary
This passage defines faith (iman) and its characteristics. The definition is: confession by the tongue (al-iqrar bil-lisan) and affirmation by the heart (al-tasdiq bil-janan). This is the standard Sunni definition. Then the author states that everything revealed in the Qur'an and authentically from the Prophet regarding law and faith is truth. Next, he says that faith is one (wahid) and that all believers are equal in its essence (aslihi sawa'). However, superiority among them is by piety (taqwa) and opposing desires. So while the core of faith is the same, there are degrees in its perfection. Finally, he says all believers are friends (awliya') of the Most Merciful, and the most honorable are those who are most obedient and most following of the Qur'an.

Key Terms
إِقْرَار (confession)
لِسَان (tongue)
تَصْدِيق (affirmation)
جَنَان (heart)
إِيمَان (faith)
تَقْوَى (piety)
هَوَى (desire)
وَلِي (friend)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that faith is only in the heart or only on the tongue, or that faith does not have degrees.
Correction: The passage shows that faith requires both confession and affirmation, and while faith is one in essence, believers differ in piety and obedience.

Checkpoint
According to this passage, what is the definition of faith?
A) Confession by the tongue only.
B) Affirmation by the heart only.
C) Confession by the tongue and affirmation by the heart.
D) Confession by the tongue and actions.

Key Takeaway
Faith is confession and affirmation, one in essence but believers excel in piety, and all believers are friends of Allah.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

The Six Articles of Faith
Imam Tahawi enumerates the six articles of faith and affirms belief in all without distinction.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the six articles of faith as enumerated by Imam Tahawi and the importance of believing in all of them without making any distinction between the messengers.

Core Idea
Faith requires affirming all six articles entirely, without exception.

Imam Tahawi begins by defining the content of faith (iman) as a set of six core beliefs. This passage lists them clearly and emphasizes that we must affirm every single one, without picking and choosing. It also warns against differentiating between the prophets, a key Sunni position.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then read the literal translation. Notice the rhythm and the list of items.
The Arabic uses 'wa' (and) to connect each article.
2
Identify the six articles
List the six articles of faith mentioned: Allah, angels, books, messengers, Last Day (including resurrection), and qadar (divine decree). Note that resurrection is part of the Last Day.
Some count resurrection separately, but it is traditionally part of belief in the Last Day.
3
Understand the affirmation
The passage says 'we are believers in all of that' and 'we do not distinguish between any of His messengers.' Ask: Why is it important not to distinguish?
This refutes those who accept some prophets but reject others.
4
Grasp the scope of qadar
Notice the description of qadar: its good and evil, sweet and bitter. This means all events, whether pleasing or painful, come from Allah.
This affirms that everything happens by divine decree.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَالإِيمَانُ هُوَ الإِيمَانُ بِاللهِ وَمَلَائِكَتِهِ وَكُتُبِهِ وَرُسُلِهِ وَاليَوْمِ الآخِرِ وَالبَعْثِ بَعْدَ المَوْتِ وَالقَدَرِ خَيْرِهِ وَشَرِّهِ وَحُلْوِهِ وَمُرِّهِ مِنَ اللهِ تَعَالَى، وَنَحْنُ مُؤْمِنُونَ بِذَلِكَ كُلِّهِ، وَلَا نُفَرِّقُ بَيْنَ أَحَدٍ مِنْ رُسُلِهِ وَنُصَدِّقُهُمْ كُلَّهُمْ عَلَى مَا جَاءُوا بِهِ.
And faith is faith in Allah, His angels, His books, His messengers, the Last Day, and resurrection after death, and qadar—its good and its evil, its sweet and its bitter—from Allah, the Exalted. And we are believers in all of that. And we do not distinguish between any of His messengers, and we affirm all of them upon what they brought.
Source pages p. 220

Commentary
This passage explicitly lists the six articles of faith (arkan al-iman). They are: 1) belief in Allah, 2) His angels, 3) His books, 4) His messengers, 5) the Last Day, and 6) resurrection after death and qadar (divine decree) with its good and evil. The author stresses that we believe in all of it, without making any distinction between the messengers; we affirm all of them and what they brought. This is a standard Sunni creedal enumeration.

Key Terms
إِيمَان بِالله (faith in Allah)
مَلَائِكَة (angels)
كُتُب (books)
رُسُل (messengers)
يَوْم الآخِر (Last Day)
بَعْث (resurrection)
قَدَر (divine decree)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some sects deny qadar or claim that only some prophets are valid.
Correction: The passage affirms qadar with its good and evil, and requires belief in all messengers without distinction.

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT listed as an article of faith in this passage?
A) Belief in Allah
B) Belief in angels
C) Belief in the Imamate
D) Belief in qadar

Key Takeaway
Faith requires affirming all six articles—Allah, angels, books, messengers, the Last Day, and qadar—without making any distinctions between the prophets.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
After reading that we must believe in all messengers without distinction, examine your heart: Do you truly honor all prophets equally, or do you feel more connection to some over others? How might this affect your faith in the message they brought?
?
The lesson states that qadar includes both good and evil from Allah. Is there a trial in your life that you have struggled to accept as from Allah? What would it mean for you to truly believe that even the 'bitter' comes from Him?
?
Belief in resurrection after death is a core article. Does your daily life reflect that you are preparing for that day, or do you live as if this world is permanent? What specific change can you make today to align your actions with this belief?
