Major Sinners Are Not Eternally in Hell
Imam Tahawi states that major sinners are not eternal in Hell if they die as monotheists.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that major sinners who die as monotheists are not eternally in Hell, and that their forgiveness is subject to Allah's will, as established in the Qur'an.

Core Idea
Major sinners from the Muslim community are not eternally in Hell if they die as monotheists.

This passage from Imam Tahawi's creed addresses a critical question: what happens to Muslims who die without repenting from major sins? Imam Tahawi affirms that they are not eternally in the Fire, and their ultimate fate is in Allah's hands. The verse from Surah an-Nisa provides the scriptural foundation for this belief.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing. Then read the translation. Notice the strong negative statement 'la yukhalladun' (they shall not be made eternal).
2
Identify the main claim
The passage states that major sinners are in the Fire but not eternal. Note the condition: they die as monotheists and believers, even without repentance.
This directly contradicts the Khawarij position.
3
Understand the role of Allah's will
The passage says they are under Allah's will and judgment. He may forgive by His grace. The verse from an-Nisa supports that shirk is unforgivable but lesser sins may be forgiven.
This shows Allah's absolute sovereignty.
4
Reflect on the significance
This belief distinguishes Sunni Islam from extreme sects that declare major sinners eternally damned or that sin does not affect faith.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَأَهْلُ الْكَبَائِرِ مِنْ أُمَّةِ مُحَمَّدٍ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ فِي النَّارِ لَا يُخَلَّدُونَ إِذَا مَاتُوا وَهُمْ مُوَحِّدُونَ وَإِنْ لَمْ يَكُونُوا تَائِبِينَ بَعْدَ أَنْ لَقُوا اللَّهَ عَارِفِينَ مُؤْمِنِينَ، وَهُمْ فِي مَشِيئَتِهِ وَحُكْمِهِ إِنْ شَاءَ غَفَرَ لَهُمْ وَعَفَا عَنْهُمْ بِفَضْلِهِ كَمَا قَالَ تَعَالَى فِي كِتَابِهِ الْعَزِيزِ: ﴿إِنَّ اللَّهَ لَا يَغْفِرُ أَنْ يُشْرَكَ بِهِ وَيَغْفِرُ مَا دُونَ ذَلِكَ لِمَنْ يَشَاءُ﴾ [النِّسَاء: ٤٨]، وَإِنْ شَاءَ عَذَّبَهُمْ فِي النَّارِ بِقَدْرِ جِنَايَتِهِمْ بِعَدْلِهِ ثُمَّ يُخْرِجُهُمْ مِنْهَا بِرَحْمَتِهِ وَشَفَاعَةِ الشَّافِعِينَ مِنْ أَهْلِ طَاعَتِهِ ثُمَّ يَبْعَثُهُمْ إِلَى جَنَّتِهِ؛ وَذَلِكَ بِأَنَّ اللَّهَ مَوْلَى أَهْلِ مَعْرِفَتِهِ وَلَمْ يَجْعَلْهُمْ فِي الدَّارَيْنِ كَأَهْلِ نُكْرَتِهِ الَّذِينَ خَابُوا مِنْ هِدَايَتِهِ وَلَمْ يَنَالُوا مِنْ وِلَايَتِهِ، اللَّهُمَّ يَا وَلِيَّ الْإِسْلَامِ وَأَهْلِهِ مَسِّكْنَا بِالْإِسْلَامِ حَتَّى نَلْقَاكَ بِهِ.
And the major sinners from the nation of Muhammad, peace and blessings be upon him, are in the Fire but they shall not be made eternal (khalidun) when they die as monotheists, even if they did not repent, after they have met Allah as knowing and believing. And they are under His will and judgment: if He wills, He forgives them and pardons them by His grace, as He said in His Mighty Book: 'Indeed Allah does not forgive that partners be associated with Him, and He forgives what is less than that for whom He wills' [an-Nisa: 48]. And if He wills, He punishes them in the Fire according to the measure of their offense by His justice, then He brings them out of it by His mercy and the intercession of the intercessors from among the people of His obedience, then He sends them to His Paradise. And that is because Allah is the protector of the people of His knowledge, and He does not make them in both abodes like the people of His rejection, who are disappointed from His guidance and did not attain His protection. O Allah, O Protector of Islam and its people, make us cling to Islam until we meet You with it.
Source pages p. 220

Commentary
This passage addresses the fate of grave sinners (ahl al-kaba'ir) from the Muslim community. The author affirms that they will enter the Fire but will not remain in it forever (la yukhalladun) provided they die as monotheists (muwahhidun) who are aware and believing, even if they did not repent. Their ultimate destiny is subject to Allah's will: either He forgives them by His grace, as per the verse that shirk is unforgivable but lesser sins are at Allah's discretion, or He punishes them in proportion to their sins, then brings them out through His mercy and the intercession (shafa'ah) of righteous people. After that, they are admitted to Paradise. This is because Allah is the protector (mawla) of those who know Him, and He does not treat them like the disbelievers who reject Him. The passage ends with a supplication to Allah to make us cling to Islam until we meet Him.

Key Terms
كَبَائِر (major sins)
خُلُود (eternity)
مُوَحِّد (monotheist)
مَشِيئَة (will)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Major sinners from the Muslim community are eternally in Hell.
Correction: Imam Tahawi states they are not eternal (la yukhalladun) if they die as monotheists.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what condition must be met for major sinners not to be eternal in Hell?
A) They must repent before death.
B) They must die as monotheists.
C) They must avoid all major sins.
D) They must perform good deeds.

Key Takeaway
Major sinners who die as monotheists are not eternally in Hell; their forgiveness depends on Allah's will.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you assume that because you believe in one Allah (tawheed), your major sins are automatically forgiven? How does this passage challenge that assumption?
?
Think of a major sin you have committed. Does the fact that you are a monotheist give you a false sense of security about the Fire? What does this lesson teach you about the seriousness of sin and the need for repentance?
?
If you were to die tonight as a monotheist but with unrepentant major sins, would you be content to leave your fate entirely to Allah's will? What does your answer reveal about your relationship with sin and repentance?

The Mercy and Intercession for Believing Sinners
Imam Tahawi describes the process of punishment and mercy for believing sinners, and the supplication to remain on Islam.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that believers who are punished in Hell will eventually be brought out by Allah's mercy and the intercession of the righteous, and that believers and disbelievers are treated differently.

Core Idea
Allah's mercy and intercession will ultimately save believing sinners from Hell.

After establishing that major sinners are not eternal, Imam Tahawi explains their possible fate: if they are not forgiven, they will be punished according to their sins, but then brought out by mercy and intercession. This lesson highlights the balance of justice and mercy, and the distinction between believers and disbelievers.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic and translation. Note the sequence: punishment, then exit by mercy and intercession, then admission to Paradise.
2
Identify the role of intercession
The passage mentions 'shafa'at al-shafi'in' (intercession of intercessors) from among the obedient. This is a key concept in Sunni theology.
Intercession benefits even major sinners.
3
Understand the distinction between believers and disbelievers
Allah is the protector (mawla) of those who know Him, unlike those who reject Him. Believers are not treated like disbelievers in the Hereafter.
4
Reflect on the supplication
Imam Tahawi ends with a prayer to cling to Islam until meeting Allah. This shows the importance of seeking steadfastness.

Negation of the Createdness of the Qur'an
Sanusi negates the createdness of the Qur'an and affirms unity with the Muslim community.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Ahl al-Sunnah position that the Qur'an is uncreated and why it is important to align with the Muslim community on this issue.

Core Idea
The Qur'an is Allah's speech, not created.

In this brief passage, the author firmly denies the Mu'tazilite claim that the Qur'an is created. This position is a foundational tenet of Ahl al-Sunnah. The lesson clarifies this stance and its significance for unity within the Muslim community.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic statement
Read the Arabic sentence carefully: 'ولا نقول بخلق القرآن، ولا نخالف جماعة المسلمين.'
Notice the double negation: we do not say created, and we do not contradict the congregation.
2
Identify the two affirmations
The author makes two points: (1) we do not affirm createdness, (2) we do not oppose the consensus of Muslims. Ask why both are necessary.
3
Reflect on the importance
Consider why the createdness of the Qur'an was a major theological dispute. This statement aligns the believer with the sunni position.
The Mu'tazilah believed the Qur'an was created; Ahl al-Sunnah affirm it is uncreated speech of Allah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَا نَقُولُ بِخَلْقِ القُرْآنِ، وَلَا نُخَالِفُ جَمَاعَةَ المُسْلِمِينَ. وَلَا تَقُولُ: لَا يَضُرُّ مَعَ الإِسْلَامِ ذَنْبٌ مَنْ عَمِلَهُ، وَنَرْجُو لِلْمُحْسِنِينَ مِنَ المُؤمِنِينَ وَلَا تَأْمَنُ عَلَيْهِمْ وَلَا تَشْهَدُ هم بِالجَنَّةِ وَنَسْتَغْفِرُ مِسِييْهِمْ وَنَخَافُ عَلَيْهِمْ ولَا تُقَنِّطُهُمْ. وَالأَمْنُ وَالإِيَاسُ يَنْقِلانِ عَنِ اللَّهِ، وَسَبِيلُ الحَقِّ بَيْنَهُمَا لِأَهْلِ القِبْلَةِ، وَلَا يَخْرُجُ العَبْدُ مِنَ الإِيمَانِ إِلَّا بِجُحُودِ مَا أَدْخَلَهُ فِيهِ.
And we do not say that the Qur'an is created, and we do not contradict the congregation of Muslims. And we do not say: 'No sin harms the one who commits it with Islam'—rather we hope for the good-doers among the believers, and we do not feel secure for them, and we do not testify for them with Paradise, and we ask forgiveness for their wrongdoers, and we fear for them, and we do not make them despair. And security and despair remove one from the religion of Allah, and the path of truth between them is for the people of the Qibla. And the servant does not exit from faith except by denying that which brought him into it.
Source pages p. 220

Commentary
This passage is a creedal statement on two issues: the createdness of the Qur'an and the balance of hope and fear regarding sin. The author first negates the Mu'tazilite belief that the Qur'an is created, aligning with Ahl al-Sunnah. Then he addresses the extremes of the Murji'ah and Khawarij: the Murji'ah say sins do not harm faith, while the Khawarij declare major sinners disbelievers. The author takes a middle path: believers should hope for the good-doers and not despair for sinners, but also not feel secure from punishment. He states that both false security (amn) and despair (ya's) remove one from Allah's religion—i.e., they are deviations. The correct path is between them. Finally, he affirms that a person only leaves faith by denying what brought them into it, i.e., the fundamentals of faith. This refutes those who claim major sin causes exit from faith.

Key Terms
خلق القرآن

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that Ahl al-Sunnah also believe the Qur'an is created, or that this issue is irrelevant.
Correction: This passage affirms that the Qur'an is uncreated and that opposing the consensus on this matter is a deviation.

Checkpoint
What does the author say about the Qur'an?
A) It is created
B) It is uncreated
C) It is both created and uncreated
D) He remains silent

Key Takeaway
The Qur'an is the uncreated speech of Allah, and this is the position of the Sunni community.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you recite the Qur'an, do you truly feel it is the uncreated speech of Allah? If not, what changes in your heart and actions do you need to make to realize this belief? Will you commit to reciting with deeper contemplation starting today?
?
The author affirms unity with the congregation of Muslims. Are there any beliefs or practices you hold that separate you from the mainstream understanding of the early Muslims? What would genuine repentance look like for you in that area?
?
If you were asked to defend the uncreatedness of the Qur'an to someone who doubts, could you? How urgently do you need to study this issue further to be able to stand firm and guide others?

The Balanced Position on Sin and Faith
The author refutes extremes on sin and defines the middle path of hope and fear.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the balanced Sunni position between false security and despair regarding sin, and that only denial of fundamentals removes one from faith.

Core Idea
Neither false security nor despair is the path; the truth is between them.

After addressing the Qur'an, the author tackles the extremes regarding sin: the Murji'ah claim sin does not harm faith, while the Khawarij declare sinners disbelievers. This passage lays out the middle path of hope and fear, and concludes with the condition for leaving faith.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on sin
Read from 'ولا تقول: لا يضر مع الإسلام ذنب...' to the end. Notice the series of affirmations and negations.
The passage refutes the Murji'ah statement that sin does not harm faith.
2
Identify the five actions listed
The author lists what we do: hope, ask forgiveness, fear; and what we do not: feel secure, testify for Paradise, make despair. Understand each.
3
Understand the two extremes
The author names 'الأمن' (false security) and 'الإياس' (despair) as removing from Allah's religion. Why are both dangerous?
They correspond to the Khawarij and Murji'ah extremes.
4
Grasp the condition for exiting faith
The final sentence: 'لا يخرج العبد من الإيمان إلا بجحود ما أدخله فيه.' This is a clear criterion for apostasy.
This refutes the Khawarij who say major sin causes disbelief.

وَلَا نَقُولُ بِخَلْقِ القُرْآنِ، وَلَا نُخَالِفُ جَمَاعَةَ المُسْلِمِينَ. وَلَا تَقُولُ: لَا يَضُرُّ مَعَ الإِسْلَامِ ذَنْبٌ مَنْ عَمِلَهُ، وَنَرْجُو لِلْمُحْسِنِينَ مِنَ المُؤمِنِينَ وَلَا تَأْمَنُ عَلَيْهِمْ وَلَا تَشْهَدُ هم بِالجَنَّةِ وَنَسْتَغْفِرُ مِسِييْهِمْ وَنَخَافُ عَلَيْهِمْ ولَا تُقَنِّطُهُمْ. وَالأَمْنُ وَالإِيَاسُ يَنْقِلانِ عَنِ اللَّهِ، وَسَبِيلُ الحَقِّ بَيْنَهُمَا لِأَهْلِ القِبْلَةِ، وَلَا يَخْرُجُ العَبْدُ مِنَ الإِيمَانِ إِلَّا بِجُحُودِ مَا أَدْخَلَهُ فِيهِ.
And we do not say that the Qur'an is created, and we do not contradict the congregation of Muslims. And we do not say: 'No sin harms the one who commits it with Islam'—rather we hope for the good-doers among the believers, and we do not feel secure for them, and we do not testify for them with Paradise, and we ask forgiveness for their wrongdoers, and we fear for them, and we do not make them despair. And security and despair remove one from the religion of Allah, and the path of truth between them is for the people of the Qibla. And the servant does not exit from faith except by denying that which brought him into it.
Source pages p. 220

Commentary
This passage is a creedal statement on two issues: the createdness of the Qur'an and the balance of hope and fear regarding sin. The author first negates the Mu'tazilite belief that the Qur'an is created, aligning with Ahl al-Sunnah. Then he addresses the extremes of the Murji'ah and Khawarij: the Murji'ah say sins do not harm faith, while the Khawarij declare major sinners disbelievers. The author takes a middle path: believers should hope for the good-doers and not despair for sinners, but also not feel secure from punishment. He states that both false security (amn) and despair (ya's) remove one from Allah's religion—i.e., they are deviations. The correct path is between them. Finally, he affirms that a person only leaves faith by denying what brought them into it, i.e., the fundamentals of faith. This refutes those who claim major sin causes exit from faith.

Key Terms
الأمن
الإياس
الجحود

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some claim that Ahl al-Sunnah either guarantee Paradise for all believers (Murji'ah) or declare sinners disbelievers (Khawarij).
Correction: This passage shows the middle path: hope without security, fear without despair, and sin does not remove faith.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what causes a person to exit from faith?
A) Committing a major sin
B) Denying what brought him into faith
C) Feeling false security
D) Despairing of mercy

Key Takeaway
The middle path of hope and fear is the correct stance, and only denial of faith removes one from Islam.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever caught yourself feeling that your sins are too small to matter because you are Muslim—or too great for Allah to forgive? Which extreme are you leaning toward, and what one action will you take this week to realign with the middle path of hope and fear taught in this passage?
?
The author says that false security and despair remove a person from the religion. Right now, which of these two extremes poses a greater danger to your own heart? How will you actively guard against it, using the specific guidance from the source?
?
If only denying what brought you into faith can take you out of Islam, then your sins do not make you a disbeliever. Does that truth make you more grateful and careful, or does it tempt you to be careless with minor sins? Be honest—what is your inner reaction, and what change is Allah calling you to make today?

The Definition of Faith: Confession and Belief
The author defines iman as confession and belief, and states its unity with distinction by taqwa.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Ahl al-Sunnah definition of faith as verbal confession and heartfelt belief, its unity in origin, and the basis for superiority among believers.

Core Idea
Faith is one in essence, but believers excel by piety, not by degrees of faith itself.

The great scholar Imam al-Tahawi begins by laying down the foundational definition of faith (iman) according to the orthodox Sunni creed. This passage clarifies that faith is not merely a feeling or a set of actions, but a combination of verbal confession and heartfelt conviction. It also addresses the delicate balance between the unity of faith and the diversity of believers' ranks.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and its translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the English translation. Notice the concise style and the key terms.
Pay attention to the phrase 'واليان' – it is likely a scribal variant of 'والبيان' (the explanation).
2
Identify the two components of faith
The passage defines faith as 'confession by the tongue' and 'belief by the heart'. Reflect on why both are necessary.
This refutes extreme positions that reduce faith to only inner belief or only outer action.
3
Understand unity and differentiation
The passage states that faith is one and believers are equal in its origin, but they differ in piety. Consider how this balances unity with moral hierarchy.
This clarifies that faith does not increase or decrease in its essence, but believers vary in their practice and sincerity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَالإِيمَانُ هُوَ الإِقْرَارُ بِاللَّسَانِ وَالتَّصْدِيقُ بِالجَنَانِ، وَإِنَّ جَمِيعَ مَا أَنْزَلَ اللَّهُ فِي القُرْآنِ وَجَميعَ مَا صَح عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم مِنَ الشرع واليان كُلُّه حَقٌّ . وَالإِيمَانُ وَاحِدٌ وَأَهْلُهُ فِي أَصْلِهِ سَوَاءٌ وَالتَّفَاضُلُ بَيْنَهُمْ بِالتَّقْوَى وَمُخَالَفَةِ الهَوَى.
And faith is confession by the tongue and belief by the heart, and indeed all that Allah has revealed in the Qur'an and all that is authentically reported from the Prophet, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, of the Law and the explanation, all of it is truth. And faith is one, and its people are equal in its origin, and superiority among them is by piety and opposing desires.
Source pages p. 220

Commentary
This passage defines faith (iman) according to Ahl al-Sunnah: it consists of verbal confession (iqrar) and heartfelt belief (tasdiq). This refutes those who say faith is only in the heart or only deeds. The author then affirms that everything in the Qur'an and authentic Sunnah is truth, emphasizing the comprehensive acceptance of revelation. He states that faith is one, meaning the essential foundation of belief is the same for all believers—they are equal in its origin (asl). However, believers differ in degree of piety (taqwa) and in opposing their whims, so some are superior to others. This balances unity with differentiation.

Key Terms
إيمان
إقرار
تصديق
تقوى

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that Ahl al-Sunnah believe faith increases and decreases in its essence.
Correction: The passage clarifies that faith is one in its origin; believers are equal in that. Superiority comes from piety and opposing desires, meaning the essence of faith does not vary, but its manifestations and one's attachment to it do.

Checkpoint
According to this passage, what makes believers superior to one another?
A) Their wealth
B) Their ancestry
C) Their piety and opposing desires
D) Their strength

Key Takeaway
Faith is defined as confession by the tongue and belief by the heart; all believers share the same foundation of faith, but their rank differs by piety and opposing desires.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you say 'I am a believer,' do you ever pause to ask your heart if it truly believes what your tongue confesses? What specific inconsistency in your life does this passage expose, and what will you do today to align your heart with your words?
?
This passage says all believers are equal in the origin of faith. Does that give you a sense of security or does it challenge you to examine why you are not striving more for taqwa? Where is one area you have been following your desires, and how will you oppose it this week?
?
If your superiority in faith is measured by taqwa and opposing your whims, not by your claims or outward rituals, then what is one hidden desire you have been making excuses for? Will you confess it to Allah and take a concrete step to oppose it today?

All Believers Are Allies of Allah and the Pillars of Faith
The author declares all believers as awliya and lists the six articles of iman.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that every believer is an ally (wali) of Allah and the six essential articles of faith that define Islamic belief.

Core Idea
Every believer is a wali of Allah.

This passage from the Tahawiyyah establishes the universal status of believers as allies of Allah and enumerates the core beliefs that constitute faith. It corrects the mistaken notion that only miracle-working saints are awliya and affirms the comprehensive nature of iman, including belief in divine destiny (qadar) with both its good and evil aspects.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation once to get the overall meaning. Notice the two main parts: the declaration about believers and the definition of faith.
The passage is concise but packed with doctrine.
2
Identify the two key teachings
First, note that all believers are awliya – this is a universal status. Second, identify the six items in the definition of faith (iman).
The six items are: Allah, angels, books, messengers, Last Day, and qadar.
3
Understand the implications of qadar
The passage includes belief in the good and evil of destiny, all from Allah. This refutes the Qadariyyah who deny divine decree.
Belief in qadar covers both favorable and unfavorable events.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَالمُؤْمِنُونَ كُلُّهُمْ أَوْلِيَاءُ الرَّحْمَنِ، وَأَكْرَمُهُمْ أَطْوَعُهُمْ وَأَتْبَعُهُمْ لِلْقُرْآنِ. وَالإِيمَانُ هُوَ الإِيمَانُ بِاللهِ وَمَلَائِكَتِهِ وَكُتُبِهِ وَرُسُلِهِ وَاليَوْمِ الآخِرِ وَالبَعْثِ بَعْدَ المَوْتِ وَالقَدَرِ خَيْرِهِ وَشَرِّهِ وَحُلْوِهِ وَمُرِّهِ مِنَ الله تَعَالَى، وَنَحْنُ مُؤْمِنُونَ بِذَلِكَ كُلِّهِ، وَلَا نُفَرِّقُ بَيْنَ أَحَدٍ مِنْ رُسُلِهِ وَنُصَدِّقُهُمْ كُلَّهُمْ عَلَى مَا جَاءُوا بِهِ.
And all believers are allies (awliya) of the Merciful, and the most honorable among them are the most obedient and the most followers of the Qur'an. And faith is belief in Allah, His angels, His books, His messengers, the Last Day, and the resurrection after death, and in destiny, its good and evil, its sweet and bitter, all from Allah the Exalted. And we believe in all of that, and we do not differentiate between any of His messengers, and we believe them all regarding what they brought.
Source pages p. 220

Commentary
This passage emphasizes that every believer is a wali (ally) of Allah, contrary to those who restrict wilayah to a select few. The most honored are those most obedient and following the Qur'an. It then enumerates the six articles of faith: Allah, angels, books, messengers, Last Day, and destiny (qadar) with its dual aspects of good and evil. Belief in qadar includes both good and evil, sweet and bitter, all from Allah. This refutes the Qadariyyah who deny divine decree. It also affirms belief in all prophets without distinction.

Key Terms
أولياء الرحمن
إيمان
قدر
ملائكة
كتب
رسل
يوم الآخر
بعث بعد الموت

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think only miracle-working saints are awliya, and that faith does not require belief in qadar.
Correction: Every believer is a wali by virtue of faith, and iman necessarily includes belief in qadar with both its aspects.

Checkpoint

A) Five
B) Six
C) Seven
D) Four

Key Takeaway
All believers are allies of Allah, and faith is defined by belief in six pillars, including qadar with both good and evil.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You are declared an ally of Allah simply because you believe. Does your daily life reflect the honor of being His ally, or do you live as if that status is distant and abstract? What one change will you make today to live more consistently as a wali?
?
When hardship strikes, do you truly accept that its bitterness is from Allah’s decree, or do you nurse resentment against Him? How will you train yourself to say 'al-qadru khairuhu wa sharruhu min Allah' in your next trial?
?
The most honorable believers are the most obedient and the most followers of the Qur'an. Are you content with the level of your obedience and attachment to the Qur'an, or does this truth sting you? What specific ayat or command have you neglected that you will act on from today?

Major Sinners Are Not Eternally Punished
Author states non-eternal punishment for monotheistic major sinners with Quranic proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that major sinners from the Ummah who die as monotheists will not remain in Hell forever, based on Quranic proof.

Core Idea
Monotheistic major sinners are not eternally punished; their fate is in Allah's will.

The Ahl al-Sunnah hold a balanced view on major sinners: they are not guaranteed Paradise nor eternally damned. This lesson presents the core ruling from Imam al-Tahawi's creed, along with the Quranic evidence that grounds it.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic and English translation once to get the flow of the argument.
Pay attention to the condition 'when they die as monotheists'.
2
Identify the key ruling and condition
Note that the author states major sinners will not be permanently in Hell, but only if they die as monotheists (muwahhidun).
3
Examine the Quranic proof
The verse (4:48) shows that shirk is unforgivable, but lesser sins may be forgiven. This supports the possibility of forgiveness for major sinners.
Reflect on how this verse refutes the Khawarij position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَأَهْلُ الكَبَائِرِ مِنْ أُمَّةٍ مُحَمَّد صلى الله عليه وسلم فِي النَّارِ لَا تُخَلَّدُونَ إِذَا مَاتُوا وَهُمْ مُوَحْدُونَ وَإِنْ لَمْ يَكُونُوا تَائِبِينَ بَعْدَ أَنْ لَقُوا اللَّهَ عَارِفِينَ مُؤْمِنِينَ، وَهُمْ فِي مَشِيئَتِهِ وَحُكْمِهِ إِنْ شَاءَ غَفَرَ هُم وَعَفَا عَنْهُمْ بِفَضْلِهِ كَمَا قَالَ تَعَالَى فِي كِتَابِهِ العَزِيزِ : ﴿إِنَّ اللَّهَ لَا يَغْفِرُ أَن يُشْرَكَ بِهِ وَيَغْفِرُ مَا دُونَ ذَلِكَ لِمَن يَشَاءُ) [سورة النساء آية: ٤٨] وَإِنْ شَاءَ عَذَبَهُمْ فِي النَّارِ بِقَدْرِ جِنَايَتِهِمْ بِعَدْلِهِ ثُمَّ يُخْرِجُهُمْ مِنْهَا بِرَحْمَتِهِ وَشَفَاعَةِ الشَّافِعِينَ مِنْ أَهْلِ طَاعَتِهِ ثُمَّ يَبْعَثُهُمْ إِلَى جَنَّتِهِ؛ وَذَلِكَ بِأَنَّ اللهَ مَوْلَى أَهْلِ مَعْرِفَتِهِ وَلَمْ يَجْعَلُهُمْ فِي الدَّارَيْنِ كَأَهْلِ نُكْرَتِهِ الَّذِينَ خَابُوا مِنْ هِدَايَتِهِ وَلَمْ يَنَالُوا مِنْ وِلَايَتِهِ ، اللَّهُمَّ يَا وَل الإِسْلَامِ وَأَهْلِهِ مَسَّكْنَا بِالإِسْلَامِ حَتَّى نَلْقَاكَ بِهِ.
And the people of major sins from the ummah of Muhammad, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, are in the Fire—they will not be eternally [in it] when they die as monotheists, even if they were not repentant, after they meet Allah knowing and believing. They are subject to His will and decree: if He wills, He forgives them and pardons them by His favor, as He said in His Mighty Book: 'Indeed, Allah does not forgive that partners be associated with Him, but He forgives what is less than that for whom He wills.' [Quran 4:48] And if He wills, He punishes them in the Fire according to their sins by His justice, then He brings them out of it by His mercy and the intercession of the intercessors from the people of His obedience, then He raises them to His Paradise. That is because Allah is the Protector of the people of His knowledge, and He does not make them in the two abodes like the people of His denial, who failed to attain His guidance and did not attain His friendship. O Allah, O Protector of Islam and its people, keep us firm in Islam until we meet You with it.
Source pages p. 220

Commentary
This long passage details the Ahl al-Sunnah position on major sinners (ahl al-kaba'ir). They will not be eternally in Hell if they die as monotheists (muwahhidun), even without repentance. Their fate is in Allah's will: either forgiven directly by His grace, or punished proportionally for their sins and then brought out by His mercy and the intercession of the righteous. The author cites Quran 4:48 to show that shirk is unforgivable, but lesser sins may be forgiven. The passage ends with a prayer for steadfastness in Islam. This refutes both the Khawarij (eternal Hell for major sinners) and the Murji'ah (no harm from sin).

Key Terms
الكبائر
توحيد
مشيئة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Major sinners will be eternally in Hell regardless of their faith.
Correction: The passage clarifies that those who die as monotheists will not be eternally punished, even if they committed major sins.

Checkpoint
According to this passage, what is the condition for a major sinner not to be eternally punished in Hell?
A) They must repent before death
B) They must die as monotheists
C) They must not have committed any major sin
D) They must perform many good deeds

Key Takeaway
Major sinners from the Ummah who die as monotheists will not remain in Hell forever; their final abode is Paradise.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

?
Does the promise of non-eternal punishment make you less concerned about committing major sins, or does it drive you to hope in Allah's forgiveness while fearing His justice? How will you respond to this balance?

Divine Mercy and Intercession for Sinners
Author explains the two possibilities and the role of mercy and intercession.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two possibilities for major sinners in the afterlife: direct forgiveness or punishment followed by mercy and intercession.

Core Idea
Even if punished, monotheistic sinners are eventually saved by Allah's mercy and intercession.

After stating that major sinners are not eternally punished, the author elaborates on their fate: either immediate forgiveness or just punishment followed by mercy and intercession. This lesson unpacks that process and concludes with a prayer for steadfastness.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation to see the sequence of events.
2
Identify the two possibilities
Allah may either forgive them directly by His favor, or punish them justly then bring them out by mercy and intercession.
3
Analyze the role of intercession
Note that intercession by the obedient (ahl al-ta'ah) is a means of mercy for the sinners.
4
Contrast with the deniers
The passage contrasts monotheists with 'the people of His denial' who are doomed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَأَهْلُ الكَبَائِرِ مِنْ أُمَّةٍ مُحَمَّد صلى الله عليه وسلم فِي النَّارِ لَا تُخَلَّدُونَ إِذَا مَاتُوا وَهُمْ مُوَحْدُونَ وَإِنْ لَمْ يَكُونُوا تَائِبِينَ بَعْدَ أَنْ لَقُوا اللَّهَ عَارِفِينَ مُؤْمِنِينَ، وَهُمْ فِي مَشِيئَتِهِ وَحُكْمِهِ إِنْ شَاءَ غَفَرَ هُم وَعَفَا عَنْهُمْ بِفَضْلِهِ كَمَا قَالَ تَعَالَى فِي كِتَابِهِ العَزِيزِ : ﴿إِنَّ اللَّهَ لَا يَغْفِرُ أَن يُشْرَكَ بِهِ وَيَغْفِرُ مَا دُونَ ذَلِكَ لِمَن يَشَاءُ) [سورة النساء آية: ٤٨] وَإِنْ شَاءَ عَذَبَهُمْ فِي النَّارِ بِقَدْرِ جِنَايَتِهِمْ بِعَدْلِهِ ثُمَّ يُخْرِجُهُمْ مِنْهَا بِرَحْمَتِهِ وَشَفَاعَةِ الشَّافِعِينَ مِنْ أَهْلِ طَاعَتِهِ ثُمَّ يَبْعَثُهُمْ إِلَى جَنَّتِهِ؛ وَذَلِكَ بِأَنَّ اللهَ مَوْلَى أَهْلِ مَعْرِفَتِهِ وَلَمْ يَجْعَلُهُمْ فِي الدَّارَيْنِ كَأَهْلِ نُكْرَتِهِ الَّذِينَ خَابُوا مِنْ هِدَايَتِهِ وَلَمْ يَنَالُوا مِنْ وِلَايَتِهِ ، اللَّهُمَّ يَا وَل الإِسْلَامِ وَأَهْلِهِ مَسَّكْنَا بِالإِسْلَامِ حَتَّى نَلْقَاكَ بِهِ.
And the people of major sins from the ummah of Muhammad, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, are in the Fire—they will not be eternally [in it] when they die as monotheists, even if they were not repentant, after they meet Allah knowing and believing. They are subject to His will and decree: if He wills, He forgives them and pardons them by His favor, as He said in His Mighty Book: 'Indeed, Allah does not forgive that partners be associated with Him, but He forgives what is less than that for whom He wills.' [Quran 4:48] And if He wills, He punishes them in the Fire according to their sins by His justice, then He brings them out of it by His mercy and the intercession of the intercessors from the people of His obedience, then He raises them to His Paradise. That is because Allah is the Protector of the people of His knowledge, and He does not make them in the two abodes like the people of His denial, who failed to attain His guidance and did not attain His friendship. O Allah, O Protector of Islam and its people, keep us firm in Islam until we meet You with it.
Source pages p. 220

Commentary
This long passage details the Ahl al-Sunnah position on major sinners (ahl al-kaba'ir). They will not be eternally in Hell if they die as monotheists (muwahhidun), even without repentance. Their fate is in Allah's will: either forgiven directly by His grace, or punished proportionally for their sins and then brought out by His mercy and the intercession of the righteous. The author cites Quran 4:48 to show that shirk is unforgivable, but lesser sins may be forgiven. The passage ends with a prayer for steadfastness in Islam. This refutes both the Khawarij (eternal Hell for major sinners) and the Murji'ah (no harm from sin).

Key Terms
شفاعة
رحمة
عدل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: All major sinners will be forgiven without any punishment.
Correction: The passage shows that Allah may punish them justly before bringing them out by mercy.

Checkpoint
What occurs after the punishment of major sinners according to this passage?
A) They remain in Hell forever
B) They are brought out by mercy and intercession
C) They are sent to a different place
D) They are reborn

Key Takeaway
Even if punished, monotheistic sinners are eventually brought to Paradise through Allah's mercy and the intercession of the righteous.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly believe that your ultimate salvation depends on Allah's mercy and the intercession of the righteous, not on your own deeds? How does this belief change the way you repent today?
?
When you see a fellow Muslim committing a major sin, do you treat them as a hopeless case (like the Khawarij) or as someone still under Allah's protection? What will you do this week to show them mercy, following the pattern of this passage?
?
The author prayed, 'Keep us firm in Islam until we meet You with it.' Are you genuinely afraid of abandoning Islam before death? What is one specific habit you will change tonight to strengthen your connection to Allah, seeking His protection from a bad end?

Prayer Behind the Pious and the Sinful
Imam Tahawi states the ruling on prayer behind any Muslim and not judging their final state.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Sunni position on praying behind any Muslim regardless of personal piety, and the principle of not judging a person's final state in the afterlife.

Core Idea
We treat all Muslims as Muslims outwardly; their inner state is Allah's concern.

Imam Tahawi presents a concise statement of Ahl al-Sunna's position on how to deal with Muslims, especially those who may be sinful. The passage covers the validity of prayer behind any person who faces the qibla, the treatment of deceased Muslims, and the prohibition of passing judgment on their ultimate fate. It establishes that outward actions are the basis of our treatment, while hidden matters are left to Allah.

Guided Path
1
Read the full passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation carefully. Note the sequence of statements: prayer behind any Muslim, funeral prayer, not assigning Paradise or Hell, not testifying to disbelief unless it appears, leaving secrets to Allah.
The passage is dense with multiple rulings in one sentence.
2
Identify the five rulings
List the five distinct actions/beliefs mentioned. They form a coherent position on outward treatment of Muslims.
Each ruling builds on the previous one.
3
Understand the principle
The unifying principle is that we judge by the apparent (ẓāhir) and leave the hidden (sirr) to Allah. This prevents us from declaring anyone definitively in Paradise or Hell based on outward sin.
4
Connect to broader theology
This passage reflects the Sunni middle path between Kharijites (who declare sinners as disbelievers) and Murji'ites (who suspend all judgment).
Consider how this affects your view of Muslims who commit major sins.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَنَرَى الصَّلَاةَ خَلْفَ كُلِّ بَرٍّ وَفَاجِرٍ مِنْ أَهْلِ القِبْلَةِ، وَنُصَلِّي عَلَى مَنْ مَاتَ مِنْهُمْ وَلَا نُنزِلُ أَحَدًا مِنْهُمْ جَنَّةً وَلَا نَارًا، وَلَا نَشْهَدُ عَلَيْهِمْ بِكُفْرٍ وَلَا شِرْكٍ وَلَا نِفَاقٍ مَا لَمْ يَظْهَرْ مِنْهُمْ مِنْ ذَلِكَ شَيْءٌ، وَنَذَرُ سَرَائِرَهُمْ إِلَى اللهِ تَعَالَى.
And we see prayer behind every righteous and sinful person from the people of the qibla, and we pray over those who die from them, and we do not assign anyone from them to Paradise nor to Hell, and we do not testify against them with disbelief nor polytheism nor hypocrisy as long as nothing of that appears from them, and we leave their secrets to Allah Ta'ala.
Source pages p. 221

Commentary
This passage is a statement of the Sunni position regarding the outward treatment of Muslims, especially rulers and those who may be sinful. Imam Tahawi begins by affirming the validity of praying behind any person who faces the qibla, whether righteous or sinful. This means that the validity of prayer is not contingent on the imam's personal piety. Next, he states that we pray the funeral prayer over any Muslim who dies, without judging their final state. We do not declare anyone specifically in Paradise or Hell, nor do we testify to their disbelief, polytheism, or hypocrisy unless clear evidence of such appears from them. Finally, we leave their hidden matters to Allah, who alone knows the unseen.

Key Terms
بَر
فَاجِر
أَهْل القِبْلَة
سَرَائِر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some believe that if an imam is sinful, praying behind him is invalid, or that we can judge a person's final destiny based on their sins.
Correction: The passage clarifies that prayer behind any Muslim is valid regardless of their personal state, and that we do not assign anyone to Paradise or Hell except based on clear evidence from revelation. We only act on outward appearances and leave hidden matters to Allah.

Checkpoint
According to this passage, when do we testify to someone's kufr or nifaq?
A) When we know their heart
B) When it appears from them outwardly
C) When they are a ruler
D) Never

Key Takeaway
The Sunni position is to treat all Muslims who face the qibla as Muslims outwardly, leaving their inner states to Allah, and not to judge their final abode.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you see a fellow Muslim commit a sin, does your heart begin to question their faith? How does Imam Tahawi's teaching that we do not testify to hypocrisy unless it appears outwardly challenge you to leave judgment to Allah and focus on your own faults?
?
If you were to die tonight, would you be absolutely certain that you are going to Paradise? This lesson says we do not assign anyone to Paradise or Hell. How does that humble your pride and remind you to rely on Allah's mercy rather than your own deeds?
?
Think of a secret sin you struggle with that no one knows. The passage says 'we leave their secrets to Allah.' Do you truly trust that Allah is the only judge of your inner state, or do you fear human judgment? How can this belief give you the courage to repent sincerely without despairing of Allah's mercy?

The Balanced Middle Path of Ahl al-Sunnah
Imam Tahawi describes the Sunni creed as a middle path between extremes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Sunni creed occupies a balanced position between extreme theological errors.

Core Idea
Ahl al-Sunnah is the middle path between every pair of extremes.

Imam al-Tahawi concludes his creed by affirming that Islam as understood by the Sunnis is not a compromise but a divinely guided balance. He lists four pairs of extremes that the Sunni position avoids, showing that truth lies in the center. This passage introduces the conceptual framework for recognising orthodoxy.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage identifying the pairs
Read the Arabic and translation carefully. Note the four 'between' (بَيْنَ) statements. Each contrasts two opposing errors.
The pairs are: elevation/deficiency, anthropomorphism/negation, compulsion/free will, security/despair.
2
Understand what each pair means
Reflect on each pair. For example, 'elevation and deficiency' refers to exaggerating Allah's attributes versus denying them entirely. The Sunni position is the middle that affirms without exaggeration.
This is not compromise but balanced truth.
3
Connect to the phrase 'this is our religion'
After listing the balances, the author says 'So this is our religion'. This affirms that the middle path defines Sunni identity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَرَضِيتُ لَكُمُ الإِسْلَامَ دِينًا ﴾ [سورة المائدة آية: ٣]، وَهُوَ بَيْنَ العُلُوِّ وَالتَّقْصِير وَالتَّشْبِيهِ وَالتَّعْطِيلِ وَالْجَبْرِيَّةِ وَالقَدَرِ وَالأَمْنِ وَاليَأْسِ. فَهَذَا دِينُنَا وَاعْتِقَادُنَا ظَاهِرًا وَبَاطِنًا، وَنَحْنُ نَبْرَأُ إِلَى اللَّهُ تَعَالَى مِمَّنْ خَالَفَ الَّذِي ذَكَرْنَاهُ وَبَيَّنَّاهُ، وَنَسْأَلُ اللهَ تَعَالَى أَنْ يُثَبِّتَنَا عَلَيْهِ وَيَخْتِمَ لَنَا بِهِ وَيَعْصِمَنَا مِنَ الْأَهْوَاءِ المُخْتَلِطَةِ وَالآرَاءِ الْمُتَفَرِّقَةِ وَالمَذَاهِبِ الرَّدِيَّةِ ؛ كَالمُشَبِّهَةِ وَالجَهْمِيَّةِ وَالْجَبْرِيَّةِ وَالقَدَرِيَّةِ وَغَيْرِهِمْ مِمَّنْ خَالَفَ السُّنَّةَ وَالجَمَاعَةَ وَاتَّبَعَ البِدْعَةَ وَالضَّلَالَةَ، وَنَحْنُ مِنْهُمْ بَرَاءٌ وَهُمْ عِنْدَنَا ضُلَّالٌ وَأَرْدِيَاءُ. وَاللَّهُ أَعْلَمُ بِالصَّوَابِ وَإِلَيْهِ المَرْجِعُ وَالمَابُ.
And I have chosen for you Islam as a religion. And it is between elevation and deficiency, between anthropomorphism and negation, between compulsion (Jabriyyah) and free will (Qadr), and between security and despair. So this is our religion and our belief, outwardly and inwardly, and we disassociate ourselves to Allah, the Exalted, from whoever opposes what we have mentioned and explained. And we ask Allah, the Exalted, to make us firm upon it and to seal for us with it and to protect us from confused desires, scattered opinions, and evil sects: like the Mushabbihah (anthropomorphists), the Jahmiyyah, the Jabriyyah (determinists), the Qadariyyah (free-willers), and others from those who oppose the Sunnah and the Jama'ah and follow innovation and misguidance. We are free from them, and they are in our view misguided and evil. And Allah knows best what is correct, and to Him is the return and the ultimate abode.
Source pages p. 224

Commentary
This passage is the conclusion of the Tahawiyyah creed. It begins by quoting a part of Quranic verse 5:3, 'And I have chosen for you Islam as a religion,' to affirm that Islam is the chosen religion from Allah. Then the author describes the correct understanding of Islam as being on a middle path between various extremes: between exaggeration and negligence (elevation and deficiency), between anthropomorphism (tashbih) and divestment (ta'til), between the extreme determinism of the Jabriyyah and the extreme free will of the Qadariyyah, and between unwarranted security from Allah's punishment and utter despair of His mercy. After stating this balanced position, the author declares that this is the religion and belief of the Sunni community, both outwardly and inwardly. He then makes a declaration of disavowal (bara'ah) to Allah from anyone who opposes what has been stated. The passage continues with a supplication that Allah make them firm (thabat) upon this creed, seal their lives with it, and protect them from confused desires (ahwa' mukhtalitah) and scattered opinions, as well as from evil sects such as the Mushabbihah (those who liken Allah to creation), the Jahmiyyah (followers of Jahm ibn Safwan), the Jabriyyah (extreme determinists), the Qadariyyah (extreme free-willers), and others who oppose the Sunnah and the united community (Jama'ah) and follow innovation (bid'ah) and misguidance. The author asserts that the Sunni community is innocent of them and considers them misguided and evil (ardiya'). Finally, the text concludes with a humble acknowledgement that Allah knows best what is correct and that to Him is the final return and abode. This ending reinforces the Sunni position of adhering to the middle path, dissociating from sectarian deviations, and relying on Allah for guidance and steadfastness.

Key Terms
التشبيه
التعطيل
الجبرية
القدرية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the Sunni 'middle path' is a compromise or blending of opposite views.
Correction: The Sunni position is not a compromise but the revealed truth that avoids both extremes; it is the origin from which deviations depart.

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT one of the pairs mentioned in the passage?
A) Elevation and deficiency
B) Anthropomorphism and negation
C) Compulsion and free will
D) Faith and disbelief

Key Takeaway
The Sunni creed is defined by its balanced middle position that avoids the extremes of exaggeration and denial.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you consider the pair 'false security vs despair', which of these two spiritual diseases have you felt more vulnerable to in your own life? What specific situation tempts you to either feel too safe from Allah's decree or too hopeless of His mercy, and how does the balanced path of Ahl al-Sunnah demand a change in your heart?
?
Think of a time you leaned toward one of the extremes mentioned—such as neglecting Allah's attributes by reducing Him to a mere concept, or exaggerating them by imagining Him in a human form. How did that affect your worship and your relationship with Allah? What concrete step will you take today to anchor yourself in the middle path of the Salaf?
?
The author declares that this middle path is 'our religion, outwardly and inwardly.' Is there a gap between what you claim to believe and how you actually live? Which pair of extremes exposes the deepest inconsistency in your life, and what will you sacrifice to bring your private conviction into alignment with the truth you profess?

Disavowal of Innovators and Supplication for Steadfastness
Imam Tahawi declares disavowal of deviant sects and prays for steadfastness.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the importance of disavowing deviant sects and the supplication for steadfastness in the Sunni creed.

Core Idea
Faith includes disassociation from error and reliance on Allah for guidance.

After affirming the balanced creed, Imam al-Tahawi makes a declaration of disavowal (bara'ah) to Allah from all who oppose the Sunni path. He then prays for steadfastness, sealing the creed with humility. This lesson examines the final part of the Tahawiyyah text.

Guided Path
1
Read the disavowal declaration
Notice the phrase 'نحن نبرأ إلى الله' - we disassociate ourselves to Allah. This is an act of religious distancing from falsehood.
Disavowal is not personal hatred but a theological stance.
2
List the sects mentioned
The passage names Mushabbihah, Jahmiyyah, Jabriyyah, Qadariyyah, and others. Identify what each represents.
These are examples of those who oppose the Sunnah.
3
Examine the supplication
The author asks for thabat (firmness), a good ending (khatimah), and protection from confused desires and evil sects.
This shows reliance on Allah for guidance.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَرَضِيتُ لَكُمُ الإِسْلَامَ دِينًا ﴾ [سورة المائدة آية: ٣]، وَهُوَ بَيْنَ العُلُوِّ وَالتَّقْصِير وَالتَّشْبِيهِ وَالتَّعْطِيلِ وَالْجَبْرِيَّةِ وَالقَدَرِ وَالأَمْنِ وَاليَأْسِ. فَهَذَا دِينُنَا وَاعْتِقَادُنَا ظَاهِرًا وَبَاطِنًا، وَنَحْنُ نَبْرَأُ إِلَى اللَّهُ تَعَالَى مِمَّنْ خَالَفَ الَّذِي ذَكَرْنَاهُ وَبَيَّنَّاهُ، وَنَسْأَلُ اللهَ تَعَالَى أَنْ يُثَبِّتَنَا عَلَيْهِ وَيَخْتِمَ لَنَا بِهِ وَيَعْصِمَنَا مِنَ الْأَهْوَاءِ المُخْتَلِطَةِ وَالآرَاءِ الْمُتَفَرِّقَةِ وَالمَذَاهِبِ الرَّدِيَّةِ ؛ كَالمُشَبِّهَةِ وَالجَهْمِيَّةِ وَالْجَبْرِيَّةِ وَالقَدَرِيَّةِ وَغَيْرِهِمْ مِمَّنْ خَالَفَ السُّنَّةَ وَالجَمَاعَةَ وَاتَّبَعَ البِدْعَةَ وَالضَّلَالَةَ، وَنَحْنُ مِنْهُمْ بَرَاءٌ وَهُمْ عِنْدَنَا ضُلَّالٌ وَأَرْدِيَاءُ. وَاللَّهُ أَعْلَمُ بِالصَّوَابِ وَإِلَيْهِ المَرْجِعُ وَالمَابُ.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you examine your own beliefs, do you find any traces of thinking like the sects mentioned—perhaps relying too much on your own free will (Qadari) or feeling fatalistic (Jabri)? What will you change today to align more with the balanced Sunni creed, and how will you use the prayer of Imam Tahawi to ask Allah for steadfastness?
?
Is your disavowal of religious errors directed purely for Allah's sake, or does it sometimes slip into personal grudges? How would your relationship with those who hold different views change if you genuinely made your displeasure for Allah alone, while still praying for their guidance?
?
If you were to die tonight, would the last words of your heart match the humble plea of Imam Tahawi—seeking steadfastness and a good ending? What is one specific step you can take right now to purify your creed and draw closer to the path of Ahl al-Sunnah?
